# 疯癫与文明 - Folie et Déraison

- 9TH-07 激情与谵妄 / Passion and Delirium

## 9TH-01 开篇 / Prologue

因此柏拉图年<So the platonic year>席卷出新的是非观<Whirls out new right and wrong,>而卷入旧的观念<Whirls in the old instead;>所有人都是舞者，他们的舞步<All men are dancers and their tread>迈入了野蛮铿锵的锣鼓声<Goes to the barbarous clangour of a gong.> 威廉·巴特勒·叶芝：《一九一九年》\
So the platonic yearWhirls out new right and wrong,Whirls in the old instead;All men are dancers and their treadGoes to the barbarous clangour of a gong. W.B. Yeats—Nineteen Hundred and Nineteen

三月已至下旬，随着时间推移，乌斯怀亚的白日时长正在逐渐减少。\
It's the final days of March, and the daylight hours in Ushuaia are shrinking away.

这是一座孤寂的城市。此刻，世界尽头的咖啡馆里，所有的谈话与笑闹声都如同被笼罩在一个密不透风的玻璃盏之中。\
Past the busy season, the city is faded and quiet. At this moment, in a café at the end of the world, conversation and laughter are sealed within an airtight glass dome.

**虚构集**：数年前，我在库埃纳瓦卡的露营地做守林员时，认识了一名来自墨西哥超现实主义派的诗人。\
**Recoleta**: "A few years ago, I worked as a forest ranger at a campsite in Cuernavaca. There, I met a Mexican surrealist poet."

**虚构集**：为了感谢我对他的帮助——唔，一些不足挂齿的小事，只不过是替他赶走了露营地里突然出现的野生动物罢了。\
**Recoleta**: "He was especially grateful that I was there. Some animals had wandered into the campground, and I drove them off for him. It wasn't a big deal, really."

**虚构集**：言归正传。他告诉了我一个相当离奇的故事：这个故事发生在1975年的墨西哥索诺拉州，一个名叫阿马尔菲塔诺[Amalfitano]的沙漠小镇。\
**Recoleta**: "As a token of gratitude, he elucidated this strange story to me—one that happened in a Sonoran Desert town called Amalfitano back in 1975."

**虚构集**：故事的内容和当地一个神奇的风俗有关，他们管它叫“巴比伦之骰”。\
**Recoleta**: "The people there adhered to a most unorthodox belief, which centered on the Die of Babylon."

**虚构集**：一位提着箱子的能量扰动学家为了探索、记录这神奇的民俗而踏上这片土地。你们懂的，这类人嘛，不外乎是为了什么学术研究……\
**Recoleta**: "One day, a researcher with a suitcase arrived in town. She came to study their local customs—an unsurprising reason for a learned intellectual to appear in a remote desert settlement."

**虚构集**：她却不知道，这座破败的小镇、这些周而复始的习俗成为了她命运中未知一面的开始——\
**Recoleta**: "But little did she know, this dusty old town and its peculiar custom would lead her down an entirely unexpected path—"

**同行青年Ⅰ**：虚构集，我觉得你需要给这个能量扰动学家取一个名字。\
**Young Woman**: Hold on. Sorry to interrupt, Recoleta. Does this researcher have a name?

**同行青年Ⅰ**：她可以叫诺拉、乔安娜或者特蕾莎……只需要一个名字，这个故事就会变得易于理解许多。\
**Young Woman**: She could be Nora, Joanna, or Teresa. Any name really. I feel like you want people focusing on the story, not keeping track of who's who.

迷惑和震惊的神情交织浮现在故事讲述者的脸上。\
Confusion and shock intertwine on the storyteller's face.

**虚构集**：谢谢你的建议，玛利亚。\
**Recoleta**: Errr, thank you for your advice.

**虚构集**：但她不是诺拉，也不是乔安娜和特蕾莎。她不是任何别的人。\
**Recoleta**: But she isn't a Nora, or a Joanna, or a Teresa. She's just herself.

**虚构集**：她就只是这个故事里的能量扰动学家。\
**Recoleta**: A Paracausality Researcher.

**同行青年Ⅱ**：哈哈哈哈！玛利亚，你有看到虚构集说“谢谢”的时候，那咬牙切齿的神情吗？\
**Young Man**: Hahahaha! You see that look? She's halfway to eating you alive!

**同行青年Ⅱ**：一个不容置疑的事实——如果虚构集愿意听你的建议，那她就不会是我们所认识的虚构集。\
**Young Man**: Face it, María. She wouldn't be the freak we know if she listened to anyone.

**虚构集**：好吧，我会重新思考故事的切入点。\
**Recoleta**: Ah, alright! So you didn't like the opening, fine. I'll come up with something new.

**虚构集**：从巴比伦之骰开始怎么样？它来自一位被西班牙囚禁的阿兹特克巫师——\
**Recoleta**: Maybe I'll start with a bit of exposition on the Die of Babylon? Beginning with its origins as a secret relic created by an Aztec priest imprisoned by the Conquistadors—

遗憾的是，这枚神秘的骰子并没有等来它的后续。故事第二次被打断了。\
The mysterious die's origins never get a continuation, as her story is interrupted a second time.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：唉……我很抱歉。只是看来这一次，我们也无法读懂你的小说了。\
**Young Woman**: I don't know if that's going to do much, sister. I'm beginning to think we'll never figure out what you're trying to say with this novel.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：但这并不是你的问题……\
**Young Woman**: And, well, and this isn't your fault.

**同行青年Ⅱ**：玛利亚，你为什么不直接告诉她呢？这确实不是你的问题，因为我们决定回布宜诺斯艾利斯了！\
**Young Man**: Ay, goodness! Just tell her, María. We're going back to Buenos Aires!

**虚构集**：回布宜诺斯艾利斯？可……这太突然了！\
**Recoleta**: Back to Buenos Aires? All of a sudden, just like that?

**虚构集**：潘乔，玛利亚，究竟发生了什么事？是我们路上闹了什么我不知晓的矛盾吗？\
**Recoleta**: Pancho, María, what's going on? Did I do something wrong during our travels?

毫无头绪的女孩观察着同行了两个月的诗人伙伴。\
The startled storyteller eyes her companions of the last two months, searching for reasons.

**虚构集**：我明白了，一定是你们对我一直念叨的小说感到不耐烦了。\
**Recoleta**: Ah, yes, I know what it is. I've bored you with my constant rambling over this novel.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：不，不，不是这样的。你误会了……\
**Young Woman**: No, Recoleta. It's got nothing to do with your novel.

**同行青年Ⅱ**：你还不明白吗？我们没有钱了！\
**Young Man**: Don't you get it? We're flat broke!

**同行青年Ⅱ**：不然我们在这儿干什么？我们为什么要在这里擦这些永远擦不干净的杯子、桌子和地板？\
**Young Man**: Why do you think we're stuck here scrubbing tables?

同行青年愤怒地扔下手中的抹布，拔高的音量让整座咖啡馆为之寂静一秒。\
The man slams his damp washcloth on the table to emphasize his point. His voice breaks the illusion of silence in the café.

**虚构集**：噢，那当然是因为我们还没还清这几天的马黛茶钱……\
**Recoleta**: Because we can't pay for all the mate we've been drinking.

**同行青年Ⅱ**：听着，虚构集。成为一个诗人，环游拉丁美洲，在官方大诗人的集会上闹事，这一切确实如你所说的那样酷。\
**Young Man**: That wasn't a question, Recoleta. We've crossed the continent, crashed the readings of all those "prestigious poets," and lived the way a real artist should. And, I admit it, it's been just as amazing as you promised.

**同行青年Ⅱ**：但它只是没法一直持续下去。\
**Young Man**: But we can't go on living like this.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：我们都很喜欢你，也很喜欢你的小说。\
**Young Woman**: You know that we both care about you. And we believe in your novel, too.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：我不想否认这段旅程给我带来的一切。哈，像切·格瓦拉一样骑摩托车环游拉丁美洲？自成年之后我就没有过这样的幻想了。\
**Young Woman**: I'd be lying if I said this journey meant nothing to me. Getting to ride around the continent on a motorcycle like Che Guevara himself? I never could have imagined I'd get the chance to go on an adventure like this. We got to live the dream!

**同行青年Ⅱ**：是挺好的，除了像切·格瓦拉一样摩托车坏掉的那几天。\
**Young Man**: A real dream, except for those days when the motorcycle broke down. Though that was a real tribute to Che's journey too.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：闭嘴，潘乔。\
**Young Woman**: Don't tease, Pancho.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：虚构集，你知道吗？自从你邀请我和潘乔加入本能现实主义派之后，有那么一些时刻，我们确实感觉自己成为了一名真正的诗人。\
**Young Woman**: Recoleta, since you invited us to join the visceral realists, we've both found amazing new ways to channel our inner poetry.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：哪怕我到现在都不能理解什么是本能现实主义，也从来没有看懂过你的小说。\
**Young Woman**: Even though I still don't understand what in the world you're trying to say with your novel, or for that matter, what visceral realism actually is.

**虚构集**：玛利亚，潘乔……\
**Recoleta**: María, Pancho ...

**同行青年Ⅰ**：但就像你说的那样，重要的不是这些，而是过着诗人一样的生活。我确信我们做到了。只是……\
**Young Woman**: You told us not to worry about the definitions, to feel and to live in our words. We did just as you said, and it felt great! But ...

她看向窗外的乌斯怀亚，感觉到一丝寒意。\
She looks out at Ushuaia, feeling a chill.

昏暗的天空下着小雪，季节正在蜕变。很快，灰白色将会掩盖这片土地上所有闪闪发亮、色彩斑斓的低矮房屋。\
Snow falls from the dimming sky. The season is shifting. Soon, gray and white will blanket the colorful houses of this desolate land.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：……冬天马上要来了，而你看起来像是被困在那个永恒的沙漠小镇里了。\
**Young Woman**: Now the winter chill is setting in, and the only thing you seem to care about is that little fictional town.

**虚构集**：……\
**Recoleta**: ...

审判席上，一直在接受指控的女孩陷入了短暂的沉默。\
The storyteller sinks back against their accusations, searching for words.

**虚构集**：谢谢你们的肺腑之言，潘乔，玛利亚。但我必须说，情况比我想象中的要好。\
**Recoleta**: I appreciate your honesty, friends. I was worried the problem was much worse than all that!

**虚构集**：听我说，我有一个绝妙的点子。我知道一个可以让所有神秘学家都安安稳稳度过冬天的地方。\
**Recoleta**: Winter here isn't as dreadful as you think, and I know just the place to keep us warm!

**虚构集**：1520年，神秘学家麦哲伦背负着西班牙政府赋予的伟大使命，率领舰队在一片陌生的海域中航行。\
**Recoleta**: It was 1520. Arcanist Ferdinand Magellan sailed across unfamiliar waters under orders from the Spanish crown.

**虚构集**：遥远处，岛上的堆堆篝火吸引了他的视线——他将这个新发现的神秘岛屿命名为火地岛【Tierra del Fuego】。\
**Recoleta**: Over the vast gray sea, he saw spots of light in the distance—an island. He named it Tierra del Fuego.

**虚构集**：此后四百年间，关于乌斯怀亚的历史叙事就此展开：在这座世界尽头、遥远南端的城镇，它最大的建筑竟然是一所监狱！\
**Recoleta**: For the next 400 years, Ushuaia faithfully served its role at the end of the world: it became the continent's penal colony, and its largest building even served as a prison!

**虚构集**：因其偏远的地理位置，乌斯怀亚逐渐成为了流放神秘学家死刑犯的绝佳场所。而科马拉疗养院，就建立于二十世纪初期，神秘学家获罪的高峰时刻。\
**Recoleta**: Many arcanists were exiled there. By the turn of the century, the arcanist hunt had reached its peak, and the Comala Sanatorium was built.

**虚构集**：噢，请见谅——在当时，部分，或者说大部分的神秘学家，都被定义为一种疯癫的存在。\
**Recoleta**: Well, as you may already know, at that time, most arcanists were believed to be victims of madness.

**虚构集**：毕竟没有人在意“疯癫”的本质是什么，不是么？但人们总会意识到，神秘学血统并不是一种疾病，于是在1947年，疗养院就被废弃了。\
**Recoleta**: The sanatorium was their "Ship of Fools." However, as people began to realize that arcanist blood wasn't a guarantee of madness, fewer and fewer were imprisoned there. By 1947, it was officially closed.

**虚构集**：二十世纪七十年代，被弃置的科马拉疗养院迎来了一次真正的改头换面：一群国家福柯学会的人引进了来自欧洲的先进概念。\
**Recoleta**: Until the 1970s, when a group of people from the National Foucault Studies Association returned to the island with new ideas for the location.

**虚构集**：没人知晓那些复杂的理论代表着什么含义，总之，他们将疗养院更名，并在旧址上哐哐当当地改造了数个月。\
**Recoleta**: They spoke in abstract terms and opaque theories that no one could understand. They rebuilt this place and gave it a new name.

**虚构集**：漫长的改造结束了，科马拉疗养院成为了一座真正关押神秘学家罪犯的监狱——\
**Recoleta**: After a long period of construction, the Comala Sanatorium became a prison once more, one designed to hold arcanist criminals.

**虚构集**：他们在这儿囚禁那些被诊断为精神分裂的嫌犯，那些在各种秘密集会、反对组织中被抓捕的神秘学家。\
**Recoleta**: They were taken from the streets and the psychiatric clinics, from secret societies, and rebel groups. Any arcanists deemed mentally or socially unfit would be locked away there.

**虚构集**：协会宣称会给他们最好的治疗，直到他们能痊愈，能回到日常生活里去。\
**Recoleta**: This association claimed the inmates would receive the best treatment, and they would fully "recover" before being returned to society.

**虚构集**：一所实验性质的监狱，一所监禁性质的疗养院，这就是科马拉全新的面目。\
**Recoleta**: A prison, a medical lab, a sanatorium—call it whatever you want. That is what Comala is today.

**虚构集**：我们可以在科马拉度过一整个冬天，保准不会遇到任何经济上的困难。尽管可能要付出一点点的代价……并且需要一点点的演技。\
**Recoleta**: And we could spend the whole winter there. It'd probably be the easiest winter we've ever had. All that it requires is a little bit of acting.

**虚构集**：相信我，伙计们，饰演一个精神分裂的嫌犯没什么难的——这是所有神秘学家天生就掌握的技能。\
**Recoleta**: It won't be hard to pass ourselves off as a bunch of unstable crackpots. A touch of madness comes parceled with the gifts of being an arcanist!

**同行青年Ⅱ**：你的“绝妙点子”就是让我们都去坐牢吗？!\
**Young Man**: That's your "brilliant idea"? To get us locked up in an asylum?

**同行青年Ⅱ**：再多的花言巧语也掩盖不了它是一所监狱的事实！\
**Young Man**: You understand we'd be prisoners there, don't you? It's not like we'd get to put our feet up and relax by a fire!

气急的同伴转过头看向一旁。结满霜的玻璃窗隐隐透出街道外的景色：一名巡逻的宪兵迈着轻快的步子，走过众人所在的咖啡馆。\
Her increasingly agitated companion turns his head aside, catching the faint outline of a patrolling gendarme through the frosted window.

**同行青年Ⅱ**：你看，现在外面正路过一个进入监狱的绝妙法子：冲出去，揍那个戴帽子的男人两拳，保准你马上如愿以偿。\
**Young Man**: You wanna go to jail? Well, see that man over there? Go greet him with a punch to the jaw, then you'll be set for the whole winter.

**虚构集**：这听起来是一个好主意。\
**Recoleta**: Hmm. It sounds like a good idea.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：冷静点，虚构集，宪兵不是我们能招惹的。\
**Young Woman**: Recoleta, please! We're not messing with the gendarme.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：我和胡丽娅姨妈已经说好了。她在布宜诺斯艾利斯周边有一座葡萄庄园，现在正是需要短工的时候，我们可以回去给她帮忙，再多的人也不嫌多。\
**Young Woman**: We're going to my Aunt Julia's. She said she can take us in at her vineyard up north near the capital. But it's harvest season. They could use all the help they can get.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：等明年……或者冬天过去了，我们再来乌斯怀亚一趟！那也一定会是一趟好旅程。\
**Young Woman**: We'll return to Ushuaia next year, or when the winter has passed. It'll still be great!

闻言，一直滔滔不绝的女孩平静下来，脸色疏离得好像桌上冷掉的马黛茶一样。\
Recoleta's expression is as cold as the mate tea on the table.

**虚构集**：谢谢你们，玛利亚，潘乔。\
**Recoleta**: I hear you, friends.

**虚构集**：但我拒绝。\
**Recoleta**: But respectfully, I must turn down your offer.

**虚构集**：对我而言，现在的一切不仅仅是一趟旅程而已。\
**Recoleta**: This has been more than just a road trip for me.

**虚构集**：冬天确实要到来了。但万一冬天过去，一切都变化而不复存在呢？也许这是我最后的机会了。\
**Recoleta**: I know sticking around here for the winter won't be easy. But this could be my last chance. What if things change again? I can't just wait for spring.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：虚构集……\
**Young Woman**: Recoleta ...

**同行青年Ⅱ**：我早和你说过了，玛利亚，你是永远不可能说服她的。一切都是白费功夫！\
**Young Man**: What did I tell you, María? She never listens. Wasting your breath!

**同行青年Ⅱ**：那就永别了，亲爱的虚构集——\
**Young Man**: Goodbye, Recoleta. I don't think we'll meet again—

忽然之间，潘乔脸上的表情凝固了。\
Pancho's apologetic words freeze in his mouth.

**同行青年Ⅱ**：该死，外面的宪兵好像真是冲着咱们来的！\
**Young Man**: S**t! Those gendarmes are looking straight at us!

**虚构集**：什么？\
**Recoleta**: What?!

咖啡馆的门被推开了。\
The café door swings open.

一阵寒意与潮气瞬间席卷了室内，虚构集寒毛直竖，视线不由自主地往门口聚焦。\
A gust of cold air and dampness sweeps through the room. Recoleta's hair stands on end with the chill as she turns to face the door.

**宪兵**：别跑，你们几个！在先行者路的诗会上闹事的那批人！\
**Gendarme**: Stop right there! You three match the descriptions of some intruders at the Poetry Meeting in Pioneer Street!

话音刚落，身边的两个同行青年早已脚底抹油，不见人影。\
Recoleta plans a response, only to hear the scrambling sounds of her companions bolting away out the back door.

**虚构集**：这下糟糕了。\
**Recoleta**: Just when I thought things couldn't get any worse.

宪兵已经不见踪影，但狼狈的青年作家仍然不敢停下逃跑的脚步。\
The gendarmes are left behind in the cold, but the flustered young writer still dares not stop running.

终于，她摔倒在了湿漉漉的街道上。\
Until she stumbles on a patch of wet and mushy snow.

**虚构集**：啊……！上帝保佑，他没有追上来……\
**Recoleta**: Oh! Thank God. I think I lost them.

**维尔汀**：您还好吗？\
**Vertin**: Are you alright?

**虚构集**：谢谢你，善良又热心的女士。\
**Recoleta**: Ah, thank you.

**虚构集**：但我没事。不过是在路上狠狠摔了一跤，比被宪兵勒索一顿要好得多了——\
**Recoleta**: Better to kiss the ground than kiss the gendarme's boots, if one must choose.

**虚构集**：噢，德洛丝女士！\
**Recoleta**: Wait a second. Dores? Is that you?

**虚构集**：您最近过得怎么样？果然，命运就是一个首尾衔接的环，我们又遇见了！这次，您能带我进去科马拉监狱吗？\
**Recoleta**: Funny how life moves in circles and puts an old friend in my path! How have you been? Are you paying another visit to Comala?

**维尔汀**：……德洛丝？\
**Vertin**: Dores?

一个从天而降的名字——由一位脸着地、看不清面前来人的小姑娘所提供。\
A name falls from the sky—offered by a girl who has just face-planted and cannot see the figure before her.

**十四行诗**：司辰，她提到了德洛丝女士！\
**Sonetto**: Timekeeper, could she mean our Dr. Dores?

**虚构集**：唔……我认错人了？\
**Recoleta**: Emm. Was I mistaken?

线索提供者擦干净脸上的雪水，头晕目眩的她终于看清面前的陌生人。\
She wipes the snow from her face. Still dizzy, she makes out the stranger before her.

种种迹象表明，命运并不是个首尾相衔的环——至少面前提着箱子的人不是自己数天前遇到的那位女士。\
As her vision clears, it becomes apparent that fate is not a perfect loop. At least, the person holding the suitcase in front of her is not the same woman she met before.

**虚构集**：真是神奇，这世界上竟然存在如此相似的面容。\
**Recoleta**: How strange. I've never seen two people so alike.

**虚构集**：啊！请原谅我——\
**Recoleta**: But please, forgive me. It's been a long day.

**维尔汀**：没关系。您能告诉我，您是在哪里见到德洛丝女士的吗？\
**Vertin**: No need to apologize. In fact, the person you just mentioned sounds like someone we're looking for.

**维尔汀**：……就是您所说的，与我长得有些相似的那位。\
**Vertin**: Could you tell me where you last saw her?

**虚构集**：当然可以，但——阿嚏——\
**Recoleta**: Sure, I—*sneeze*—excuse me.

**虚构集**：看你们的衣着打扮与口音，你们并不是本地人对吧。\
**Recoleta**: You're not from around here, are you? Your accents and those clothes give you away.

**虚构集**：请随我来。我知晓一个比下着雪的街道更好的谈话地方。\
**Recoleta**: Come with me. I know a warmer place to talk.

## 9TH-02 实质与环 / More than Circles

**十四行诗**：据《乌斯怀亚新闻报》报道，大约一周前，乌斯怀亚的码头被神秘术破坏，现在，所有的船只都毁于一旦。\
**Sonetto**: According to these news reports from Ushuaia, there was an arcane attack on the pier about a week ago. All the ships in the port were destroyed.

**十四行诗**：司辰，这会和重塑之手，亦或叛变的芝诺部队有关系吗？\
**Sonetto**: Could Manus Vindictae be responsible for this, or perhaps the Zeno rebels?

**维尔汀**：不能确定。但我们到达乌斯怀亚已有数日，这里平静得超乎寻常。\
**Vertin**: Hard to say. But things have been suspiciously quiet these past few days.

**维尔汀**：在自由海风号的事故之后，我们就丢失了重塑的踪迹。\
**Vertin**: I had been hoping we'd find some clues here in Ushuaia after we lost track of the Manus in the "Free Breeze" shipwreck.

**维尔汀**：重塑之手似乎隐匿在某个不为人知的角落，一个普通人不会轻易踏足的地方。亦或说，他们离开了乌斯怀亚。\
**Vertin**: They would've gone to ground, somewhere remote and off the radar. Indeed, it's possible they've already left Ushuaia.

**维尔汀**：他们再也不像往常一样，在各地积极促进“暴雨”的进程……\
**Vertin**: For whatever reason, it seems they haven't been pushing for the "Storm" to happen quite as eagerly as before.

**维尔汀**：这并不是一个好消息。他们有可能在谋划一些更为可怕的东西。\
**Vertin**: I have a strange feeling about it all. They're definitely up to something.

**维尔汀**：如果目击信息属实，我们就能印证基金会从飞蛾处得到的重要线索：德洛丝女士确实被叛变的伊戈尔一行人带到了乌斯怀亚。\
**Vertin**: For now, it seems our new friend's story lines up with the intel from Moth. It seems the Zeno rebels really did bring Dr. Dores here. We should see if there's anything more she can tell us.

**十四行诗**：但是，司辰……\
**Sonetto**: Timekeeper ...

第一助手欲言又止。\
The chief assistant hesitates.

**十四行诗**：自我们来到火地岛以来，基金会并没有足够的时间对这儿展开详尽调查。如果这里和重塑有关系……\
**Sonetto**: The Foundation doesn't have any intelligence on Tierra del Fuego. If the Manus really are here ...

**十四行诗**：离乌斯怀亚最近的基金会分部，在布宜诺斯艾利斯，有3200公里……\
**Sonetto**: Then, we'll be on our own. The closest Foundation Branch is in Buenos Aires, 3200 km away.

最新消息是，那儿目前正忙着处理伊戈尔养子叛变所留下的混乱。\
She reflects without words, a reminder that the chaos caused by Igor's rebellion is still fresh.

**维尔汀**：是的，重塑之手完全有能力在这段时间在这里进行渗透——就像他们对待那个名为奇索斯的镇子一样。\
**Vertin**: Careful and well-considered as ever, Sonetto. It's possible they've already infiltrated Ushuaia, just as they did in Chisos.

**维尔汀**：但寻找德洛丝女士的任务同样紧迫。抱歉，我想我们没有时间再等下去了。\
**Vertin**: But the Zeno rebels may still be holding Dores. We can't just wait around. I'm afraid we'll have to take the risk.

**维尔汀**：乌斯怀亚并不是一个特别大的城市。只要重塑之手在这里活动过，我们肯定会发现线索的。\
**Vertin**: Ushuaia's not very big. If Manus Vindictae is here, we'll notice. Stay sharp.

**十四行诗**：我明白了。\
**Sonetto**: Understood, Timekeeper.

**十四行诗**：我们一定会完成任务的，司辰。\
**Sonetto**: I'll keep an eye out for them and for Dr. Dores.

经过一出“亡命天涯”的闹剧之后，咖啡馆已恢复了往日的宁静。\
After a chaotic "hunt and escape," the café regains its usual peace.

好消息是，追缉虚构集的宪兵已经消失；坏消息是，连带着她的同伴也不见踪影。\
The gendarmes are gone, and so too are Recoleta's companions.

**虚构集**：噢……他们真的走了。好吧。\
**Recoleta**: My friends ... They're really gone.

**虚构集**：“那就永别了，亲爱的虚构集——”那根本算不上一个真正的道别！\
**Recoleta**: "Goodbye, Recoleta. I don't think we'll meet again—" So that's all I get?

**虚构集**：我们本可以互换最后一首诗歌，在咖啡馆里轮流念一遍，然后将它永远铭记在泪水里。\
**Recoleta**: We could've exchanged some farewell poems, read them out loud like we used to, and shed a few bitter tears over our heartfelt goodbyes.

**虚构集**：但伟大的神秘学家诗人说得对——我们不应该庆祝离别这种不幸，这是不明智的……\
**Recoleta**: But you know what they say: "Goodbyes are only a senseless feast of unhappiness."

**维尔汀**：唔？\
**Vertin**: Pardon?

**虚构集**：没什么，两位请坐。请给我们一壶加了薄荷的马黛茶！\
**Recoleta**: Oh, it's nothing. Never mind. Please, sit down. And could we get a pot of mate with mint, please?

**十四行诗**：谢谢。\
**Sonetto**: Thank you.

虚构集颇有兴趣地打量着基金会的女孩们，她们正小心翼翼地接过滚烫的茶水。\
Recoleta watches with interest as the two girls take the offered cups of tea.

**虚构集**：你们正在寻找德洛丝女士吗？\
**Recoleta**: So, you're looking for Dores?

**虚构集**：从你们的表情中，我能看出她对你们来说非常重要。\
**Recoleta**: I can tell she's important to you from your look.

**维尔汀**：是的。请您详细描述一下，您与德洛丝女士遇见的经过吧。\
**Vertin**: Correct. Is there anything more you could tell us about the day you met her?

**虚构集**：当然可以。德洛丝女士与我相遇于一个太阳被阴云遮蔽的下午……\
**Recoleta**: Of course. It was one of those gray, overcast afternoons ...

**虚构集**：在玻利瓦尔公寓外的街道，赶着去邮局寄信的我遇上了一位盲眼女士。\
**Recoleta**: I had just turned onto Calle Bolivar when I ran into this blind woman on my way to the post office.

**虚构集**：在当时，那位女士突然把我叫住，那是一个奇妙的时刻——她走了上来，将我衣服上的毛衣断线系上，仿佛这是一个神圣而包罗万象的举动。\
**Recoleta**: To be exact, I didn't run into her. She called to me. It felt like a sacred moment in time, like something unworldly. I just stood there, frozen, as she walked up and fixed a loose thread on my sweater.

**虚构集**：我几乎没能握住手中的信封。\
**Recoleta**: I stared at her until my fingers went numb and the letter almost slipped out of my hand.

**德洛丝**：这位小姐，你知道那儿是什么地方吗？\
**Dores**: Miss, could you tell me what's in that direction?

**虚构集**：我看到了那位女士，她的手指精准地指向了一个方向。也就是说，她很清楚自己的目的地位于何处——这对一位盲人来说是多么的神奇！\
**Recoleta**: I followed her hand as she pointed forward. Strangely, even though I could see she was blind, I had a feeling that she knew exactly where she was pointing and where she intended to go.

**虚构集**：女士，那里是科马拉监狱。\
**Recoleta**: That's the way to Comala Prison, madam.

**虚构集**：难道那是您的目的地吗？如果您想要去那里，也许我可以为您引路。\
**Recoleta**: Is that where you're headed? I could walk you there, if you'd like.

**德洛丝**：谢谢你，小姑娘……但我想，我已经找到了我该走的路。\
**Dores**: Thank you, Miss. But I think I've found my way.

**虚构集**：神灵同时给予她书籍与黑夜，那可真是一个绝妙的讽刺。\
**Recoleta**: She held a typewriter. How ironic that God would give her at once both books and night.

**虚构集**：女士，我可以得知您的名字吗？\
**Recoleta**: I'm Recoleta. What may I call you, Ms. ...?

**德洛丝**：……？\
**Dores**: ...?

**虚构集**：请放心，我不是什么奇怪的人……我猜您是一位作家，是吗？\
**Recoleta**: I hope you don't mind me asking, madam. I didn't mean to pry.

**虚构集**：恰好我也在进行小说的写作……我总有一种预感，您很快就会出现在我的小说中！\
**Recoleta**: It's only that I have to know. You're a writer too, aren't you? I've been working on a novel, and for some reason, I have this feeling you could be a character in it!

**虚构集**：您也知道，灵感总是不请自来的，就像一些讨人厌的访客。我很难判断该用什么样的东西招待它们——所以，最好的办法就是全部记录下来。\
**Recoleta**: Forgive me. I'm just so excited! I really want to remember this moment. Please, may I have your name? Or whatever you'd like me to call you?

**德洛丝**：哈哈……\
**Dores**: Heh heh.

**虚构集**：时至今日，我还记得她的笑容——一个出奇的笑，一个遥远的笑，一个跨越了时间、实质与世纪总和的笑。\
**Recoleta**: I don't think I'll ever forget her smile. It was soft, kind, almost merciful, and oddly, it felt so ancient.

**德洛丝**：也许比较突然，但……小姐，我有一个问题想要问你。\
**Dores**: No offense taken, Ms. Recoleta. But first, I have a question for you.

**德洛丝**：对你来说，“文学”代表着什么？\
**Dores**: What does literature mean to you?

**虚构集**：嗯？\
**Recoleta**: Sorry?

**虚构集**：这可把我难住了——一个超乎创作范畴的问题！\
**Recoleta**: What a question it was! I wasn't expecting anything like it!

**德洛丝**：你是一位具有文学追求的作家——但你是否想过，这种追求到底是从何而来？\
**Dores**: You're a writer, are you not? And one, I sense, with purpose. Tell me—where does such powerful motivation come from?

**虚构集**：……实际上，我不知道怎么回答您的问题，女士。\
**Recoleta**: Actually, well, I'm not sure, madam.

**虚构集**：就我个人的感受来说，也许文学只是文学，它不能替任何人回答问题……何况是一个关于它自身的问题。\
**Recoleta**: I have my pursuits and questions, but literature is neither the goal nor the answer to them. Literature is ... Well, it's just literature.

**虚构集**：我想，也许文学能做到的只是从某种截然不同的角度抛出问题，而这也正是我贸然猜测您职业的缘由。\
**Recoleta**: I suppose if I had to define it, I'd say it's a tool, a kindling for fire, or a lens to see through, a means to explore and raise questions from different angles and express our perspectives.

**德洛丝**：一个很有趣的说法，我明白了。\
**Dores**: And what an interesting perspective you've expressed. I see.

**德洛丝**：那么，它给你带来了一种怎样的感受呢？\
**Dores**: But how does literature make you feel?

**虚构集**：……感受吗？有时我觉得自己像个学习口语的孩子，正努力地念出书本第一页的第一个词汇。\
**Recoleta**: As though I'm a kid looking through a kaleidoscope for the first time.

**虚构集**：等等，这个比喻也许并不恰当，需要更为精妙、更为直观的……\
**Recoleta**: Well, maybe that's not the best way to put it. Perhaps something a little more subtle.

**虚构集**：就在纠结比喻措辞的时候，余光里的她轻飘飘地挥了挥手，随后穿过乌斯怀亚的细雪，朝监狱的方向走去了。\
**Recoleta**: Just when I was looking for the right word, she turned away with a little wave, heading toward the prison, her feet crunching over the fine snow.

**虚构集**：所以，德洛丝女士一定是往科马拉监狱去了！\
**Recoleta**: So, she must've gone to the prison!

**维尔汀**：您是什么时候遇到她的？\
**Vertin**: When did all of this happen?

**虚构集**：应该是三天前。那天短暂地出了一会儿太阳，街道上全是融化的雪水。\
**Recoleta**: About three days ago. I remember the sun came out for a while that day, and the streets were glistening with melting snow.

**虚构集**：如果有需要，我可以再为你们介绍一番科马拉监狱——\
**Recoleta**: You've heard of Comala Prison, haven't you?

她的暗示之意已经逐渐变成昭然若揭的明示了。\
Word by word, the question turns from an implication into a declaration.

**十四行诗**：三天前……司辰，这意味着我们还有机会追上她。\
**Sonetto**: Three days ago? Then we may be able to catch up with her there, Timekeeper.

**维尔汀**：是的。我们应该立刻进入科马拉监狱。\
**Vertin**: You're right. We need to get there as soon as we can.

**虚构集**：对，就是这样……不对，她竟然就这样斩钉截铁地说了出来……！\
**Recoleta**: Whoa. Amazing! So decisive, assertive—a true show of character!

**虚构集**：真是一位有魄力的人物！\
**Recoleta**: You must be the very archetype of a charismatic leader!

**虚构集**：我能说什么呢？当一个不可思议的巧合来得过于轻易的时候，我们总是会质疑作者的机械降神，觉得这是一个很烂的桥段。\
**Recoleta**: What's left to say? Whenever the protagonist has what they want fall into their laps, we're all quick to complain about lazy writers using "deus ex machina" to keep the story together. So let's not dwell on it.

她很快和自己还有作者和解了。\
She reconciles this observation with a silent nod to an unseen author.

**虚构集**：但不要紧，在一个白日只有四个小时的季节，一座以关押神秘学家作为历史叙事的小镇，发生什么事情都不稀奇。\
**Recoleta**: But anything can happen in a place like Ushuaia. It's a city where the day may only last four hours and the streets are full of exiled arcanists.

**维尔汀**：感谢您的协助，这位——\
**Vertin**: We appreciate your help, Ms. ...

**虚构集**：无需客气，叫我虚构集就好。\
**Recoleta**: Recoleta. Please, think nothing of it.

**维尔汀**：我是维尔汀。这位是十四行诗，我们来自圣洛夫基金会。\
**Vertin**: Ms. Recoleta, I'm Vertin, and this is Sonetto. We're investigators from the St. Pavlov Foundation.

**十四行诗**：您好，虚构集小姐。\
**Sonetto**: Pleasure to meet you.

**虚构集**：我很高兴我能帮上忙，维尔汀，十四行诗。\
**Recoleta**: Likewise, likewise! Glad that I could help. But listen, ladies.

女孩狡黠地眨了眨眼睛。\
The girl winks playfully.

**虚构集**：还有什么比这更巧的事情呢？你们要去科马拉监狱，我也要去科马拉监狱。\
**Recoleta**: Everything happens for a reason, and now it's becoming clear. You're going to Comala Prison, and so am I.

**虚构集**：最终我们都会在科马拉监狱里相遇，也许这就是神秘学家的宿命……\
**Recoleta**: Maybe it's fate that brought us together.

**维尔汀**：虚构集小姐，您为什么要去科马拉监狱呢？\
**Vertin**: What's your business there, if you don't mind our asking?

**虚构集**：哈哈，那必然是出于一些文学方面的原因——总之，从现在起，我们是朋友了！\
**Recoleta**: Oh, it's a ... writer's mission. But anyway, we're friends now.

**虚构集**：让我们出发吧！我想，你们至少需要一个熟悉当地情况的人来带路。\
**Recoleta**: If you're going to Comala, you'll need someone who knows the way.

## 9TH-03 岁月遗忘之地 / The Place That Time Forgot

灰色的河床在冰冷的大地上蜿蜒，直至消失在视线的深处。\
The gray riverbed winds through the frostbitten earth, disappearing into the distant horizon.

这栋整洁而破旧的圆形建筑，像是被人类、上帝、鬼魂同时遗弃的存在，孤零零地伫立于雪山之下。\
A neat yet dilapidated circular complex stands alone beneath the snow-capped mountains, as if abandoned by God, humanity, and ghosts alike.

围栏外，不请自来的三人正商讨着进入的方式。\
Outside the fence, three uninvited guests discuss their plan to get inside.

**虚构集**：瞧，这就是科马拉监狱！它是镇上最大的建筑，天晴时，我们总能一眼看到它。它就像一个锈掉的金属纽扣，歪歪扭扭地钉在地面上。\
**Recoleta**: Behold! Comala Prison! It's the biggest building around. When the sun comes out, it looks like a rusty button stitched into the earth.

**虚构集**：没人在意它，但谁也不能少了它。小心点，上山的路不太好走……噢……！\
**Recoleta**: Everyone tries not to pay attention to it, but it's undoubtedly one of the most important places in town. This way, careful, we're heading uphill—Oops!

快要滑倒的青年作家被眼明手快的第一助手拉住，避免了第二次摔倒的悲惨命运。\
The young writer begins to slip again. She is prevented only by Sonetto's quick reflexes.

**虚构集**：呼……谢谢！所以，你是来自圣——\
**Recoleta**: Phew! Thanks. So, my new friends! You're from that St. Palomino's ...

**十四行诗**：圣洛夫基金会。\
**Sonetto**: St. Pavlov Foundation.

**十四行诗**：维尔汀则是圣洛夫基金会的司辰。\
**Sonetto**: And Vertin is the Timekeeper there.

**虚构集**：好极了，一个伟大的官方称呼。你们一定有办法，堂堂正正从门口进去是吗？\
**Recoleta**: Ah, very impressive! Sounds all official and polished! Then, I take it you've already got a way into the prison?

大门紧闭着，它不欢迎任何的访客。\
The gate presents an unwelcoming face to the world.

**十四行诗**：我可以立刻撰写一封信件，联络基金会总部。总部通过审核后，将会通知布宜诺斯艾利斯分部，随后通知阿根廷本地政府。\
**Sonetto**: I'll draft a letter to headquarters right away. Once they approve it, they'll notify the local branch in Buenos Aires. From there, they'll need to inform the Argentine government,

**十四行诗**：届时，基金会可以为我们颁发一张特殊的准入许可……\
**Sonetto**: who will then issue us a permit.

**虚构集**：听起来，官方机构偶尔还是能发挥些作用的。噢，请见谅，没有针对两位的意思。\
**Recoleta**: Excellent! Looks like our bureaucrats still have some worth. No offense intended, of course.

**十四行诗**：如果情况紧迫，相信基金会会加快他们的审批速度——顺利的话，预计在一个月之后，我们就可以拿到那张准入许可。\
**Sonetto**: Since we're pressed for time, I believe we can ask that headquarters give high priority to our request. If all goes well, we should have the permit in about a month.

**虚构集**：……我改变主意了，我们还是不要麻烦官方比较好。\
**Recoleta**: Ah. How, how expedient of them! But you know what? Maybe we shouldn't bother all those hard-working government officials with these trifling matters after all.

她一秒重拾了自己的成见。\
She instantly returns to her previous judgment.

**虚构集**：比起原地等待那封不知何时到来的倒霉许可，眼下，我有一个更快捷便利的做法。\
**Recoleta**: I have a simpler solution that suits the urgency of our cause!

**十四行诗**：等等……虚构集小姐，你要做什么？\
**Sonetto**: That sounds great. Oh! Umm, where are you going, Ms. Recoleta?

来不及阻止，女孩已经熟练地、手脚并用地爬上墙头。\
Before anyone can stop her, the young writer hurls herself up the wall, scaling the side with the sort of skill that immediately suggests she's done this before.

**虚构集**：从瓜达拉哈拉到乌斯怀亚的这一路，没有任何一堵墙能拦住一个想要逃跑的诗人。所有的一切，都只是为了这刻而进行的演练……\
**Recoleta**: To the other side of the wall, of course! From Guadalajara to Ushuaia, there has yet to be a wall that could stop me!

**虚构集**：来吧，两位来自基金会的淑女！十四行诗，请把手递给我！\
**Recoleta**: Come on, ladies of the Foundation! Sonetto, take my hand!

被点名的第一助手显得十分慌张。\
Sonetto looks utterly flustered.

**十四行诗**：你的行为十分危险，虚构集小姐，请从围栏上下来……！\
**Sonetto**: Ms. Recoleta, please! A reckless act like that could have serious consequences! Please come back down!

**十四行诗**：感谢你的引路，根据《暴雨改革：增员与秩序》条约，接下来的任务会有一定危险性。我们无法告知你详情，但你可以返回小镇，在安全的地方等待。\
**Sonetto**: In fact, while the details of our mission are classified, I should warn you, it may be dangerous, and we cannot guarantee your safety once we're inside. Perhaps it's in your best interest to return to town.

**虚构集**：这根本没有道理！\
**Recoleta**: What? That is definitely not in my best interest!

**虚构集**：我以为我们已经是命定的同路人了！因为，我也有必须进入监狱的理由——\
**Recoleta**: What sort of pusillanimous coward would I be if I just abandoned my fated companions here? Of course, I'm going in with you, or rather, you're coming with me!

**维尔汀**：虚构集小姐，有人过来了。\
**Vertin**: Please get down, Ms. Recoleta. Someone's coming our way.

监狱围栏的另一侧，属于大型捕食者的视线锁定了围墙上鬼鬼祟祟的身影。\
From the other side of the prison fence, a predator's gaze locks onto the figure perched on the wall.

**？？？**：你们在这儿做什么？\
**???**: Stop right there! What do you think you're doing?!

**虚构集**：噢，糟糕，又是她。科马拉的狱卒来了。\
**Recoleta**: Damn! It's her again. The jailer of Comala!

**十四行诗**：科马拉的狱卒……？\
**Sonetto**: Did she say jailer or jaguar?

**狱卒**：虚构集小姐，我认得你。并且我衷心地希望不要再见到你。\
**Jailer**: Ms. Recoleta. Haven't I made myself clear? I don't want to see you here again.

**虚构集**：嗨，狱卒小姐，我倒是很高兴见到你。你瞧，今天的天气多么——\
**Recoleta**: Jailer! We meet again! What a delightful encounter on such a—

一阵冷风及时打断了她无意义的寒暄。\
A sudden gust of cold wind interrupts her.

**虚构集**：多么舒适宜人！\
**Recoleta**: —lovely day!

**狱卒**：你可以现在就离开这里吗？\
**Jailer**: Would you please just leave this place alone?

**狱卒**：我不明白，一位像你这样的小姐，为什么要执着地进入监狱？\
**Jailer**: I'll never understand why a promising young woman like you keeps snooping around a prison.

**狱卒**：我已经告诉过你，像试图闯入科马拉的这种行为，并不足以让你真正坐牢，却会让你在宪兵处吃尽苦头。\
**Jailer**: I can't make this any clearer: trying to break into Comala will do nothing to get you inside, but it will get you into a world of trouble with the gendarmes.

**狱卒**：希望你不要再进行无谓的尝试了。\
**Jailer**: So, will you stop these senseless break-in attempts?

**狱卒**：除却官方批准的学会成员与报社记者，科马拉监狱不允许任何外人参观。\
**Jailer**: Comala Prison is only accessible to academic researchers and journalists, and even they must have official credentials in order to enter.

**虚构集**：但、但是我必须得找到……\
**Recoleta**: Isn't there any other way to pay a visit? I truly do need to get in there.

她绞尽脑汁地思索着理由。\
She racks her brain for a plausible excuse.

**维尔汀**：您刚刚提到了，官方。\
**Vertin**: Sorry to interrupt, but did you just say "official credentials"?

**狱卒**：是的。这位小姐，请问您是？\
**Jailer**: Yes, you heard me right. And you are?

**维尔汀**：实际上，我是圣洛夫基金会的司辰。\
**Vertin**: I'm the Timekeeper of the St. Pavlov Foundation.

**维尔汀**：根据圣洛夫基金会的指令，我们前来拜访这座科马拉监狱——这是我的证件，它如假包换。\
**Vertin**: My assistant and I are here to visit Comala Prison on official orders from the Foundation. Here, this is my ID.

**十四行诗**：……\
**Sonetto**: ...

一些无关紧要的先斩后奏，让旁边并不擅长撒谎的第一助手涨红了脸。\
At the thought of lying, Sonetto's lips fail to open for even a squeak. She goes flush red with embarrassment.

隔着监狱的围栏，狱卒犹豫地接过了那张身份证明。\
Through the prison fence, the jailer examines the pair as she takes the ID in her sizeable paws.

那是一张很有质感的卡片，上面还印有圣洛夫基金会的印章。\
It is at least a very presentable-looking card, boldly stamped with the seal of the St. Pavlov Foundation.

**狱卒**：……的确是真的。\
**Jailer**: This is indeed legitimate.

她喃喃地说道。\
She murmurs.

**狱卒**：欢迎您来到科马拉监狱，维尔汀小姐。\
**Jailer**: Welcome to Comala Prison.

**狱卒**：请您原谅我的鲁莽。事实上，已经很久很久，没有官方相关的人员来过这里了。\
**Jailer**: Apologies for my earlier behavior. It's been a while since we've had any official visitors.

## 9TH-04 科马拉流浪记 / Comala's Callers

关于那些神秘的字句，那些词语中的停顿，能量扰动学家为了研究它们的随机性，日日夜夜躲藏在阿马尔菲塔诺城镇外的沙丘中。\
Day after day, the Paracausality Researcher hid away in the wilderness outside the town of Amalfitano studying the data she had collected.

一天傍晚，就在能量扰动学家来回捣鼓那些断电的录音设备与磁带时，有人叫住了埋在沙洞里的她。\
One evening at dusk, a voice called out from outside her cave. She put down the equipment and her tapes and stepped outside. A man stood curiously at her door.

“阿马尔菲塔诺已经什么都不剩了。”陌生的男人好奇地问道，“你在这干什么？”\
"What are you doing here?" he asked, raising both eyebrows. "Nothing ever happens in Amalfitano these days."

来人说他是阿马尔菲塔诺的银行职员。他面上带着一种灵动的希望，仿佛让人可以一直信任，而从不会对所处的境地感到绝望。\
The local introduced himself as the Bank Clerk. He had probably the most amiable face around—bright eyes, lifted cheeks, a soft jawline. It was a face beaming with hope.

Una tarde al anochecer, una voz llamó desde fuera de su cueva. Ella dejó el equipo y las cintas y salió afuera. Un hombre estaba de pie, curioso, frente a su puerta. "¿Qué haces aquí?" preguntó, levantando ambas cejas. "Nada sucede en Amalfitano en estos días." El local se presentó como el Empleado del Banco. Probablemente tenía la cara más amable del lugar—ojos brillantes, mejillas levantadas, una mandíbula suave. Era una cara llena de esperanza.\
能量扰动学家解释了那些高高低低的波纹中蕴含的迷人随机性：无限的宇宙与时间尽数潜藏于此，而她正是为此而来。\
Una tarde al anochecer, una voz llamó desde fuera de su cueva. Ella dejó el equipo y las cintas y salió afuera. Un hombre estaba de pie, curioso, frente a su puerta. "¿Qué haces aquí?" preguntó, levantando ambas cejas. "Nada sucede en Amalfitano en estos días." El local se presentó como el Empleado del Banco. Probablemente tenía la cara más amable del lugar—ojos brillantes, mejillas levantadas, una mandíbula suave. Era una cara llena de esperanza.\
The Researcher showed him the spectrums she'd been compiling. "I've been collecting stories about the Die," she explained. "Perhaps they hold the key to explaining the randomness that fate displays."

“伙计，这听起来真有意思，我愿意一直听你讲下去。但我必须去参加沙漠捕鱼人的葬礼了！”银行职员向她告别。\
"Ah, that does intrigue me so!" the Bank Clerk replied briskly, "I'd love to hear all about it. But I have to go. I mustn't be late to the Dune Piscator's funeral." And with that, he left.

三天后，同样的脚步声出现在相反的方向。\
Three days later, the same footsteps returned to her cave.

La Investigadora le mostró los espectros que había estado recopilando. "He estado recolectando historias sobre el Dado," explicó. "Quizás ellos contienen la clave para explicar la aleatoriedad que muestra el destino." "¡Ah, eso realmente me intriga!" respondió rápidamente el Empleado del Banco, "Me encantaría escuchar todo sobre eso. Pero debo irme—no debo llegar tarde al funeral del Pescador de Dunas." Y con eso, se fue. Tres días después, los mismos pasos regresaron a su cueva.\
能量扰动学家向这位老熟人问好：“银行职员，好久不见。你从葬礼回来了！”\
La Investigadora le mostró los espectros que había estado recopilando. "He estado recolectando historias sobre el Dado," explicó. "Quizás ellos contienen la clave para explicar la aleatoriedad que muestra el destino." "¡Ah, eso realmente me intriga!" respondió rápidamente el Empleado del Banco, "Me encantaría escuchar todo sobre eso. Pero debo irme—no debo llegar tarde al funeral del Pescador de Dunas." Y con eso, se fue. Tres días después, los mismos pasos regresaron a su cueva.\
"You're back! How have you been? Did you make it to the funeral?" She asked.

“我不知晓你在说什么，我并不是你想象中的那个人。”面前的男人说。他的神色是一种深深的疲惫，如同他的生活已经没剩什么可期待的了。\
"I have no idea what you're talking about," he replied tersely. "I'm not the man you think I am." His face was drained and gaunt, his eyes sunken deep into hollow sockets. It was as if every spark of life had been drawn out of him, leaving only an empty husk.

"¡Volviste! ¿Cómo has estado? ¿Lograste llegar al funeral?" Preguntó. "No tengo idea de lo que estás hablando," respondió de manera cortante. "No soy el hombre que crees que soy." Su rostro estaba agotado y demacrado, sus ojos hundidos profundamente en huecos vacíos. Era como si toda chispa de vida le hubiera sido arrancada, dejándolo solo con una cáscara vacía.\
能量扰动学家尝试向面前的人说明，她通过频谱中的停顿与随机性来辨认万事万物，因而她绝不会错认任何一人。\
"¡Volviste! ¿Cómo has estado? ¿Lograste llegar al funeral?" Preguntó. "No tengo idea de lo que estás hablando," respondió de manera cortante. "No soy el hombre que crees que soy." Su rostro estaba agotado y demacrado, sus ojos hundidos profundamente en huecos vacíos. Era como si toda chispa de vida le hubiera sido arrancada, dejándolo solo con una cáscara vacía.\
The Researcher insisted she wasn't mistaken. "I know people by their deeper nature, down to the synchronicity of their spectrums. I've never been wrong before."

“我听不明白这些玄乎的。捕鱼耗尽了我的精力，现在我要回家去休息了。”沙漠捕鱼人迈着与银行职员一模一样的步伐，拖着破旧的渔网朝小镇中走去。\
"Whatever you say." The man muttered roughly. "I don't understand anything of your high-minded ideas. Just let me go. It's been a long day out there fishing, and all I want now is to collapse on my rickety bed." He trudged off with footsteps that sounded exactly like those of the Bank Clerk's.

**狱卒**：La investigadora insistió en que no se había equivocado. "Conozco a las personas por su naturaleza más profunda, hasta la sincronización de sus espectros. Nunca me he equivocado antes." "Lo que tú digas." El hombre murmuró de manera áspera. "No entiendo nada de tus ideas tan elevadas. Solo déjame ir. Ha sido un largo día de pesca, y lo único que quiero ahora es desplomarme en mi cama tambaleante." Se alejó con pasos que sonaban exactamente como los del Empleado del Banco.\
 如您所见，维尔汀小姐，这里是一个特殊的实验机构——\
**Jailer**: La investigadora insistió en que no se había equivocado. "Conozco a las personas por su naturaleza más profunda, hasta la sincronización de sus espectros. Nunca me he equivocado antes." "Lo que tú digas." El hombre murmuró de manera áspera. "No entiendo nada de tus ideas tan elevadas. Solo déjame ir. Ha sido un largo día de pesca, y lo único que quiero ahora es desplomarme en mi cama tambaleante." Se alejó con pasos que sonaban exactamente como los del Empleado del Banco.\
 As you might have noticed, Ms. Vertin, this facility isn't just a prison. It's also a research center.

**狱卒**：它的全名为科马拉实验性全景监狱，由国家福柯学会在1975年建立。\
**Jailer**: Its full name is "the Panopticon of Comala." It was established by the Foucault Association in 1975.

**狱卒**：科马拉监狱举办过很多的学术讨论，如果您有留意过之前的官方报纸，甚至还能看到关于科马拉的专题报告……\
**Jailer**: We've hosted workshops, academic sessions, and even lectures about the Panopticon. You may even have seen some reports about it.

**狱卒**：协会一直保持开放与进步的态度。我们很欢迎任何官方的成员与精神分析专家前来共同探讨。\
**Jailer**: Experts of psychoanalysis and scholars from various fields have come here to exchange ideas and seek collaboration in their studies.

**狱卒**：很快，您就会发现，这里和普通的监狱并不一样。\
**Jailer**: In many ways, the Panopticon is unlike any other prison you've seen before.

**维尔汀**：谢谢您的介绍，我理解为什么会有人想主动被关进监狱了。\
**Vertin**: I see. No wonder Ms. Recoleta has gone to such lengths to become a part of it.

**维尔汀**：事实上，我们本次前来，还有一个重要的任务。请问这里是否有一位名叫德洛丝的女士？\
**Vertin**: Actually, my assistant and I are here to inquire about a prisoner named Dores. Does that name sound familiar?

**狱卒**：据我所知，监狱中并没有名叫德洛丝的囚犯。她是否有别的名字，或者身份？您能描述一下她的外貌特征吗？\
**Jailer**: Not that I recall. Could she have used a different name? What does she look like?

**维尔汀**：让我想想。德洛丝女士有可能是被囚禁于此的囚犯，也可能是……监狱的客人。我并不确定，她是三天前到达科马拉监狱的。\
**Vertin**: Hmm. She'd have arrived here about three days ago. It's also possible that she came as a visitor, not a prisoner.

**维尔汀**：她是一位盲眼的女士，总是手持一台老式的打字机。\
**Vertin**: She's a blind woman who always carries an old typewriter.

**维尔汀**：她来自巴西圣保罗荣军院，是一名无国界医生。\
**Vertin**: She used to be a doctor at the São Paulo Veterans' Residence in Brazil.

**维尔汀**：偶尔，她会编写游记，以“兀尔德”的笔名给神秘学杂志投稿。\
**Vertin**: And on the subject of different names, she once wrote for UTTU under the name "Urd."

**狱卒**：维尔汀小姐，您的描述让我困惑了。我没有见过这位女士，三天前也并无任何新囚犯进入。\
**Jailer**: I don't think I've seen anyone fitting that description. And as I said, we haven't had any visitors in some time. Certainly not in the last three days.

**虚构集**：但我确实是在三天前遇到德洛丝女士的。当时，她正往科马拉的方向走去！\
**Recoleta**: But I did see her! I saw her walking towards Comala Prison!

**狱卒**：那消息的来源就显得有些可疑了——\
**Jailer**: Someone must have mixed up their memories. Simply put, I don't recall seeing anyone by that name or with that description here.

**维尔汀**：没关系，感谢您的回答。也许是我们弄错了。\
**Vertin**: I see. Thank you, Miss. Perhaps we made a mistake.

问话无果，在狱卒对她们生疑之前，调查员们马上转移了话题。\
Sensing that her current line of questioning is going nowhere, she shifts toward a different topic.

**维尔汀**：虚构集小姐，刚刚您说，您有必须进入监狱的理由，所以为什么要如此执着地进入科马拉监狱呢？\
**Vertin**: Ms. Recoleta, you've gone to great lengths to get into the Panopticon. Would you mind telling us why?

**虚构集**：终于，你终于问出了这个问题！我一直等待着这一刻，维尔汀。\
**Recoleta**: Finally! I've been waiting for you to ask!

**虚构集**：一切都起因于我那位居住在科马拉的笔友！\
**Recoleta**: I'm here to find my pen pal in Comala!

**维尔汀**：笔友？\
**Vertin**: You have a pen pal ... in here?

**虚构集**：半年前，在瓜达拉哈拉的图书博览会中，我给一些与会的作家寄去我的小说开头，希望能得到他们的回覆和评价。\
**Recoleta**: Yes. 6 months ago, I went to a book exhibition in Guadalajara and came across the contact details of a few writers. I sent them my novel and asked for feedback.

**虚构集**：这听起来有些冒犯，但很多作家间的友情都是这样开始的。\
**Recoleta**: Looking back, it was a bit forward. But nothing unheard of between writers. A lot of friendships start through letters, you see.

**虚构集**：就是在这时，我收到了阿莱夫的回信。\
**Recoleta**: And Aleph wrote back.

虚构集从怀中取出一沓厚厚的信件。\
Recoleta produces a thick stack of letters from her coat.

收信的地址一直在发生变化，象征着面前流浪作家波动不断的人生；但寄信地址却是永恒静止的科马拉。\
The recipient's address changes with each letter, reflecting the turbulent lifestyle of the wandering writer, yet the sender's address is eternally constant—Comala.

**维尔汀**：所以您的笔友，他是个怎样的人？\
**Vertin**: And how much do you know about this pen pal of yours?

**虚构集**：噢！这很难形容，但首先“阿莱夫”是一个阳性词。\
**Recoleta**: Oh, well. He calls himself "Aleph," which is a grammatically masculine word, so—

**维尔汀**：这就是您将阿莱夫称为“他”的原因。\
**Vertin**: So you assume Aleph is a man.

听起来只是一个没什么道理的主观臆测。\
A reasonable suspicion, but in her experience, never a certainty.

**虚构集**：其次，我认为他是一个诗人，一个博学的作家，有可能是个隐居的炼金术师。他总是能回答我的任何问题，任何！\
**Recoleta**: Yes. He's probably a poet, a writer, perhaps even an alchemist. He's one of the brightest people I know. There's never been a question that he couldn't answer!

**虚构集**：你能想象吗？无论是宗教、政治还是历史，或者偏门的魔药与炼金学……从来没有他答不上的范畴。他甚至给了我小说的续写建议。\
**Recoleta**: I've asked him about religion, politics, history, potions, even critters in length and breadth. Can you imagine someone who knows all those things and so extensively too?

**虚构集**：他对小说中人物动态的掌握总是无比精确而真实，就像那些人物都有了自己的意志一样。\
**Recoleta**: And he helped me with my novel. He always seems to know the best ways to bring my characters to life.

**虚构集**：也许他真的是个故事天才，或者有着超于常人的阅历……\
**Recoleta**: Honestly, he's so insightful. I've begun wondering if he's omniscient.

**虚构集**：在他的协助下，我完善了一版又一版的小说开头，只是这个沙漠小镇的故事，却总是无法得到真正的结局……\
**Recoleta**: With his help, my story grew richer and fuller, like a well-tended plant. Strangely, I can't seem to take it any further now. It's as if the roots have been sapped of their strength.

**虚构集**：这太不可思议了。我必须见到他，亲口问他，我的小说究竟哪里出了问题？\
**Recoleta**: I couldn't understand why. So, I resolved that I would see him in person to find out.

**狱卒**：……关于你的笔友，我已经听过二十遍有余了。\
**Jailer**: Again with this story about your uncanny pen pal. I've already told you a dozen times.

**狱卒**：感人的故事。但很遗憾，我丝毫看不出这种无关紧要的个人琐事能成为你闯入公共权力机关的理由。\
**Jailer**: It's all very moving, but it still doesn't justify your actions.

**狱卒**：不少作家都会遇到这样的难题，写了一个美好的开头，却无法让故事继续下去，这没什么特别的。不是仅存在于你一个人身上的困境。\
**Jailer**: Writers experience mental blocks all the time. Yet you don't see them trying to break into a prison over it.

**维尔汀**：确实如此。\
**Vertin**: She does have a point.

**虚构集**：狱卒小姐，维尔汀，你们的说法有些伤人了。\
**Recoleta**: Please, Vertin, Jailer! Have a little mercy, will you?

**维尔汀**：我还有另一个问题，虚构集小姐。为什么您一直称呼狱卒小姐为“狱卒小姐”？\
**Vertin**: Hold on. I've been meaning to ask—why are you only calling her "Jailer"?

**维尔汀**：将职务作为名称，这是作家特有的习惯吗？\
**Vertin**: Don't you know her name? Or do you just prefer addressing people by their occupation?

**虚构集**：啊！不是，关于这个——\
**Recoleta**: Oh, about that—

出乎意料，这回却是美洲豹打断了她们的对话。\
Unexpectedly, it is the jaguar herself that speaks up.

**狱卒**：请不要在意，维尔汀小姐。狱卒就是狱卒，它是一个很好的身份，也是一个很好的称呼。\
**Jailer**: It's okay, Ms. Vertin. I don't mind being called by my job title. I take pride in what I do.

**狱卒**：当然，您可以不用称呼我为“小姐”。我只是一个狱卒。\
**Jailer**: I'm perfectly fine with just being "the jailer."

**虚构集**：是的，就像能量扰动学家一样，她只是一个能量扰动学家。\
**Recoleta**: Exactly! A researcher is a researcher, and a jailer is a jailer.

**维尔汀**：……？\
**Vertin**: ...?

**虚构集**：我的意思是，这是一个值得琢磨的象征。就像你的名字一样，十四行诗。\
**Recoleta**: Titles and code names often tell us more about people than their ordinary given names, don't you think? Take Sonetto, for example.

**虚构集**：你的名字很具有象征性。十四行诗，那是一种伟大的体裁，来自诗一般的意大利。\
**Recoleta**: Your name comes from sonnets, doesn't it? That great poetic form from Italy.

**虚构集**：少部分人误以为它来自于莎士比亚，而更多人以为它来自彼特拉克……但没人真正知道第一个写出它的人是谁。\
**Recoleta**: Some people mistakenly think Shakespeare invented it; some say it was Petrarca ... Though no one really knows when the first sonnet was written.

**虚构集**：十四行诗，从你的手势中，我猜你也的确是一位意大利人。这是你的笔名、代称，还是真正的名字？也许你是出生于一个诗人的家庭？\
**Recoleta**: Sorry, I'm straying from my point. You're Italian, aren't you, Sonetto? Is that your real name, or just a code name? Were your parents poets?

**十四行诗**：嗯……我很愿意回答你的问题，但我其实没有父母，也没有对于家庭的印象。\
**Sonetto**: Umm. As much as I'd like to be able to answer your question, I never knew my parents.

**十四行诗**：自我有记忆起，我就在基金会的第一防线学校了。\
**Sonetto**: My earliest memories were of the School of Primary Defense of Mankind. I've lived there since I was a small child.

**虚构集**：……抱歉，我不该这么冒犯的。\
**Recoleta**: Ah. My apologies. That was thoughtless of me.

**十四行诗**：没关系，虚构集小姐。如果德洛丝女士确实如你所说，进入了科马拉监狱……\
**Sonetto**: It's fine. You meant no ill intent, I'm sure.

**十四行诗**：司辰，无论是狱卒小姐对此并不知情，亦或是监狱方藏匿了德洛丝女士的行踪，我们都应该继续调查。\
**Sonetto**: Timekeeper, if Ms. Recoleta was right about Dr. Dores's whereabouts, perhaps the jailer is keeping things from us, or perhaps Dr. Dores visited the Panopticon without her knowledge. Either way, we need to do some digging here.

**维尔汀**：我认同。在这种情况下，也许询问囚犯们更能获得线索。\
**Vertin**: I agree. Let's see if we can talk to some of the inmates and find out what they know.

闲谈之间，无穷延伸的水域与甬道终于走到了尽头，前面也隐隐传来喧闹声。\
As they chat, the corridors—until now endless—reach a terminal point, with voices echoing ahead.

**狱卒**：来自基金会的诸位，我们马上要到达科马拉监狱的大厅了。\
**Jailer**: Ladies, we're about to enter the main hall of the Panopticon.

**狱卒**：平日，这里是囚犯活动的场地之一。但现在应该不是活动的时间……\
**Jailer**: This is one of the places where the inmates spend their recreation time. At this hour, they're supposed to be in their cells. But what's all that noise?

一反常态的嘈杂让狱卒心中有了不祥的预感。\
The jailer seems to be tense with the apparently unusual amount of noise.

**狱卒**：……如果一会儿发生了什么事儿，维尔汀小姐，您能帮我看好她吗？\
**Jailer**: Ms. Vertin, could you keep an eye on Recoleta if anything happens?

狱卒指了指正在努力融入基金会队伍，让自己不那么瞩目的虚构集。\
Recoleta tries her best to avoid the hard stare of the feline jailer by blending into the Foundation team.

**维尔汀**：没问题。\
**Vertin**: Certainly.

**虚构集**：什么？我不会逃跑的！\
**Recoleta**: What do you take me for? I'm not going to run away!

**虚构集**：如果我逃跑的话，那可真是一个无比糟糕的故事开头！\
**Recoleta**: That'd be a pretty cheesy way to start a story!

**狱卒**：……\
**Jailer**: ...

**狱卒**：诸位，请跟紧我的步伐。\
**Jailer**: Please just stay close to me.

## 9TH-05 美洲神话 / A Latin American Fable

**十四行诗**：没想到这座环形建筑的内部，竟是这样的……\
**Sonetto**: I didn't expect any of this from what we saw outside.

斑驳而整洁的墙壁，平静的水域，迷宫中无声伫立的白色巨塔。\
The mottled yet pristine walls, the still waters, the silent white tower standing within the labyrinth.

不远处，数名囚犯围成一圈，他们有站有坐，正在交流着什么。\
Nearby, several prisoners form a circle, some standing, some sitting, engaged in conversation.

**狱卒**：……哎。我要去履行一下我的工作职责，请几位稍等片刻。\
**Jailer**: *sigh* Excuse me for a moment. I have duties that I must attend to.

狱卒一边叹气，一边走进了集会的圈子。出乎意料的是，囚犯们并未表现出任何应有的情绪。\
With a sigh, the jailer steps into the gathering, causing a strangely subdued reaction from the prisoners.

**十四行诗**：他们并不害怕她。\
**Sonetto**: They don't seem intimidated by her at all.

**虚构集**：比起囚犯，他们反倒像一群在自家花园里聊天的艺术家们。而狱卒呢，只是因他们大声喧闹而前来喝止的倒霉邻居。\
**Recoleta**: Yeah, they just look like a bunch of artists having a chat in the garden. And the jailer seems to be like a grumpy neighbor coming over to ask them to keep it down.

面前，“倒霉邻居”正呵斥着“艺术家们”。\
The "grumpy neighbor" continues her chastising.

**狱卒**：我已经说过许多遍，狱医没有允许你们在这里举办集会，你们不能这么做。\
**Jailer**: Everyone, you know the rules. There are to be no after-hours gatherings here without the Physician's approval.

**囚犯Ⅰ**：哈哈哈……你的每一次警告，语气都会比上一次更温和。要不干脆加入我们？这可比你那无聊的工作要有意思多了！\
**Inmate I**: You sound softer and softer each time you come to warn us. Why not just join us? Isn't it better than circling around the Panopticon all day?

**囚犯Ⅰ**：触发事件之厅可是监狱中最适合举办沙龙的地方。\
**Inmate I**: And look around you. We're in the Hall of New Encounters. What better place to host a salon?

**囚犯Ⅱ**：如果你不能理解文学的美妙之处，那你在科马拉的人生将会毫无意义。\
**Inmate II**: You're missing out in Comala if you don't even get a taste of our literature.

**囚犯Ⅰ**：的确如此。先前，就连那群滴石油的音乐家们，也会偶尔参加我们的集会呢——虽然我敢打包票，他们对文学一点儿兴趣都没有。\
**Inmate I**: Exactly. Even those oil-dripping musicians drop by from time to time. Not that they're the kind to care about the beauty of words.

**十四行诗**：滴石油的音乐家？司辰，难道他们说的是——\
**Sonetto**: Oil-dripping musicians? Timekeeper, could they mean—

狱卒正打算再说些什么，闲谈中的两名囚犯却同时朝她比了一个噤声的手势，指了指围成一圈的人群。\
Before the jailer can say anything else, two of the prisoners simultaneously gesture for her to stay silent, pointing to the center of their gathering.

**囚犯Ⅰ**：请保持安静！理想家先生的沙龙要开始了。\
**Inmate I**: Quiet now, please! The Idealist's salon is about to start.

**狱卒**：……\
**Jailer**: ...

**维尔汀**：看来那边已经没什么危险了。走吧，我们也去看看。\
**Vertin**: These people seem friendly enough. Why don't we see what this is about?

**集会囚犯Ⅰ**：我们在荒漠，在恒星，在迷宫\
**Gathering Participant I**: In deserts, in stars, within labyrinths,

**集会囚犯Ⅱ**：我们在水面，垂直下沉，照镜子\
**Gathering Participant II**: In waters, in mirrors, within reflections,

**集会囚犯Ⅲ**：我们在村庄，做梦，与死亡贴脸颊\
**Gathering Participant III**: We dream on death's straw pillow.

**集会囚犯Ⅳ**：我们在此处，向幽灵致意\
**Gathering Participant IV**: Here we are, paying tribute to the ghosts,

**集会囚犯Ⅴ**：我们抛开一切，再一次\
**Gathering Participant V**: To give it all up again.

**所有集会囚犯**：再一次，再一次\
**All Participants**: To give it all up again.

**理想家**：朋友们，我必须宣布：本能现实主义运动仍处于困难时期。\
**The Idealist**: My dear friends, we face a difficult truth: the movement of visceral realism still stumbles in the dark.

**理想家**：我们的诗歌、我们的语言、我们的头脑、我们的世界，每一个角落都充斥着古旧的幻想：一个属于中产阶级的幻想。\
**The Idealist**: Our poems, our language, our minds are tangled by a stifling vine—a mundane, stale vision shared among all bourgeoisie.

**理想家**：这是我们最大的障碍，在这种幻想之中，我们无法创造出任何的新艺术形式——人类的障碍在于过度依靠逻辑和常识。\
**The Idealist**: We follow this vision blindly, clinging to the comfort brought by logic and conventional wisdom, and by it, we nip every branch of new art in the bud.

**理想家**：在个人层面，诗歌是无用的举动。但在这所监狱里，举办葬礼的我们比谁都崭新。\
**The Idealist**: Poems are perhaps too fragile an outgrowth to develop one's life upon. But here, we may light them like candles at our funerals.

**理想家**：我们必须不断地活着，不断地死去，让诗歌连接我们与这个世界。\
**The Idealist**: Let poetry become the bridge between us and the world.

突兀而孤单的掌声响了起来：它比其余所有观众的欢呼都来得要早。\
A lone clap breaks the silence. It comes earlier than all the other cheers from the audience.

**虚构集**：在不断活着与死去之中，我们将获得一双生死过渡的眼睛。它能越过那些人类的障碍，这是一双属于诗人的眼睛。\
**Recoleta**: As we come back and forth over the boundaries of life and death, the old obstacles begin to take on a new look. With the eyes of poets, we may see behind them.

**虚构集**：你是一位本能现实主义者。\
**Recoleta**: You're a visceral realist.

**虚构集**：错不了，这位先生，你一定是——\
**Recoleta**: I can't be mistaken. You must be—

理想家的目光穿越了文学爱好者的树林，直达远处漂浮而来的新大陆。\
The Idealist's eyes pierce through the grove of literary enthusiasts, reaching a distant, drifting new world.

**理想家**：我记得每一个牛仔回到故乡的神情，记得那种迟来的欣喜。\
**The Idealist**: A lonely cowboy. Finally home.

**理想家**：它是一个美丽的奇迹。\
**The Idealist**: What a wonder.

**理想家**：诸位很好运，本次文学沙龙才刚刚开始，并且美洲诗社与那些具备领地意识的\
正统沙龙不同——我们欢迎诸位的参与。\
**The Idealist**: You're in time. The salon has just begun. And La Sociedad de Poetas de las Américas isn't like those salons that care more about who's invited than the art. All are welcome here.

**十四行诗**：一个在监狱里的……文学沙龙，亦或是探戈舞会。还是说，两者兼具……\
**Sonetto**: A literary salon in a prison? Though so far it seems to have more dancing than poems.

**维尔汀**：你能理解这位先生方才的发言吗？\
**Vertin**: Did you understand what that man just said?

**十四行诗**：暂时还没有，司辰。我需要时间思考一下……\
**Sonetto**: No, sorry, Timekeeper. I need a moment to think it through.

**维尔汀**：没关系的。我想并不是只有我们听不懂。\
**Vertin**: Don't worry, Sonetto. I would guess we're not the only ones who are confused here.

**维尔汀**：狱卒小姐，这就是您所说的，科马拉监狱的不同寻常吗？\
**Vertin**: Ms. Jailer, is this that peculiarity about Comala you mentioned earlier?

**狱卒**：……\
**Jailer**: ...

**狱卒**：理想家，停止你的危险行为。你应该意识到这里是监狱。\
**Jailer**: Enough, Idealist. You're still an inmate here, and you're walking a very fine line right now.

**理想家**：噢，是的，正因如此。\
**The Idealist**: Oh, I'm quite aware of where I am and what lines I tread.

**理想家**：这里可是监狱。纵观拉丁美洲，还有什么地方比这儿的风险更小吗？毕竟我总不能被抓进监狱里的监狱去。\
**The Idealist**: This is a prison. The safest place for poets in this part of the continent. One cannot be arrested twice, after all.

男子的话引得哄堂大笑，囚犯们眉飞色舞，兴高采烈地讨论着刚才的演说。\
The man's words draw laughter from the other prisoners as they turn to discuss the speech with excitement.

**理想家**：请你放心，狱卒小姐，我们不过是一群诗人罢了，又能制造什么麻烦呢？\
**The Idealist**: But please, don't trouble yourself with our little farce. What harm could a few poets possibly do?

所有不规则的韵脚、自由野性的美学矛盾，都汇聚成一股纷扰的逆流，冲击着初来乍到的访客。\
All the irregular rhymes and wild contradictions of aesthetics converge into a chaotic countercurrent, crashing against the newcomers.

虚构集震惊地握紧拳头，她几乎要确信面前的男子就是自己那神秘的笔友了。\
Recoleta clenches her fists in shock—certain that the man before her is her mysterious pen pal.

**虚构集**：这位先生，你是叫……理想家对吗？虽然有点冒昧，但我能问你一些问题吗？\
**Recoleta**: Mr. Idealist? Might I ask you something?

**狱卒**：等等！所有与囚犯的交流都必须符合监狱的行为规范。我们会将访谈进行记录并上交官方。\
**Jailer**: Hold on, Recoleta. All forms of communication with the inmates must conform to our regulations. We will need to record the conversation and submit it to higher authorities for review.

**维尔汀**：我也有些问题想要问这位先生。狱卒小姐，我们会遵守规定的。\
**Vertin**: I have some questions for the gentleman as well, but we're more than willing to follow the rules.

**维尔汀**：身为传记作家的德洛丝女士也许会对这个诗社感兴趣。\
**Vertin**: I think the person I'm looking for might have attended this literary salon, or at least talked to some of its members.

**维尔汀**：如果她真的进入了科马拉监狱，面前这位……先生就有可能见过她。\
**Vertin**: I'd wager she's spoken to that gentleman. That is ... if she has been here at all.

**狱卒**：……我明白了。请诸位控制交流的时长。\
**Jailer**: I see. Go ahead then. Just watch the time.

在访客们低声向狱卒解释的片刻，虚构集已越过纷纷攘攘的人群，她深吸一口气。\
As the visitors petition the jailer, Recoleta pushes past the bustling crowd and takes a deep breath.

**虚构集**：我就单刀直入地问了。理想家先生，你就是阿莱夫吗？嘈杂的氛围忽然陷入了寂静——就像一旁了无涟漪的水域。理想家因这个出人意料的名字而诧异，他一边整理领带，一边整理措辞。理想家: 哈，又是一个等待阿莱夫回答的索问者。虚构集: ……你果然知晓阿莱夫这个名字！理想家: 当然，只是——我没有义务告诉你。沙龙主持人不置可否。他的目光好奇地转向了虚构集的同行者。理想家: 你呢，这位戴帽子的女士，你们都是来找阿莱夫的吗？真是热闹的一天！维尔汀: 我与虚构集小姐有不同的目标。我正在寻找一位名叫德洛丝的盲眼女士。理想家: 噢，我记得她，她的文字干净整洁，仪表堂堂，就像橱窗里精美漂亮的异国鳄鱼皮手包，充满着高贵的凝视、傲慢和偏见。维尔汀: 您知道她现在在哪里吗？理想家: 女士，我不可能时刻掌握监狱中每一位囚犯的去向。理想家: 那些代表权力的规则知晓一切，也许它才是你该询问的对象。理想家: 在这里，一切的行为都无法逃离瞭望塔里面的那双眼睛。虚构集: ……眼睛？她下意识环顾监狱的大厅。墙壁、巨塔和水池一如既往，四周没有任何异样。在场所有的囚犯都深以为然地点头，这让一直忍受着荒唐对话的狱卒叹了口气。狱卒: 理想家，你今天按时服药了吗？理想家: 无需服药，我现在状态极佳，谢谢你的关心。狱卒: 我警告过你，反抗狱医安排的治疗是不明智的行为。理想家: 你误会我的意思了。反抗？我们这里没有人想要反抗狱医。理想家: 事实上，狱医应该根本听不懂一个字——他是怎么得到他的医学学位的？靠用锯子打开神秘学家的脑壳吗？还是那落后的神秘学家颅相学？囚犯们都会意地笑了起来。理想家: 唉！狱卒小姐，也许你仍有机会成为一位诗人，但绝对不是现在。理想家: 那些反抗，那些政治的话题，在科马拉外头的时候，我们已经聊得够多了——不然我们为什么会在这里，成为一名“精神病人”？理想家: 已经过去太久，久到军政府下台，我们仍没能摆脱被成为一名精神病人的命运。理想家: 久到文学大爆炸的时代过去，短暂的繁华消失，世界重新变成一片荒芜。狱卒: ……你到底想说什么？虚构集: 我想他要说的是，有关权力的一切都让人感到厌倦而毫无意义。虚构集: 和生命真正有关的只有诗歌本身。理想家: 狱卒小姐，你瞧，一位科马拉的外人都比你更通情达理。是时候适当地听从这些意见了。理想家: 为了对抗那双无处不在的眼睛，诗社才是我们使自己存在的方式——狱卒: 理想家！最后一次警告，你该停止这一切了。理想家: 好吧，好吧！很遗憾，由于狱卒小姐的到来，今日的沙龙到此结束了。底下嘘声一片，聚集的囚犯渐渐散去了。理想家: 至于诸位敬爱的客人，我并不想卖关子，但我诚挚地邀请各位，与我一同前往美洲诗社的根据地。理想家: 也许你们要找的人，就在诗社的成员之中。男人做出了滑稽又肃穆的邀请姿势。维尔汀: 我们很乐意。狱卒小姐，请问我们能前往参观吗？狱卒: ……如果你们感兴趣的话，这也是囚犯生活的一部分。只是，请诸位不要把囚犯的胡言乱语当真。理想家: 太好了！让我为诸位引路，请随我来。\
**Recoleta**: *deep breath* Are you Aleph?

The noisy atmosphere plunges into silence, just like the still waters nearby.

The Idealist is evidently taken aback by the name.

**The Idealist**: Oh! *chuckle* Another visitor looking for Aleph.

**Recoleta**: So you know him!

**The Idealist**: Naturally. But I'm not obliged to speak of him to one who does not, stranger.

The salon host is noncommittal, turning toward Recoleta's companions.

**The Idealist**: And you, young lady in the hat? Are you here for Aleph as well? What a lively day this is!

**Vertin**: No. I'm looking for a blind woman. Her name is Dores.

**The Idealist**: Ah, yes. I remember. Her writing was impeccable, like an exquisite crocodile-skin handbag in a shop window, elegant, yet condescending.

**Vertin**: Do you know where she is now?

**The Idealist**: I'm not able to keep track of every inmate here, Miss.

**The Idealist**: Perhaps you should ask those who have seen everything from above.

**The Idealist**: Through the glass, where the scrutinizing eyes of power look down on us.

**Recoleta**: Eyes?

She scans the prison hall. The walls, the great tower, and the pool remain unchanged. Nothing appears amiss.

All the prisoners present nod in agreement, prompting a weary sigh from the jailer.

**Jailer**: Have you taken your medicine today, Idealist?

**The Idealist**: I'm feeling marvelous! Today, I require no help from them!

**Jailer**: I've warned you. It's unwise to act against the Physician's orders.

**The Idealist**: Act against him? No one may act against him here.

**The Idealist**: The Physician must have misunderstood us. I suspect he doesn't understand half of what we say. I'd like to know how he got his medical degree. Not by cracking open skulls, I should hope.

The prisoners exchange knowing smiles.

**The Idealist**: What a pity, Jailer! You know, I've always believed you had the soul of a poet, just like us.

**The Idealist**: We've already spoken enough "rebellious thoughts" outside of Comala.\
How else do you think we ended up in your nuthouse?

**The Idealist**: We've been here far too long, long after the Junta was removed from office,

**The Idealist**: after our home became a deserted wasteland in the aftermath of the Latin American Boom.

**Jailer**: What are you getting at?

**Recoleta**: That power is boring, meaningless. Nothing holds onto power forever.

**Recoleta**: And the one true connection we have to life is poetry.

**The Idealist**: See, Jailer? Even an outsider understands our ideas better than you. It's time to open your eyes to reality.

**The Idealist**: La Sociedad is the only way for us to feel truly alive in here, beneath the gaze of those prying, ever-vigilant eyes.

**Jailer**: Idealist! Last warning. Stop this now.

**The Idealist**: Fine, fine! Alright, companions. Sadly, the salon must come to an end, as our jailer insists.

The crowd murmurs and grumbles as they begin to disperse.

**The Idealist**: Dear friends, I do not mean to abuse the power of suspense. I sincerely invite you to come with me to the heart of La Sociedad de Poetas de las Américas.

**The Idealist**: Perhaps you'll find the person you look for there.

The man strikes a gesture somehow equally comedic and solemn.

**Vertin**: We'd love to. Umm, only if that's okay with you, Ms. Jailer?

**Jailer**: I suppose that's alright. You're already here; we can call it part of your tour. But, please, ladies, take none of their ramblings seriously.

**The Idealist**: Thank you, Jailer! Please, follow me.

## 9TH-06 生者的幻影 / Shadows of the Living

黎明前，能量扰动学家在形如墓穴的沙丘中醒来。\
The Researcher awakens in her dune cave, which felt to her as hollow as a tomb. It was a little before dawn.

磁带逐渐侵蚀了她所有的生存空间，录音反反复复地讲述着关于那座蓝色屋顶茅屋的传闻。\
Stacks of tapes had eaten up her living space, climbing up again and again, each of these spinning reels speaking of stories about that cottage with a blue roof.

La investigadora se despierta en su cueva en la duna, que le parecía tan vacía como una tumba. Era poco antes del amanecer. Montones de cintas habían ocupado su espacio vital, apilándose una y otra vez, cada uno de estos carretes giratorios hablabade historias sobre esa cabaña con techo azul.\
身后，死于谋杀的赶驴人幽灵说：“我听到过那些嘈杂的声音，那些来自不同年代的声音。如果我是你，我就不会进入那间诡异的屋子！”\
La investigadora se despierta en su cueva en la duna, que le parecía tan vacía como una tumba. Era poco antes del amanecer. Montones de cintas habían ocupado su espacio vital, apilándose una y otra vez, cada uno de estos carretes giratorios hablabade historias sobre esa cabaña con techo azul.\
She heard the voice of the Murdered Donkey Driver behind her: "I hear them all, the laughter and voices of generations past. Like dry leaves caught in the cracks of old walls, rustling only when the wind blows through. I wouldn't set foot in that house if I were you."

门槛旁边的乞丐说：“我在屋子外面过夜，每天凌晨时都能看见屋里有微弱的光亮。但从没人进去，也从没人出来。”\
The Door-Side Beggar spoke too: "I sleep on the porch every night. Each morning, a dim light glows through the window. But no one ever leaves through that door ... and no one has ever entered."

Then the Bank Clerk's voice: "It's the story of the 'alter ego.' That house must've been filled with debts no one would return to claim."

**另一个我**：银行职员推测：“一切都是有关[alter ego]的故事。这屋子里一定填满了死者的债务和无人偿还的账单。”\
Oyó la voz del Asesinado Conductor de Burros detrás de ella: "Oigo a todos ellos, las risas y las voces de generaciones pasadas. Como hojas secas atrapadas en las grietas de viejas paredes, crujiendo solo cuando el viento sopla a través. No pondría un pie en esa casa si fuera tú." El Mendigo al Lado de la Puerta también habló: "Duermo en el porche cada noche. Cada mañana, una luz tenue brilla a través de la ventana. Pero nadie sale nunca por esa puerta... y nadie ha entrado nunca." Luego la voz del Empleado del Banco: "Es la historia del "alter ego". Esa casa debe haber estado llena de deudas que nadie reclamaría."\
卧床的老妇人声音混杂着忏悔：“这屋子有自己的记忆。它记得那些在夜里失踪的人，还有在风暴中被带走的孩子。”\
Oyó la voz del Asesinado Conductor de Burros detrás de ella: "Oigo a todos ellos, las risas y las voces de generaciones pasadas. Como hojas secas atrapadas en las grietas de viejas paredes, crujiendo solo cuando el viento sopla a través. No pondría un pie en esa casa si fuera tú." El Mendigo al Lado de la Puerta también habló: "Duermo en el porche cada noche. Cada mañana, una luz tenue brilla a través de la ventana. Pero nadie sale nunca por esa puerta... y nadie ha entrado nunca." Luego la voz del Empleado del Banco: "Es la historia del "alter ego". Esa casa debe haber estado llena de deudas que nadie reclamaría."\
The sick old lady, struggling in her bed, whispered: "The house remembers those days, when people vanished in the darkness of night and children were stolen by the storms."

能量扰动学家听得够多了，于是她昏昏沉沉地睡去。巴比伦之骰在风中、小镇中，在所有的频率中反复回荡。\
The Paracausality Researcher had heard enough and drifted back to sleep again. There was only the rattling of the Die of Babylon echoing in her hollow cave.

La anciana enferma, luchando en su cama, susurró, "La casa recuerda esos días, cuando la gente desaparecía en la oscuridad de la noche y los niños eran robados por las tormentas." La Investigadora de Paracausalidad había oído suficiente y volvió a dormirse. Solo quedaba el traqueteo del Dado de Babilonia resonando en su cueva vacía.\
荒废的活动场地内，成千上万张纸条悬浮在空中，构成了一张模糊的巨大面庞。很难想象监狱中的囚犯们，是如何将这里改造成如今的模样的。\
La anciana enferma, luchando en su cama, susurró, "La casa recuerda esos días, cuando la gente desaparecía en la oscuridad de la noche y los niños eran robados por las tormentas." La Investigadora de Paracausalidad había oído suficiente y volvió a dormirse. Solo quedaba el traqueteo del Dado de Babilonia resonando en su cueva vacía.\
In a deteriorating activity hall, thousands of floating slips of paper form a blurred, colossal face. It is hard to imagine how the prisoners managed to transform this place into what it is now.

**加西亚**：我一直认为，加入一部分非理性的幻想元素能够完美推进这个主题，如今它已经做到了。\
**García**: I've always wanted to use the element of fantasy to better establish our theme. And I was right.

**加西亚**：令人着迷的舞台，恰如其分的时间，构成精妙的观展人群……\
**García**: Now the stage is captivating, the timing is perfect, and the audience is ideally placed.

**加西亚**：时至如今，我唯一能够审视的，也是唯一不可称之为完满的构成部分……只有身为创作者的自己。\
**García**: Only one imperfect element remains in the scene—the creator, who hasn't stepped away from his creation.

**加西亚**：不，至少我还有一件事可做……\
**García**: No, there's another thing.

监狱中的策展人站在自己的作品下苦思冥想，每英寸的误差都让人难以忍受。\
García, the curator of the exhibition, stands beneath his work, deep in thought, agonizing over every minute imperfection.

与此同时，一旁围观的诗社成员正窃窃私语着。\
His fellow poets whisper to one another.

**罗贝托**：考验你的时候到了。你能看出，今天的布置和昨天有什么不同吗？\
**Roberta**: Can you even tell any difference between today's setup and yesterday's?

**诗社囚犯Ⅰ**：这是一个冒犯的问题，罗贝托。\
**La Sociedad Member I**: Seriously, Roberta? That's a rude question!

**罗贝托**：所以，究竟有什么不一样？\
**Roberta**: Well, what's the difference, then?

**诗社囚犯Ⅰ**：我也不知道。但你不该用如此肤浅的眼光去衡量一件艺术品诞生的过程！\
**La Sociedad Member I**: Well, I can't see one either. But you should never judge art by how much it changes in a day! It's a creative process.

**诗社囚犯Ⅰ**：即使在世界尽头的监狱中，艺术也是不死的！我们应该竭尽所能地支持他！\
**La Sociedad Member I**: We might be standing at the edge of the world, but art has no boundaries! We have to show him our support.

**罗贝托**：唉……我就跟你说实话吧，他已经在这儿调整了三个月有余了。\
**Roberta**: Easy for you to say. He's been tinkering and tweaking for over three months.

**罗贝托**：虽然是理想家先生亲自将活动场地交给他做展览的，但要我说，理想家先生就是太相信他了。这儿马上就要变成垃圾场了！\
**Roberta**: Even if the Idealist himself entrusted him with this exhibition, he can still be wrong sometimes. This gallery is turning into a dump!

**？？？**：笼罩在这片土地上面容相似的幽灵太多了，加西亚。你会迷失在这些幻影中的。\
**???**: I'm seeing ghosts, all with the same faces, García. All too many. It's easy to get lost in them.

终于摆脱了迷宫的纠缠，诗社领袖带着数个崭新的面孔与狱卒，一同出现在展厅入口处。\
Having navigated through the labyrinth, the Idealist—the leader of La Sociedad—arrives at the exhibit's entrance, accompanied by several new faces and the jailer.

**加西亚**：理想家先生，您回来了。这些都是要加入诗社的新人吗？真是收获颇丰的一天。\
**García**: Idealist! You're back. Are these new recruits for La Sociedad? You must have had a very successful day!

**理想家**：午安，加西亚。今日的布展还顺利吗？\
**The Idealist**: It is good to see you, García. How has your vision progressed today?

**虚构集**：布展？难道说，这里是一个艺术展厅？！\
**Recoleta**: First a salon, and now an art gallery? Is this really a prison?

女孩震惊地看向面前的布展人。对方正向着诗社首领汇报自己的苦恼。\
Her shock is evident on her face, but her words are ignored as García begins to vent his frustrations.

**加西亚**：先生，如您所见，它在非理性的幻想元素上已经达到了我的追求……\
**García**: As you can see, I've strived to push the element of fantasy in my work so that it might reach perfection.

**加西亚**：但我仍然不明白，这张面孔为何总是与我所想象的有微妙的差异？\
**García**: But why doesn't it look like what I imagined?

**加西亚**：日复一日，它似乎时刻处于变化之中……难道是我又发病了吗？但我明明照着规则得到了药物，也按时服用了那些小圆片……\
**García**: It's like I'm trying to work on a shadow—some shapeless thing that morphs and shifts by the hour. Idealist, am I losing it again? I took my medicine as instructed.

**理想家**：那些药并不重要，加西亚。\
**The Idealist**: It was never the pills that blinded you, my dear García.

**理想家**：别让美好的事物因繁复而黯然失色，你的展览该如古老诗篇那般，拥有一种不被打扰的纯净韵律！\
**The Idealist**: You mustn't let tedious routine stifle what's truly alive. Remember, like those old poems, your exhibition must have a timeless rhythm that's never lost to the changing of minds.

加西亚感觉自己似乎领略了什么，但又抓不住那转瞬即逝的感觉。\
García holds out his hands as if grasping something fleeting but fails to hold onto it.

**加西亚**：请原谅我的愚钝。\
**García**: Sorry, maybe I'm just not getting it.

**理想家**：你有注视过那伟大日神的不灭光辉吗？尽管它日复一日地洒落于人间，但每日投影出的面孔却是无穷无尽的。\
**The Idealist**: Look up! There's your answer. Though the sun rises the same way every day, the multitudes of shadows it casts are ever-changing.

**理想家**：这不正是我们所追寻的亘古不变之物吗？\
**The Idealist**: Isn't that the only constant in life—change?

**理想家**：时间，呵！它不过是人类痴迷的一场浪漫的幻象。忘记所谓的视角吧，你只需要想象自己是一位游离于时间之外的旁观者。\
**The Idealist**: We foolishly pursue stability and constancy, but our very world denies it. Take a step back—take several—and see the truth for yourself, lest you too become lost among the shifting shadows.

**加西亚**：我想我明白您的意思了。一切都是因为日照的偏移……！\
**García**: I get it now! It's the changing light that makes the exhibits seem different from what I expected.

**加西亚**：随着季节变换，太阳偏移的微妙角度，造成了展品投影的差异……这正是这张面孔不停变幻的原因……\
**García**: I shouldn't waste my time on freezing things in one perfect moment. Instead, I need to embrace change as it comes.

**加西亚**：理想家先生……我不知道该如何答谢。眼下，我在这世间唯一需要做的，就是完成它……\
**García**: I don't know how to thank you! I won't let you down. I must complete this exhibition.

**加西亚**：完成我的作品，另一个我【alter ego】。\
**García**: Complete my "alter ego."

突然出现的名字，让一直旁听的青年作家瞪大了眼睛。\
The choice of word widens the writer's eyes.

**虚构集**：你刚刚说什么？另一个我……？\
**Recoleta**: Did you say "alter ego"?

**虚构集**：等等，这位先生，你是叫“加西亚”对吗？！\
**Recoleta**: And he called you García. Is that your name?

**虚构集**：加西亚先生，你是如何得知“另一个我”这个名字的？你是否有个笔名叫——\
**Recoleta**: García, where did you learn about this "alter ego"? Do you happen to write under the name—

但策展人已经走回展品之下，无心顾及来客的任何言语了。\
But the curator has already returned to his work, uninterested or oblivious to his visitors.

**理想家**：虚构集小姐，别太心急！你没看出来吗？时间与空间在他身上成为了重叠的波纹，外界的话语已经无法掀起涟漪了。\
**The Idealist**: Please, Recoleta! Give our artist some space. Can't you see? He's already returned to his own time and space. He can't hear a thing you say.

**罗贝托**：新来的朋友，我可以作证，在加西亚完成他的展览之前，都没可能听见你说的任何话语了。\
**Roberta**: He's right. García is deep in his own head now. He won't hear a thing until he's done with whatever he has to do.

**罗贝托**：每次他开始捣鼓那些破纸屑的时候，除非监狱塌了，他都不会挪开屁股半步。\
**Roberta**: Even if the floor were to collapse out under us, I think he would be left standing in the air without even noticing.

**虚构集**：好，好吧。\
**Recoleta**: Ah. Pardon me then.

女孩不甘心地后退了一步。\
She takes a step back out of respect.

**理想家**：虽然介绍得晚了些，但，无人能懂展厅欢迎诸位的到来。\
**The Idealist**: Alright. My dear guests! Please forgive my late introduction. Welcome to the Gallery of Bewilderment.

**维尔汀**：谢谢您的邀请，理想家先生。\
**Vertin**: Thank you for inviting me here, Mr. Idealist.

在到达展厅之后，调查员们的视线关注着每一位囚犯的动静。但遗憾的是，她们并没有找到德洛丝女士的身影。\
The Foundation's investigators have been carefully observing each prisoner's movements since they arrived. But unfortunately, there is no sign of Ms. Dores.

**理想家**：亲爱的客人们，你们一定很好奇美洲诗社究竟在这里做些什么。现在，让我来为诸位介绍一番：\
**The Idealist**: I imagine you're curious about what we do here, in the heart of La Sociedad de Poetas de las Américas.

**理想家**：我们计划在监狱中出版一本属于自己的《美洲之家》，一本科马拉的诗集！\
**The Idealist**: We're putting together a magazine—a collection of poems from Comala, our very own Casa de las Américas.

**虚构集**：我没听错吧，你说的是《美洲之家》……？！\
**Recoleta**: Casa de las Américas?!

理想家微笑地点点头。\
The Idealist nods with a smile.

**理想家**：这位流浪的牛仔，你相当识货。目前，诗社中所有的同僚都正在为了这个伟大的目标而忙碌。\
**The Idealist**: Exactly. Named after its great predecessor! You're a fine mind indeed! At this very moment, all our companions are working on it.

**理想家**：加西亚的艺术作品“另一个我”，正是为了记录这本诗集诞生的过程！\
**The Idealist**: García's exhibition, "Alter Ego," is centered around the birth of this magazine.

**理想家**：你可以在上面找到诗社所有成员的署名，还有他们所写下的思绪片段……\
**The Idealist**: And here, you can see the signatures from all the poets involved, along with a few words they've written for it.

**理想家**：这一切共同构成了一张复杂、变幻的面容，属于美洲诗社的面容。\
**The Idealist**: Reading it is like looking into the soul of our society.

**十四行诗**：诗社所有囚犯的署名吗……？\
**Sonetto**: All these signatures ...

第一助手走上前，观察着面前难以理解的“艺术品”。昏暗的光线下，那张巨大的面容静静俯视着房间内的所有人。\
Sonetto steps forward to examine the perplexing "artwork." In the dim lighting, the enormous face appears to be looming watchfully over the entire room.

一张漂浮的碎纸片引起了她的注意。\
A floating slip of paper catches her attention.

**十四行诗**：司辰，这上面写着德洛丝女士的笔名——兀尔德！\
**Sonetto**: Timekeeper, here! It's Dr. Dores's pseudonym—Urd!

**维尔汀**：德洛丝女士，她果然来过这里。\
**Vertin**: Then she was here.

第一助手小心翼翼地将那张纸片收好。\
Sonetto pockets the slip of paper dutifully.

**理想家**：是的，如你们所料。德洛丝是诗社的一员，她曾经是，将来是，永远都是。\
**The Idealist**: Precisely. She used to be one of us, and still is, if I may correct myself.

**理想家**：至于她如今在监狱的何处，你可以尽情地询问诗社的成员们！\
**The Idealist**: You can ask around here. Maybe some of our members know where she went.

**理想家**：我相信，美洲诗社的成员们都有一副热心肠。他们会极力促成这场感人的会面。\
**The Idealist**: Don't we all miss the familiar faces of old friends? I'm sure they'll do everything they can to help you find yours.

话音刚落，数名“热心肠”的囚犯都前来向理想家问好。\
As he finishes speaking, several enthusiastic prisoners come forward to greet the Idealist.

**诗社囚犯Ⅱ**：堂理想家，我撰写了一篇短篇小说《失重》，并让它就像失去重力的羊一般漂浮于意义之外！读者可以从任意一行开始，也可以按任何顺序解读情节！\
**La Sociedad Member II**: Mr. Idealist, I've finished my short story. It's called "Weightlessness." It drifts around the subject like a sheep floating in space! The readers can start anywhere in the story or read it in any order they like!

**诗社囚犯Ⅲ**：不如先看看我的《禁区》！凡是出现在禁区内的词汇，在该段落内全被剔除或替换成符号……我为读者带来了断断续续的阅读体验！\
**La Sociedad Member III**: And please take a look at my piece, "Off Limits!" Every word that has been forbidden is either erased or replaced with symbols. It's a one-of-a-kind jarring experience!

**诗社囚犯Ⅳ**：请您也过目我今日新写的部分——\
**La Sociedad Member IV**: And I've finished a new paragraph! Just wrote it today.

一名囚犯拖着数米长的稿纸，如同一个自我包裹的木乃伊挤入了人群中。\
A prisoner, wrapped in several meters of manuscript paper, like a strange sort of mummy, squeezes into the crowd.

**诗社囚犯Ⅳ**：噢，等会儿？这些都是诗社的新人吗？欢迎大家！\
**La Sociedad Member IV**: Oh! New faces! Welcome!

猝不及防地，他抬起手臂，平静地将手中的稿纸撕成了碎片。\
Without any warning, he calmly tears the manuscript to shreds.

纷纷扬扬的碎纸屑落下，好像一场古怪的礼花。\
The fluttering fragments fall like trailing sparks from a fireworks show.

唐突的“欢迎仪式”让新来者们愣在原地。而监狱的“原住民”们神情淡然，脸上浮现出一种见怪不怪的微笑。\
The abrupt "welcome ceremony" leaves the newcomers stunned, while the "natives" share knowing smiles.

**虚构集**：理想家先生，这是——？！\
**Recoleta**: Idealist! Did he just ...?

**理想家**：噢，这位是目前负责编写序章的同僚。\
**The Idealist**: This is the writer for the prologue of our magazine.

兴致勃勃的诗社首领全然误解了对方的提问。\
The leader of La Sociedad, either misunderstanding or evading the question, responds with enthusiasm.

**理想家**：诗集的序章包含一首两千行的长诗与八十六段不同语言版本的引子，用以保证所有描述的精确性。它将会分毫不差地代表诗社中所有人的每一秒——\
**The Idealist**: The prologue consists of a two-thousand-line poem and an introduction that is written in 86 languages to avoid misinterpretation. It represents every second we spend here.

**理想家**：一位新成员的到来意味着整个循环结构彻底地紊乱，每一个标点符号和字母都势必要挪动它的位置。\
**The Idealist**: Naturally, the arrival of new members disrupts its structure, and so we must begin again from scratch.

**虚构集**：他认为我们加入了诗社，所以就把先前编写的部分全部摧毁了吗？\
**Recoleta**: So he just tore it all up like that because he thought we were joining?

**虚构集**：请原谅我的唐突，但这是不是有点太拘泥于结构了？唔，也许我没资格说这话，我也忍不住在不断的重写中调整结构……\
**Recoleta**: With all due respect, isn't this a little excessive? Heaven knows I'm not one to judge. I've torn up plenty of writing for my novel.

**理想家**：别担心，这是一个艰巨的任务，但他完成得很好。\
**The Idealist**: Please pay it no mind. It may not be an easy task, but he's doing his part.

**理想家**：打破一切是很有意义的，我们的所作所为就是在不停地打破旧有的事物。\
**The Idealist**: Destruction is hard, but more necessary than you think. Without it, we'd all be stuck in a still and stagnant pond, with all the smells that entail.

**维尔汀**：如果是这样，这部诗集要什么时候才能完成？\
**Vertin**: This all sounds very complicated. When will your magazine be finished then?

**维尔汀**：失去重力的羊、断断续续的阅读体验和不断的重写……这些行为有什么必要性吗？\
**Vertin**: Forgive me, but I'm not sure what a floating sheep, a jarring reading experience, and all this constant rewriting are meant to express.

一直沉默的狱卒深呼了一口气，出言打断了这一切。\
The jailer, having remained silent, takes a deep breath and interrupts.

**狱卒**：我想你们已经发现了，科马拉监狱中囚犯的异于常人之处。\
**Jailer**: As I've said, Comala is unlike any other prison.

**维尔汀**：狱卒小姐，您的意思是——\
**Vertin**: Ms. Jailer, do you mean ...

**狱卒**：其实，在进入监狱的伊始，我已经给诸位讲解过科马拉监狱的建立理念。这里的囚犯，他们并不是单纯的文学家，也不是所谓的“诗人”。\
**Jailer**: This place also serves as a research center. And the prisoners here, for all they claim, are not just "poets."

**狱卒**：被送入科马拉监狱的神秘学家，他们都是患有严重精神分裂的嫌犯。\
**Jailer**: They are arcanist criminals, and each one of them has been diagnosed as mentally ill.

面对狱卒的指控，一旁的诗社首领好整以暇，这位精神病人中的“佼佼者”丝毫不显慌张。\
The leader of La Sociedad remains composed, like an island in a rough sea,

他要么是完全没疯，要么是疯得彻底。\
leaving the onlookers to question whether he is entirely mad or the sanest of them all.

**理想家**：狱卒小姐，也许你说得不错，但究竟由谁来定义这“疯癫”？是狱卒、狱医、典狱长，还是来自外面的人？\
**The Idealist**: You're quite right, Jailer. But let's not forget that mental illness is merely a deviation from the norm. And who decides the norm? You? The Physician? Or the ones outside these walls?

**理想家**：我们在社会的规训下被遣往此地，在囚禁的惩罚中丧失身份。请你不要干扰诗社的运作，这是我们一早就定好的约定！\
**The Idealist**: We've been exiled here by the standards of our time, deprived of our roles in the outside world. So please, as we agreed before, I ask you not to interfere with the affairs of La Sociedad!

**狱卒**：理想家，她们是前来科马拉拜访的基金会客人，并不是诗社的成员。\
**Jailer**: These people are visitors, not your new recruits.

**理想家**：但如果她们想加入诗社呢？\
**The Idealist**: But should we not hear their thoughts first?

理想家迫切地转向来访者们。\
The Idealist turns toward the visitors with an urgent plea.

**理想家**：诸位，加入诗社，加入我们对抗权力视线的实验吧，趁现在，一切还来得及！在权力的视线之下，只有文学是我们最后能苟且的所在。\
**The Idealist**: My friends! No one escapes the Eye of Power. We must resist. Stand with us. Pick up your pen and take poetry as your shield before it is too late!

**虚构集**：理想家先生，我非常敬佩诗社的一切，但我来这里……还有更重要的任务。\
**Recoleta**: Idealist, I admire your fight. But I came here with a different goal.

陷入亢奋的诗社首领无视了她的婉拒。\
The leader of La Sociedad, caught in his fervor, ignores her words and carries on.

**理想家**：还记得那句话吗？“我们是最后一代拥有神话的拉丁美洲作家。”\
**The Idealist**: "We're the last true owners of an old legend, words now only remembered as myth."

**理想家**：在文学这条道路的最终，我必能寻找到，超越一切的方式……\
**The Idealist**: We must stay on the path of literature until I find that transcendental solution ...

**理想家**：当那一天到来的时候，我就能找到一门包罗万象、又无比精确的语言，不需要模糊我任何的理解，去将那道无尽的、悲伤蜿蜒的诗歌完成。\
**The Idealist**: To invent an idiom that is generic, all-encompassing, yet precise. My poem will be written in this language, leaving no room for doubt or misinterpretation!

**理想家**：试想一下，如果一个人能记住所有的事情，那么只要穷尽所有时间和物质，就能获得自己想要的答案。这是一件多么幸运的事情！\
**The Idealist**: How blessed is a man with infallible memory! He holds the finer details of each object within him, more vivid than anyone else. In the end, he'll have all the answers, if time allows him!
