他的面上呈现出一种梦幻的表情，仿佛变了一个人似的。可惜理想注定是要被打断的，这一次也不例外。\
A dream-like expression crosses his face. It briefly seems as if he has become an entirely different person. But his vision is soon interrupted.

**诗社囚犯Ⅳ**：甜美的……坦克……！嚎叫的……的姐姐……！钻石歌曲……不对，沙漠……！\
**La Sociedad Member IV**: Sweet tank! Sister ... howls! Hermaphrodite—Tango ...!

**诗社囚犯Ⅳ**：我们所在的城市……就是疯人院……！\
**La Sociedad Member IV**: They put the whole city ... in the nuthouse!

**十四行诗**：司辰，那是……？！\
**Sonetto**: Timekeeper, look over there!

**维尔汀**：这是刚刚那位撕碎自己稿纸的囚犯？\
**Vertin**: Isn't that the prologue writer?!

**十四行诗**：他的样子不太对劲……司辰，请小心！\
**Sonetto**: There's something off about him. Please, Timekeeper, stay away from him!

**理想家**：发生了什么？\
**The Idealist**: What's happening?

**罗贝托**：理想家先生，糟糕了！巴勃鲁又发病了！\
**Roberta**: Idealist! Pablo is having another episode!

**诗社囚犯Ⅳ**：多重……我们！你让现实恶心！\
**La Sociedad Member IV**: Multiples of ... us! You make reality sick!

电光火石间，神秘术的辉光已经亮起，狱卒也闪身至众人身前。\
A flash of arcane energy flares up, and the jailer steps into the crowd reactively.

**狱卒**：各位，请协助我制服他。\
**Jailer**: I could use your help, ladies!

终于，陷入癫狂的囚犯被众人制服，他四肢抽搐地倒在展厅的中央。\
The frenzied prisoner is subdued. He lies convulsing in the center of the exhibit hall.

**罗贝托**：唉，可怜的巴勃鲁……让我先扶着他躺下。\
**Roberta**: Poor soul. I'll bring him to bed.

**罗贝托**：真是虚惊一场，没想到你们这些新人除了写东西之外，还有这么两下子！\
**Roberta**: Well done, ladies. Aren't you full of surprises!

**狱卒**：这究竟是怎么一回事？\
**Jailer**: What was all that?

**维尔汀**：在刚刚，这位囚犯陷入了神秘术暴走的状态。他所念出的诗句，都成为了释放神秘术的载体。\
**Vertin**: It seems he had a mental breakdown and lost control of his arcane skill. It appears that every line he recited carried unbridled power.

**十四行诗**：只有满足苛刻条件的诗句，才能用于释放神秘术，这是可遇不可求的。\
**Sonetto**: Usually, only specific lines can channel arcane energy. You can't just force the power into words or craft a poem to serve your purpose.

**十四行诗**：我想，巴勃鲁先生只是能一眼辨认出那些最适合释放神秘术的诗句，这却恰恰导致了神秘术的暴走……\
**Sonetto**: Pablo must have a rare gift for identifying empowered lines. When he recited them all aloud, they overwhelmed him.

**罗贝托**：是的，他是个情感的天才，就像纯粹而野性的兰波，终日被澎湃的情感淹没。\
**Roberta**: That's right. He's a genius who rides the tides of emotion, just like Arthur Rimbaud.

**罗贝托**：平日里，我们都会小心地控制他，不让他将所写的内容念出来。\
**Roberta**: We always keep a close eye on him to make sure he doesn't recite anything while reading or writing.

罗贝托尴尬地瞧了一眼严阵以待的狱卒，以及一旁的访客。\
Roberta trades glances between the tense jailer and her visitors.

**罗贝托**：但凡事终究有意外——\
**Roberta**: But, sometimes, things slip through.

**理想家**：希望你们能理解，对一位诗人来说，终生不能读诗，这是多么残酷的惩罚。\
**The Idealist**: You must understand how difficult it is for a poet to never taste the words on his own lips.

**狱卒**：看起来他并不是第一次发病了，而你们也完全知晓这个情况。\
**Jailer**: So, then this isn't the first time. And you're all fully aware of it.

**狱卒**：理想家，你们在这里藏匿了一个严重的癫痫病人吗？\
**Jailer**: Do I understand you right? Did you just admit that you've been hiding an inmate with a dangerous condition from us?

**狱卒**：按照《科马拉实验性全景监狱安全管理条约》，他必须马上送往狱医处接受治疗。\
**Jailer**: According to the Safety Regulations for the Panopticon of Comala, he must be sent to the Physician for immediate treatment.

狱卒的话让在场所有囚犯都面色一变。\
The jailer's command causes a dramatic shift in the room.

**罗贝托**：等一下……狱卒小姐！我们能解释！\
**Roberta**: No, no! Wait, we can explain!

**罗贝托**：我想是新人的到来让他太兴奋了，一时间忘了要遵守约定！或者说，是，是……\
**Roberta**: He's doing fine! We know how to help him. This was just an accident. We-We got distracted by the new members.

**理想家**：我们不能将他交给狱医。\
**The Idealist**: We won't be handing him over to the Physician.

**理想家**：没有任何一位作家愿意把藏着无限灵感与巧思的大脑区域交由一位冷漠而不可沟通的暴徒——即使是彻头彻尾的唯心主义作家。\
**The Idealist**: No true writer would allow their mind—the most sacred palace of their thoughts—to be opened up to that cold-hearted, ignorant butcher. Even one who believes their inspiration flows from a source beyond the mere substance of a brain would refuse it!

**狱卒**：……\
**Jailer**: ...

狱卒皱起了眉头，亦取出了随身的武器。无形的空气被拉成了紧绷的细线。\
The jailer furrows her brows and pulls out her weapon. The air tightens into an invisible thread.

## 9TH-07 激情与谵妄 / Passion and Delirium

**狱卒**：你们已经严重违反了规定。我需要和狱医重新评定你们的治疗方案。\
**Jailer**: This is a serious violation of the rules. I'll have to report this to the Physician, and all of your treatments will need to be reassessed.

**狱卒**：在评估完成之前，请“诗社”的诸位回到自己的房间。接下来的一段时间内，所有人的活动范围将会受到限制。\
**Jailer**: Until a new treatment plan is in place, all members of La Sociedad are confined to their cells without any of their usual privileges.

狱卒加重了“诗社”的咬字，这让四周的囚犯陷入了喧哗。\
The jailer heavily emphasizes "La Sociedad," triggering a commotion among the prisoners.

**诗社囚犯Ⅱ**：这，这和当初说好的不一样……！\
**La Sociedad Member II**: This is not what we agreed to!

**诗社囚犯Ⅲ**：你们承诺过不会干涉诗社的一切的！\
**La Sociedad Member III**: You gave us your word! Affairs within La Sociedad were not to be disturbed!

**罗贝托**：请你不要这样做，狱卒小姐！\
**Roberta**: Please don't do this!

**罗贝托**：不要送走我们的同伴，让他们消失在未知的命运之中，这太残忍了。\
**Roberta**: Please, he doesn't deserve this. No one does! We don't wanna lose our friend.

方才发病的囚犯亦挣扎着爬起身。\
The previously convulsing prisoner struggles to his feet.

**诗社囚犯Ⅳ**：狱卒小姐，拜托了……我会好好吃药、好好治病……\
**La Sociedad Member IV**: Please, madam! I swear it won't happen again. I'll take the medicine on time as instructed.

**诗社囚犯Ⅳ**：我不会影响到、别的囚犯……\
**La Sociedad Member IV**: I promise I won't hurt anyone.

**狱卒**：我很抱歉，巴勃鲁。但规定就是……规定。\
**Jailer**: I'm sorry, Mr. Pablo, but rules are rules.

**理想家**：狱卒小姐，我想请问你一件事——\
**The Idealist**: Before you take this poor man from his friends, may I ask you something?

**理想家**：你是否知晓，所有那些被送往狱医处的囚犯，他们最终去了哪里？\
**The Idealist**: Do you know where these inmates go after they see the Physician?

**狱卒**：……\
**Jailer**: ...

**狱卒**：我并没有再见过他们。这不是我负责的范畴……\
**Jailer**: My duty is to keep order here. What happens beyond these walls is not my concern.

**狱卒**：在接受狱医梅林先生的治疗后，他们的身心状态也许已经逐渐恢复，并已经重新融入社会，回归正常生活。\
**Jailer**: Perhaps they've recovered from the Physician's treatment and were returned to society.

狱卒的面色有所松动。\
The jailer's expression relaxes.

**理想家**：是的，所有被送去“治疗”的人，最终都从监狱里面消失了。他们再也没有在科马拉里出现过。\
**The Idealist**: Within these walls, the only truth we know is this: no one returns from the clinic of the Physician of Comala.

**理想家**：但你能肯定地告诉我，狱卒小姐，这种消失，真的是痊愈吗？\
**The Idealist**: Are you certain this "treatment" they received is really a cure?

**罗贝托**：巴勃鲁他……只是一个有诗人天赋的神秘学家。\
**Roberta**: Pablo is harmless. He-He's just a writer who has a talent for finding words and poems. That's all.

**罗贝托**：狱卒小姐，求您网开一面！我们会让出自己的药品份额，好好看管他。\
**Roberta**: Please, let him stay. We'll look after him. He can have our share of the medicine. We'll keep him in check.

**狱卒**：可是……这，这并不符合科马拉的规定。\
**Jailer**: But this doesn't conform to our regulations.

**？？？**：你太狂妄了，理想家。\
**???**: Still as arrogant as ever, Idealist.

**？？？**：你的决定会害了我们所有人。\
**???**: One day, you'll get us all killed.

一名陌生的囚犯从展厅入口走出。随着来人的出现，狱卒肉眼可见地松了口气。\
A stranger enters the exhibition hall. As she arrives, the jailer exhales with relief.

**狱卒**：是你，奥克塔维奥。\
**Jailer**: Ah, it's you. I'm glad to see you here.

**维尔汀**：这位小姐是？\
**Vertin**: Who is that?

**狱卒**：奥克塔维奥在许多方面帮到了我们，她理应是囚犯们的模范对象。\
**Jailer**: That's Octavia, one of our model inmates. She's been a great help in the past.

**狱卒**：事实上，如果你们需要了解囚犯的文学生活，我更建议诸位与她而非理想家接触。\
**Jailer**: If you're interested in prison literature, I'd suggest talking to her instead of the Idealist.

**维尔汀**：所以，奥克塔维奥小姐也是一位作家。\
**Vertin**: So, she's a writer, too.

**虚构集**：真有意思，又是一个生面孔！我还以为科马拉中的所有作家都在诗社里了。\
**Recoleta**: Who would've thought! This place has got writers coming out of the woodwork!

**虚构集**：我本来以为在监狱中寻找一位作家并不是一件难事。\
**Recoleta**: I thought it would be easy to find my writer friend in a prison. But what are the odds that I'd break into a place absolutely lousy with them?

**狱卒**：她的确是诗社的成员，只是不再参与这种无聊的集会了——她成立了所谓另一派的文学派系，并且拉拢了不少囚犯过去。\
**Jailer**: She used to be in their gatherings, until she got tired of their nonsense and started her own faction.

新生的派系领袖出场，令理想家不可察觉地啧舌。\
The new arrival brings out a change in the Idealist. He clicks his tongue imperceptibly.

**理想家**：奥克塔维奥，你来这儿干什么？属于族长、鬼魂和种植园故事的年代已经过去了，现在是本能现实主义掌控着拉丁美洲！\
**The Idealist**: What are you doing here, Octavia? Haven't you heard? The era of chieftains, ghosts, and plantation stories is over. Visceral realism is the future!

**奥克塔维奥**：哼，你还真是一如既往地热衷于装腔作势。你那不知所云的“本能现实主义”，帮你写完那首长诗了吗？\
**Octavia**: Ha. And has this brilliant "visceral realism" helped you finish any of these poems?

**奥克塔维奥**：算了……我不想跟你胡扯，也对反驳你的创作理念没有兴趣。\
**Octavia**: What a waste of time. I'm not interested in your movement or arguing with you.

**奥克塔维奥**：方才我听到这儿的喧闹声，然后不得不目睹了你对巴勃鲁所做的狂妄行为。\
**Octavia**: I just walked by and happened to witness another episode of your brutal arrogance.

**奥克塔维奥**：我郑重地警告你，理想家，我绝不允许以往的悲剧再发生一次。\
**Octavia**: And I'm not about to just stand aside and watch you repeat your mistakes!

**奥克塔维奥**：我要把巴勃鲁送到狱医先生那儿去。狱卒小姐，请帮助我！\
**Octavia**: I'm taking Pablo to the Physician. Care to lend a hand, Ms. Jailer?

**理想家**：这完全打破了我们之前河水不犯井水的约定。\
**The Idealist**: We agreed to mind our own business. Are you breaking our agreement?

**理想家**：无论是你还是狱医，都别想从美洲诗社中抹去长诗的任何一个词汇！\
**The Idealist**: No one, no one will be allowed to erase a word from our poems!

**狱卒**：奥克塔维奥，理想家，你们都冷静一些！\
**Jailer**: Stand down, both of you!

但陷入激烈争辩的二人，根本无心顾及来自狱卒的警告。\
Their heated debate continues without any concern for the jailer's warning.

**奥克塔维奥**：自始至终，你从没有听过我或其他人的任何一句劝诫。可笑的是，你根本不知道之后会发生什么。\
**Octavia**: You've never listened. I pity your followers—to be led by such a reckless megalomaniac! Do you even think about the consequences of your actions?

**奥克塔维奥**：我们好不容易在监视中获得了谈论文学的自由，而你的狂妄将令一切都归于废墟。\
**Octavia**: We fought hard to earn the freedom to discuss literature under their watch. Your impulsive ego threatens to destroy everything we've built here.

**理想家**：哈哈，将那些多余的说辞省去吧，奥克塔维奥。什么时候谈论文学的自由需要靠外界来赋予了？\
**The Idealist**: Spare me the lecture, Octavia. We don't need permission to do as we please.

**理想家**：你不过是想让我们也像你一样，屈服于监视背后的权力罢了。\
**The Idealist**: You're just another puppet of power, kneeling to the eyes behind those glass walls.

**理想家**：真正的权力，会让你们以为这是你们自己的信念：做个好人，好好遵守规矩，写一点儿从不出格的魔幻现实主义……\
**The Idealist**: They have trained you to believe it was your own decision: to be good and conform. Who could've done a better job?

**理想家**：真是悲哀，你已经完全被来自瞭望塔的视线驯化了！文学向来不是规规矩矩地坐在公寓里听着古典音乐就能完成的事情。\
**The Idealist**: When I look at you, all I see is a sheep, docile and obedient, just the way the tower wants! What kind of work could someone like you create? Literature isn't defended by those lounging in cozy rooms, scribbling to soothing music.

**奥克塔维奥**：你……你从来没有透过镜子看到自己的丑陋姿态，理想家！你简直是一头拒斥一切形态威权的、离经叛道的、可悲的怪物！\
**Octavia**: Have you looked in a mirror, Idealist? You've become a pathetic, windmill-tilting fool, a monster tearing down everything around you!

**理想家**：呵！在长期被圈养、被看管的宠物那丁点儿大的脑袋里，当然无法想象猛兽的存在，也无法想象猛兽的缺席。\
**The Idealist**: A beast of prey, you mean? Naturally, a sheep would be appalled by the mere thought of such a creature.

**理想家**：你们先是将表现主义与意象主义那盘转缠绕的根系用手术刀从中切开，然后又将老虎与危险的武器混为一谈！\
**The Idealist**: A fearful sheep caught in a vine, confusing the blade that would set it free with the jaws of a tiger!

**奥克塔维奥**：你就这么喜欢玩文字游戏吗？在文学这座孤独的迷宫中，想要对民族性进行剖析，你就必须得先知道什么是正确的，什么是现实的。\
**Octavia**: Such a master of metaphor! But I beg you—learn to distinguish right from wrong, fantasy from reality. Only then can you truly lead our people toward what's right.

**理想家**：你们的脑袋里只能装得下一种标准——那就是“正确”！多么无趣的词汇！\
**The Idealist**: "Distinguish right from wrong." Don't make me laugh. Is that the limit of your vision?

**奥克塔维奥**：你……你这个……\
**Octavia**: You ... You ...

情绪激动的诗社首领跳至一旁的长凳上，在人群中做出演讲的姿势。\
The impassioned leader jumps onto a nearby bench, striking a dramatic pose before the crowd.

他举起手，振臂高呼起来。\
He raises his arms and launches into a speech.

**理想家**：朋友们，我的同胞们！你们都应该知道——！\
**The Idealist**: Companions! Friends! Listen to me!

**理想家**：除了监狱，这个世界上再也没有文学的归处——\
**The Idealist**: There is no truer home to literature than a prison—

一声枪响终结了理想家慷慨激昂的陈述。\
A blast of deafening sound and all words fall from the air.

诗社首领的表情凝固了，他低头看向自己胸前的洞口。\
The Idealist's expression freezes. His eyes search down from a frozen face to a dark red hole in his chest.

而如今，那儿正慢慢渗出代表不祥的血色。\
An ominous shade of crimson seeps out.

**奥克塔维奥**：噢……！不！\
**Octavia**: No! NO!

陷入惊骇的神秘学家倒退一步，失声尖叫起来。\
The horrified arcanist stumbles back, screaming.

**狱卒**：是谁？！在场所有人，双手抱头蹲下！\
**Jailer**: Who did this?! Hands behind your head and drop to your knees, all of you, now!

**狱卒**：这是最后一次警告！！\
**Jailer**: This is your last warning!!

然而囚犯们对于狱卒的最后通牒毫无反应。他们一齐看着理想家，面容呆滞。\
The prisoners show no reaction to the jailer's final ultimatum. They stare at the Idealist, unmoving.

**罗贝托**：理想家先生，您、您的胸口……在冒血……\
**Roberta**: Idealist, you-you're bleeding. It's in your chest.

对于自身生命的流逝，理想家似乎并不感到惊讶。他只是看向了虚构集的方向。\
As his life drains away, the Idealist appears unsurprised. He simply turns his gaze toward Recoleta.

**理想家**：你要……\
**The Idealist**: You must ...

**虚构集**：理想家先生，你……？！\
**Recoleta**: Yes, Idealist?

未竟的话语随着监狱的剧烈震动消失了。\
Unfinished words dissolve into silence as the prison itself begins to tremble.

整座展厅在震动中扭曲起来，四周呈现出难以理解的变化，仿佛一切事物都在溶解，自由地生长、变幻。\
The entire exhibition hall twists and contorts, its surroundings warping beyond comprehension, as if dissolving and expanding freely.

**虚构集**：发生了什么事……！\
**Recoleta**: What's going on?

寂静的展厅内，时间仿佛永恒地凝固。直到第一个人，说了第一句话。\
The hall is still. Time seems frozen in place, until someone utters the first words.

**奥克塔维奥**：他……他中弹了？我的天呐……我甚至都没听清是哪个方向传来的枪声！\
**Octavia**: Was he shot? Where did the bullet come from?

**奥克塔维奥**：狱卒小姐，以及那边的几位看起来有自保能力的访客们，快帮我一起把这家伙抬到狱医那儿……\
**Octavia**: Ms. Jailer, and you ladies over there, come give me a hand! We need to get him to the Physician!

第一句话，点燃了第一根引线。\
Her words ignite the first spark.

**诗社囚犯Ⅱ**：是你，奥克塔维奥？是你的恼羞成怒，令你用话语的子弹击穿一位诗人为理想而鼓动的心脏？\
**La Sociedad Member II**: Did you do this, Octavia? You couldn't face the burning truth of his words, so you pierced his very heart instead, just as it was blazing with the fire of justice!

**诗社囚犯Ⅱ**：还是你，狱卒？是你的权力意志，令你竟不惜用官僚的齿轮将不朽的诗篇压成粉末，而浑然不为所动？\
**La Sociedad Member II**: Or was it you, Jailer? Did you intend to crush the voice of poetry beneath your wheel of power?

**诗社囚犯Ⅱ**：一定是你们……一定是你们这帮披着人皮的魔鬼……\
**La Sociedad Member II**: It has to be one of you. Devils in disguise! Beasts in human skin!

**奥克塔维奥**：你们在说什么？！我根本就没有反应过来发生了什么事情！\
**Octavia**: Can't you see? I had nothing to do with this. I'm as innocent as any of you.

**奥克塔维奥**：天呐……我一直以来都在致力于维护这里的秩序，挽救大家的生命……现在，你竟然怀疑我是杀人凶手？\
**Octavia**: I've been trying to keep order here, to protect everyone. And now you blame me?

**诗社囚犯Ⅲ**：不，就是她，就是奥克塔维奥！我分明听到理想家先生向我们传递的隐喻，他说她“将老虎与危险的武器混为一谈”！\
**La Sociedad Member III**: Don't listen to her! The Idealist made it very clear. She's trying to get us punished for her own gain!

**诗社囚犯Ⅲ**：奥克塔维奥，你杀害了理想家先生！\
**La Sociedad Member III**: You're a murderer, Octavia!

囚犯们的怒气一触即发。\
The prisoners' fury erupts.

混乱之中，十四行诗匆忙挡下了一道偏离方向的神秘术。\
In the chaos, Sonetto blocks an arcane skill that pierces the air.

**奥克塔维奥**：你们都疯了……这完全是无理的指控，我说了，不是我动的手！\
**Octavia**: This is mad. You're accusing me without proof. It wasn't me.

**狱卒**：这里的情况已经逐渐失控了……我建议诸位客人先离开这里。\
**Jailer**: This is getting out of hand. I suggest you ladies leave now.

**虚构集**：等一下，可是……\
**Recoleta**: No, wait.

**虚构集**：这太突然了，理想家先生，他到底怎么样了？他还好吗？！\
**Recoleta**: It all happened too fast. What happened to the Idealist? Is he alright?

**虚构集**：我，我还没有来得及找到阿莱夫……\
**Recoleta**: I ... I didn't even get a chance to ask about Aleph.

人群的潮涌中，生与死的界限早已模糊不堪。\
As the tide of people surges around them, the line between life and death blurs beyond recognition.

**十四行诗**：我认同狱卒小姐的建议。\
**Sonetto**: I agree with the jailer.

**十四行诗**：司辰，虚构集小姐，安全起见，我们先离开此地吧。\
**Sonetto**: Timekeeper, Ms. Recoleta, let's get out of here.

在激烈的冲突之中，一切都显得不再重要。\
The violent conflict rages on, and everything else becomes meaningless.

时间如一场痴迷的幻象，无人知晓它流逝的速度。\
The illusion of time dissolves, its flow unknown.

受到花园的影响，陷入混乱的囚犯们露出了谵妄的神色，就像一首每个部分都不可解读的紊乱长诗。\
Under the garden's influence, the frenzy of prisoners begins to resemble an unreadable, chaotic epic.

就在此时，一个看不清面庞的人影靠近了，但没有人在乎。\
At this moment, an unidentifiable figure enters their midst, though no one takes notice.

来者打量着理想家毫无动静的尸体。\
The newcomer scrutinizes the motionless corpse.

**？？？**：很好，他的生命体征完全消失了，我再也不会被这个聒噪的家伙打扰了。\
**???**: His vitals are gone. At last, some peace and quiet.

**？？？**：对于一个谎话连篇的、可耻的盗窃者来说，最好的下场就是如此。\
**???**: Well. For a liar and a thief like him, there's hardly a better end than this.

他从理想家的外套口袋中取出一颗骰子。\
He reaches into the Idealist's coat pocket and pulls out a die.

一个于烟雾中隐约可见纹理的艺术品，一类仿佛不应存在于现世的象征物，一颗在全景视角中已知具有二十个面的骰子。\
It is an artifact marked by patterns veiled in smoke, an object seemingly not meant to exist in this world, a twenty-sided die known only through an omniscient perspective.

而现在，它已经被糟糕透顶的黑色所污染了。\
And now, it is stained in an utterly corrupted blackness.

**？？？**：骰子果然在你这里。\
**???**: Heh. Just as I thought. You had it all along.

## 9TH-08 蛛丝网 / The Spider's Web

**狱卒**：对于方才的事件，我谨代表科马拉监狱向各位致以歉意。\
**Jailer**: Ladies, I must apologize for what happened back there.

**狱卒**：虽然听起来很像是辩解，但从我就职以来，几乎未曾发生过如此大规模的暴乱。我必须向狱医先生汇报此事。\
**Jailer**: We were caught off guard. There has never been a commotion of that scale before. I must report this to the Physician.

**维尔汀**：没关系的，狱卒小姐，我们并没有人遭到袭击或受伤。\
**Vertin**: Don't worry, Ms. Jailer. We made it out in one piece.

**狱卒**：感谢理解。虽然我很想立刻护送各位离开监狱，但恐怕有些困难。在这个时间，乌斯怀亚的交通基本停运了，外面的道路还有积雪……\
**Jailer**: Thank you for your understanding. Ordinarily, I would arrange to escort you to a safer location, but I'm afraid at this hour, you'll have missed the last train. And the roads are icy at night.

闻言，虚构集连忙朝一旁的同行者们挤了挤眼睛。\
Hearing this, Recoleta exchanges a quick but meaningful expression with her companions.

**虚构集**：嘿，嘿！维尔汀，我们不能现在就离开——\
**Recoleta**: Psst, Vertin. We can't leave like this.

**维尔汀**：是的，我们还有一些基金会的重要任务没有完成。\
**Vertin**: We appreciate your kind consideration, Ms. Jailer, but we still have some unfinished business here.

**狱卒**：……好吧。如果诸位不嫌弃的话，我会在安全的区域安排干净的房间以供休息。\
**Jailer**: I see. I'll arrange a clean room in a safer section for you.

**狱卒**：我保证，科马拉监狱会对诸位的安全负责。\
**Jailer**: We'll do our best to ensure your safety tonight.

夜深了，女孩们围在一处，打量着这个陌生的居所。\
Night falls as the girls huddle together, scrutinizing their unfamiliar surroundings.

**十四行诗**：一个监狱里的房间。\
**Sonetto**: They actually found us a spare room.

**虚构集**：一个破败而井然、静谧而忧伤的，监狱里的房间。\
**Recoleta**: Bleak, quiet, and somber. It's a cell like all the others.

**维尔汀**：别担心，这并不是我们第一次在坐牢了。\
**Vertin**: Don't worry. This isn't the first time we've ended up on the wrong side of the bars.

**十四行诗**：司辰，这只是狱卒小姐给我们提供的休息房间。我不认为我们在坐牢……\
**Sonetto**: At least this time we're just here for the night, not a full sentence.

第一助手发出细如蚊蚋的反驳声。\
Sonetto lets out a whisper-thin protest.

**维尔汀**：这个牢房和我先前见过的都不一样。\
**Vertin**: Though, this cell is quite different from the ones we've been in before.

**虚构集**：不仅仅是这个牢房。这个监狱中的一切，都和外面的不一样。\
**Recoleta**: Not just this cell. The whole prison is unlike anything I've seen.

**虚构集**：那些来自诗社的囚犯，他们并不是在过家家或聊以解闷。那些讨论与实验，是真正跟文学的处境相关的。\
**Recoleta**: And this society they've been running here isn't some mere pastime. They're having real discussions about meaningful topics, even though the rest of the world has been cut off from them.

**十四行诗**：但这里仍然是一个神秘学家监狱，一个充满着冲突与暴力的地方。我认为，你太轻视这一切了。\
**Sonetto**: But we're still in an arcanist prison, a place where conflicts and violence can erupt at any moment. Let's not forget that.

**十四行诗**：狱卒小姐一早就警告过我们，这些囚犯都是危险的精神分裂患者。\
**Sonetto**: Ms. Jailer warned us from the start. These prisoners are mentally unstable and potentially dangerous.

**十四行诗**：虚构集小姐，我想……你并没有意识到那些真实存在的危险，就像方才一样。\
**Sonetto**: Ms. Recoleta, with all due respect, we can't afford to see this place through rose-colored glasses. We'd be overlooking the risks, as we did earlier.

**虚构集**：我当然意识到了危险。一个作家必须得先懂得观察现实，才能精准地反映在笔下。\
**Recoleta**: And with all due respect, Sonetto, we didn't overlook any danger. At least I didn't. A writer must be observant if she is to accurately reflect the world in her writing.

**十四行诗**：但是……\
**Sonetto**: But you—

**维尔汀**：我们抱有各自的目的，而它们尚未达成。\
**Vertin**: We came here with different goals, and still, none of them have been accomplished.

**维尔汀**：我想，眼下争执并不能帮我们达成目的。\
**Vertin**: I suggest we focus on our respective missions instead of fighting with one another.

**十四行诗**：……对不起，司辰，虚构集小姐。\
**Sonetto**: Apologies, Timekeeper. Ms. Recoleta, I take back everything I said.

**虚构集**：我也很抱歉，也许我有时候是太冲动了一些……我能理解，你只是非常担忧同伴的安危。\
**Recoleta**: Don't apologize, Sonetto. I'm at fault, too. Sometimes I forget that words can be as sharp as swords. You were only thinking about our safety. I shouldn't have been so rude.

**虚构集**：我很敬佩你刚才在冲突时刻挺身而出的表现！我愿意将它写成一首诗赠予你，来赞颂你们如钻石一般璀璨的友谊，只需要等我完稿小说即可。\
**Recoleta**: I actually really admire how you fought back there! If you'd allow me, I'd like to write a poem for you, once my novel's finished.

**十四行诗**：唔……？！\
**Sonetto**: Ah ...

**维尔汀**：请不要这样做，虚构集小姐。\
**Vertin**: That's terribly kind of you. But honestly, I think we've had enough poetry today to last a lifetime.

**虚构集**：但刚刚……理想家先生，他究竟发生了什么事了？\
**Recoleta**: Let me know if you change your mind. By the way, did either of you see what happened to the Idealist?

提及不久前的那场冲突，这位一向以超乎常人的执着示人的少女，罕见地陷入了迟疑之中。\
Recalling their recent conflict, the indomitable girl finally hesitates.

**维尔汀**：在骚动平息之后，狱卒小姐回去无人能懂展厅查看了情况。\
**Vertin**: The jailer told me she went back to the gallery once everything calmed down.

**维尔汀**：她说，她发现一件诡异的事情。那里已经什么都没有了。没有弹壳，没有血迹，连理想家先生都消失了。\
**Vertin**: She found nothing: no blood, no shell cases, not even a trace of the Idealist.

**十四行诗**：司辰，现在可不是讲鬼故事的时候。\
**Sonetto**: Timekeeper, now's really not the time for ghost stories.

**虚构集**：维尔汀，所以你的意思是，理想家先生的伤势并不严重，自己设法逃走了是吗？！\
**Recoleta**: Do you mean that maybe the Idealist somehow managed to get out of there on his own?

**虚构集**：不对，也可能是有囚犯带走了他，他并没有死亡……\
**Recoleta**: Or perhaps someone else helped him.

**维尔汀**：理想家先生与狱卒小姐先前都提及过，发病的囚犯会被送往狱医处治疗。\
**Vertin**: Well, according to the Idealist and our jailer, any inmates who are unwell will be taken to the Physician.

**维尔汀**：也许在混乱之中，有囚犯将其送走了。\
**Vertin**: It's possible someone brought him there while everyone else was shouting and running about.

**虚构集**：谢天谢地，那真是太好了！这个转折来得过于迅猛了，他的退场不应该是如此悄无声息的。\
**Recoleta**: You're right. It could be that he's with the Physician right now. I'm relieved! That was a sudden plot twist, but a visionary of his magnitude doesn't deserve to die in silence like that.

**维尔汀**：事实上，那声枪响还挺大的。\
**Vertin**: To be fair, the gunshot was quite loud, as was the ensuing commotion.

**虚构集**：……\
**Recoleta**: ...

**虚构集**：……我的意思是，在这种时候让关键人物悄无声息地退场，读者是会写信到出版社抗议的！\
**Recoleta**: Nonetheless, he couldn't have just died like that! I mean, the readers would riot if a writer were to kill off a character so abruptly!

**虚构集**：所以他一定还活着，对吗？！\
**Recoleta**: But, you believe he's still alive, too. Am I right?

她知道那些言辞只是掩饰。她迫切需要一个答案，一个现实的、肯定的答案。\
She knows her words are merely a cover. She needs an answer—a real, undeniable answer.

**维尔汀**：我们一定能弄清楚这一切的。事实上，我们并非一无所获。\
**Vertin**: There's nothing that we can be certain of for now. But on a brighter note, we didn't come back empty-handed from our mission either, Sonetto.

**维尔汀**：在混乱发生之前，我们成功在展厅里找到了德洛丝女士的签名。虚构集小姐，您提供的目击线索是正确的，德洛丝女士就身处科马拉监狱之中。\
**Vertin**: We found Dr. Dores's signature in the gallery. You were right all along, Recoleta. She was here.

**十四行诗**：但我们并没有发现德洛丝女士的身影。难道那位女士，也陷入了和理想家先生一样的状况吗？\
**Sonetto**: But we didn't see her at the gathering. Could something have happened to her, like with the Idealist?

**虚构集**：你的意思是，他们都是因为科马拉监狱的治疗而失踪的？\
**Recoleta**: Do you think she was also sent to the Physician and never made it back?

**维尔汀**：并不一定。想要查找到更多的线索，我们需要见到监狱的幕后之人，比如说狱卒一直提到的“狱医”。\
**Vertin**: This is all just speculation. If we want to find the Idealist or Dr. Dores ...

**维尔汀**：无论是关于理想家先生，还是德洛丝女士的下落——\
**Vertin**: We need to speak to this Physician first.

**维尔汀**：只是，虚构集小姐，您确定理想家先生就是您一直在寻找的笔友阿莱夫吗？\
**Vertin**: Ms. Recoleta, do you believe that the Idealist could be your pen pal, Aleph?

**虚构集**：哪怕他并不是我的笔友，他也是这个监狱里唯一知晓阿莱夫的存在的人。\
**Recoleta**: Whether he is or not, he's still my best lead.

那个名字再一次触动了她的神经。\
That name touches a nerve once again.

**虚构集**：我有强烈的预感，这个监狱里有一些异常的要素，它一直在阻拦着我们。\
**Recoleta**: Friends, I've had this strange feeling in my gut since we got here. Something is slowing us down.

**虚构集**：如果能搞清楚这一切……\
**Recoleta**: Now to figure out what it is ...

一种无声的恐惧击中了她，就像在寂静的湖面看到阵阵涟漪那般令人心生不安。\
A silent fear grips her, like ripples suddenly appearing on a once-still lake, unsettling in its quiet disturbance.

**虚构集**：听着，虽然这有些魔幻，但我有一个猜测——\
**Recoleta**: Look, it's a wild guess, but just wait till I finish.

**虚构集**：我认为，监狱中的一切似乎都和我的小说《理性家族的崛起与衰落》有联系。\
**Recoleta**: It feels like everything happening in this prison is somehow connected to my novel, The Rise and Fall of Sanity.

**维尔汀**：别担心，魔幻的事情对我们来说并不少见。所以，您的小说《家族的历史》——\
**Vertin**: We're no strangers to wild guesses, and sometimes they're closer to the truth than you'd think. So this ...

**虚构集**：是《理性家族的崛起与衰落》。\
**Recoleta**: The Rise and Fall of Sanity.

**维尔汀**：……我会记下来的。请问它讲了什么内容？\
**Vertin**: Sorry. What exactly is your story about?

猝不及防的提问吹散了午夜的阴霾。窗外，有月光正洒在灰白的雪地上。\
The question scatters the midnight gloom. Outside, moonlight spills over gray-white snow.

**虚构集**：噢……？噢！我还以为你们也不会感兴趣呢。\
**Recoleta**: Hah! I never thought that you'd be interested!

**虚构集**：让我想想……数、数年前，我认识了一名来自墨西哥超现实主义派的诗人……因此得知了一则关于阿马尔菲塔诺小镇的离奇故事……\
**Recoleta**: It starts—sorry, it's been a while since I told it from the beginning: A few, a few years ago, I worked, worked as a forest ranger. It happened in a desert town called Amalfitano, in Sonora back in 1975 ...

两位耐心的听众注视着面前结结巴巴的女孩，等待故事的下文。\
Two patient listeners watch the stammering girl, waiting for the next part of her story.

**虚构集**：唔……事实上，许多人反馈过这样的开头有点难懂，除了我的笔友阿莱夫。\
**Recoleta**: Ah, you know what? Most people say the beginning's a bit hard to get into, except for Aleph. I'm thinking of rewriting it.

**虚构集**：如果你们还愿意继续听的话，我还是想念一念最新的修改。\
**Recoleta**: But if you like the sound of it so far, maybe I could read you the latest part I just finished?

她谨慎地观察着两位读者的神色，小心翼翼地等待着答复。\
She studies her readers' expressions, guessing madly at their responses.

**维尔汀**：当然。\
**Vertin**: Please.

**虚构集**：故事起源于磁带中所记录的频率。\
**Recoleta**: "It all started with the frequency data from the tapes."

**虚构集**：能量扰动学家认为，巴比伦之骰的随机性正发生着变化——噢，很抱歉。\
**Recoleta**: "The general pattern seemed to have changed. At first, the Paracausality Researcher chalked it up to a statistical error—a glitch, perhaps."—Oh, sorry.

**虚构集**：有人做了小小的变革：能量扰动学家不停地计算，最终发现它的随机性中增加了一倍幸运，也增加了一倍罚码。她知晓巴比伦之骰的规则已然改变。\
**Recoleta**: But after a few days and long nights of meticulous calculations, that explanation only became less and less plausible. The odds of success and failure kept shifting, and the chance of repeating the previous result kept growing. It was as if someone had tampered with the rules and tweaked it to their liking.

**虚构集**：能量扰动学家带着这项可怖的消息走进了无人的阿马尔菲塔诺。\
**Recoleta**: She took her findings to Amalfitano, "the town of nothing," as they called it then.

**虚构集**：古旧的作坊中，那里的织工双眼已盲，她低声诉说着自己经历的一切。\
**Recoleta**: Near the old looms, she met a blind weaver who spoke softly of an old tale:

**虚构集**：“有一天，我在黎明时分听见骰子转动的声音。有什么东西夺走了我的视力，从此我不再能工作。”\
**Recoleta**: "I heard a strange rustling at dawn, like a die rolling along a wooden floor. Then the morning light dimmed and died. That was the last time I saw the sun, my own hands, or the threads I worked with."

**虚构集**：“骰子转动了一次，老迈的牛在犁地时寿终正寝。合眼前，它回忆起牛犊时代对劳作满怀期待的遥远下午。”\
**Recoleta**: "The second time I heard the die roll, I was told the oxen in the field sank to their knees and never stood again."

**虚构集**：“骰子转动了一次，无数青蛙在泥土间被犁耙碾过。它们拼命扭动着，向大地的裂缝绝望地钻去。”\
**Recoleta**: "By the third roll, the fields were crawling with frogs. Plows ran over them, and some still writhed, squeezing themselves deeper into the cracks in the earth."

**虚构集**：“骰子转动了一次，十只睡鼠在睡梦中坠向大海，十只熊在冬天前得以餍足。”\
**Recoleta**: "The fourth time the die rolled, ten dormice plunged into the sea in a strange sleepwalk, and ten bears feasted for the last time before winter arrived."

**虚构集**：“在界限中，最后一次转动应当是一次瞩目的决斗。胜者得到了十磅金子，败者引来了十只蝇虫。”\
**Recoleta**: "The final roll of the die was cast in a cage, during a duel, before a crowd of eager eyes. The winner left with ten pounds of gold, and the loser left with ten flies which fell on him to feast."

**维尔汀**：……\
**Vertin**: ...

**十四行诗**：……\
**Sonetto**: ...

名为静默的无形潮水，在狭小的囚室中漫延开来。\
The quiet spreads through their cell like a rolling tide.

**维尔汀**：这个故事，结束了吗？\
**Vertin**: Is that all?

**十四行诗**：我想……应该是的？\
**Sonetto**: Emm. Seems like it.

**虚构集**：唔……后面的部分还没有完整到可以拿出来讲的程度。\
**Recoleta**: Well, there's more, but I haven't quite figured those parts out yet.

**虚构集**：总之，目前的部分你们有什么读后感吗？什么都好！\
**Recoleta**: Any thoughts? Anything? I can take it. Please. I really need some feedback.

**维尔汀**：我只想知道主人公最后能不能找到那个骰子。\
**Vertin**: I ... I wonder if the protagonist ever finds this "Die of Babylon" in the end.

**虚构集**：噢噢，事实上，那并不是一个具体的骰子。维尔汀，那只是一个意象！\
**Recoleta**: Oh, Vertin, it isn't a real die. It's just a metaphor!

**维尔汀**：很抱歉，看来我没有理解它想要表达的内容。但这并不妨碍我能感受到，它应该是一个凄美而奇幻的故事。\
**Vertin**: Oh, I see. I must've missed that. Sorry. Still, it's a beautiful story. Sad, but beautiful.

**虚构集**：所以主题还是过于晦涩吗？唉……阿莱夫在上一次的回信中也提出了些建议，比如说这个盲眼的织工，就是他建议增加的角色，让她来引出主题的关联性。\
**Recoleta**: The story is still too obscure, isn't it? *sigh* Aleph warned me about this. In our last correspondence, he suggested adding the Blind Weaver to shed light on the hidden theme.

**虚构集**：这确实有些帮助，但角色们总是在讲话，而故事其实并没有实质性的进展。\
**Recoleta**: It helped at first. But even with this sage advice, no matter how hard I tried, the plot just didn't seem to move forward.

**虚构集**：这很奇怪。就像这个小镇中缺乏了某种至关重要的元素，导致每个篇章仿佛游荡在各自的世界里，无法交汇，而逐渐走向瓦解。\
**Recoleta**: I feel stuck in that village with them—lost, dazed, isolated inside their small, disconnected moments. Something crucial is missing, leaving gaps between the characters and scenes.

**虚构集**：叙事视角、故事主题、人物设计……它究竟在哪方面有所欠缺？又缺了什么？\
**Recoleta**: Should I change the storyteller's perspective? Start a different angle? Or maybe rewrite the characters completely? What should I do?

在不知名作家陷入自我怀疑的漩涡之前，需要有人推动眼下的实质性进展。\
Before the writer sinks into a swirling vortex of self-doubt, someone decides to push for something tangible.

**十四行诗**：所以，你认为科马拉监狱与你的小说有什么联系？\
**Sonetto**: Apologies, but you said your story somehow connects to what's happening here in the Panopticon. What makes you think that?

**虚构集**：我……我不知道。你们能理解这种感受吗？就像是你在梦里见过的场景出现在了现实中，虚实交织、令人恍惚，不知身处何境。\
**Recoleta**: It's a strange feeling. Like everything here belongs to a dream I once had, only I can't remember it.

**十四行诗**：你所描述的感觉，指的是似曾相识的既视感[déjà vu]吗？\
**Sonetto**: Do you mean that you have a sense of déjà vu?

**十四行诗**：卡卡尼亚小姐曾告诉过我，那是一种潜意识矛盾冲突的感知障碍……\
**Sonetto**: It's nothing to worry about. Our psychiatrist friend, Kakania, told me those moments are often the result of a dysfunctional connection between two parts of the brain, like a little glitch in our heads.

**虚构集**：不不，我不是这个意思……！\
**Recoleta**: No, it's nothing like déjà vu!

不被理解的故事讲述者显得有些焦躁。\
The storyteller snaps back, politely agitated.

**虚构集**：诗社、规则、理想家……那些象征、意象和隐喻，它们分明就是按照同一种规律在推进！\
**Recoleta**: Déjà vu is a single moment, a specific situation. But here it's everything! La Sociedad, the rules, the Idealist, even the incidents in the gallery! Each one unfolds in a similar pattern, like the grooves on a record, telling a story I feel I've listened to before.

**虚构集**：从阿马尔菲塔诺到科马拉，故事与现实构成了一个巨大的整体。当一个事物出现时，另一个也随之而定。\
**Recoleta**: Amalfitano and Comala. They're two sides of that same record, playing out the same tune. Whatever happens in my story seems to be happening here too.

**虚构集**：维尔汀，这一切都是从我遇见你开始的。\
**Recoleta**: I had that feeling when I met you as well, Ms. Vertin.

**虚构集**：因为在这个故事的开头，也有一个和你一样的、提着箱子的能量扰动学家……！\
**Recoleta**: At first, I thought it was only an interesting coincidence. You're much like the first character in my story—a traveler with a suitcase.

女孩语无伦次地解释着人物的对应关系。\
The girl rambles on, desperately relating to her characters.

**虚构集**：就像德洛丝女士……她是盲眼的织工。织工是一个宿命论的拥护者，一直崇奉巴比伦之骰的存在，却被它夺去了双眼……\
**Recoleta**: But then I realized, the doctor, your Dores—she's like the Blind Weaver, who lost her sight to the die despite having always been faithful to it.

**虚构集**：而狱卒小姐，则是银行职员，为了遗忘可怕的过去，甘愿让跨国集团建立的新制度将小镇侵蚀……\
**Recoleta**: And the jailer—she's the Bank Clerk who assisted the corporation in taking over the town in order to escape her past.

**虚构集**：至于理想家先生，他则是死于谋杀案的赶驴人幽灵……当然，还有巴比伦之骰……\
**Recoleta**: And the Idealist? He's the Murdered Donkey Driver. And the Die of Babylon ... No ...

**虚构集**：我亲爱的虚构朋友们，你们身上究竟发生着什么？\
**Recoleta**: My dear fictional friends ... What on earth is happening to you?

**维尔汀**：你所说的联系，指的是监狱里的人物，和你的小说是一一对应的吗？\
**Vertin**: Wait. Are you saying that everyone we've met here matches a character from your story, like some kind of archetype?

**维尔汀**：……它太过抽象了，但我不否认你的推测，因为我觉得你有一个新奇、独特的视角。\
**Vertin**: That sounds unbelievable. But, then again, maybe you're onto something.

**维尔汀**：你用文学考量这个世界，而那是我和十四行诗都未曾尝试过的。\
**Vertin**: You see the world through a different lens that none of us share.

**虚构集**：不，除了人物，事件也是对应的！只是，我还不能确认这种联系……\
**Recoleta**: Not just the characters! The events here are mirroring my story, too.

**虚构集**：阿莱夫是唯一能看懂我小说的人。如果这里发生的一切，真的与我的小说有关——\
**Recoleta**: Aleph—he's the only one who truly understood my story. If things are playing out just like my novel, then ...

**虚构集**：那么阿莱夫，他一定就在科马拉监狱之中。\
**Recoleta**: Maybe Aleph is in fact still here.

**维尔汀**：所以，你认为有人将你的小说作为操纵监狱的蓝本？\
**Vertin**: Are you suggesting that someone is controlling the Panopticon in order to make it follow the same plot as your story?

**维尔汀**：他根据小说情节修改了科马拉监狱的规则，策划了理想家先生的遇袭，也隐匿了德洛丝女士的踪迹。\
**Vertin**: That they've set the rules, started the poetry group, planned the attack on the Idealist, and tried to prevent us from finding Dr. Dores?

**维尔汀**：如果有这个人，那么他只可能是你的笔友，阿莱夫。\
**Vertin**: If that's true, Ms. Recoleta, it's very likely that the one acting against us is in fact Aleph himself.

虚构集从未想过推理的链条会演变成这副模样。\
Recoleta never expected the chain of reasoning to unravel this way.

**虚构集**：等等，维尔汀，我、我没有这样说过！我只是……\
**Recoleta**: But I ... No ... How could that be possible?!

她着急地打断了对方的话，片刻后，女孩的神色显得迷茫起来。\
She interrupts, only for confusion to creep onto her face moments later.

**虚构集**：不，我不能明白。他为什么要这么做？他完全没有这么做的理由。\
**Recoleta**: Why? Why would he do this?

**虚构集**：他是博学的炼金术师，是高深的隐秘诗人，是世上唯一能为我的小说提供建议的导师。他怎么会和谋杀扯上联系？\
**Recoleta**: I don't see any reason why he'd be connected. He's an intelligent, cultured, and profound person, not a common killer.

**虚构集**：这个监狱，这一切……究竟是哪里不对劲呢？\
**Recoleta**: No, none of this adds up.

**十四行诗**：德洛丝女士是由叛变的伊戈尔一行人带来乌斯怀亚的。\
**Sonetto**: Remember, Dr. Dores was brought to Ushuaia by the Zeno rebels.

**十四行诗**：而我们已经确认，伊戈尔已与重塑之手勾连……\
**Sonetto**: And we know they're connected to Manus Vindictae.

**十四行诗**：如果按照虚构集小姐所说，阿莱夫隐匿了德洛丝女士的踪迹，那么他就与重塑之手有联系。\
**Sonetto**: If this Aleph really is hiding Dores from us, he may be working with them.

虚构集哑然地望向对方，随后仓促地转移了话题。\
Recoleta stares blankly for a time before clumsily shifting the topic.

**虚构集**：就此打住！维尔汀，十四行诗，没想到你们如此有编故事的天赋……也许二位该加入本能现实主义派。\
**Recoleta**: Oh my, Sonetto! I didn't know you had such a flair for stories! Maybe you should join us and become a visceral realist too.

**虚构集**：我知道了，是这个隔绝现实的监狱，以及我那迟早会成为杰作的小说启发了你们！\
**Recoleta**: I think you're only imagining things. Perhaps you were inspired by this strange prison? Haha.

**维尔汀**：你说得对，我们应该学习一些虚构的思维。\
**Vertin**: Perhaps we all need to start writing our own stories.

**维尔汀**：另外，躲在门外的先生，您在那里已经偷听了有一些时候了。\
**Vertin**: Come out, now. Whoever's out there, speak up.

**维尔汀**：请问您有什么事吗？\
**Vertin**: How can we help you?

**十四行诗**：什么？是谁在那儿！\
**Sonetto**: Who's there?

## 9TH-09 全景中央 / The Central Tower

**加西亚**：嘿，快停手……！我是加西亚，白天在诗社中布展的。\
**García**: Easy, easy! It's me, García! We met at the gallery earlier.

**加西亚**：我没有恶意。事实上，我带来的是友善与和解的信息。\
**García**: Please. I come in peace.

虚构集并不在乎青年的解释，她的注意力完全停留在加西亚身旁的女性身上。\
Recoleta pays no mind to the young man's explanations; her focus holds on the woman beside him.

**虚构集**：是你，奥克塔维奥！对理想家先生动手的人！！\
**Recoleta**: It's you, Octavia! The murderer herself!

**维尔汀**：冷静些，虚构集小姐。\
**Vertin**: Please, calm yourself, Ms. Recoleta.

**维尔汀**：狱卒小姐已经确认过了，那声枪响，并不是由她所造成的。开枪者另有其人。\
**Vertin**: The jailer has already confirmed that she wasn't the one to fire at the Idealist. The shot came from somewhere else in the room.

**虚构集**：……哼。\
**Recoleta**: Hmph.

虚构集咬了咬唇，不甘心地后退了一步。\
Recoleta bites her lip, giving up a little space to the intruders.

**维尔汀**：奥克塔维奥小姐，您深夜拜访，是有什么想要和我们说的吗？\
**Vertin**: Ms. Octavia, what brings you here at this hour?

**奥克塔维奥**：诸位，我也无法想象在科马拉会发生这种事……我从来都不支持以暴力作为维持秩序的手段。\
**Octavia**: I come here out of goodwill. Believe me, I didn't want any bloodshed either.

**奥克塔维奥**：你们应该是第一天来到科马拉的吧？所以并不了解这座监狱的运转情况。\
**Octavia**: I understand you just arrived today. There's something you need to know about the inmates here.

来者的神情中带有不难察觉的疲惫。\
Their visitor's expression is weary and low.

**奥克塔维奥**：无论是文学还是现实，我们都是被放逐至边陲之人。事实上，在成立新派系之前，我就已经与监狱的管理者们达成了共识。\
**Octavia**: We're outcasts rejected by society and literature, and our privileges are limited within these walls. But before I started my own literature group, I struck a deal with the Panopticon authorities.

**奥克塔维奥**：只要我们配合管理者的一切行动，就能获得在监狱中自由谈论文学的权利——你可能很难理解这对我们来说有多重要。\
**Octavia**: If we cooperate and stay out of trouble, they'd leave us be. We could discuss literature freely and openly in Comala. Such a thing may seem trivial to you, but this is of immense importance to us.

**虚构集**：谈论文学是世上最快乐的事情，它不应该需要什么前提条件。\
**Recoleta**: Oh, there's no happier thing in this world than discussing literature! No one should ever put limits on it!

**奥克塔维奥**：虚构集小姐，你并不明白我们的处境。只要在这座监狱里，有些规则就是永远无法逃离的。\
**Octavia**: You're right, Recoleta. But we're prisoners here. There are certain rules we have to follow.

**奥克塔维奥**：理想家……他总以为自己是这里唯一清醒的存在，认为那篇长诗和所谓的主义能带领大家冲破“视线”的牢笼。\
**Octavia**: Except, the Idealist didn't see it our way. He refused to compromise, believing that the long poem and his so-called "-ism" could break us free from the cage of the ever-watchful eye.

**虚构集**：理想家先生他并没有错……因为本能现实主义，本身就是一个能够让我们回归创作本质的好东西。\
**Recoleta**: Perhaps he was right. You might've achieved more if you'd listened to him. After all, visceral realism keeps us connected to who we are.

**虚构集**：在外面，许多像我一样的青年诗人，都相信它带来的力量。\
**Recoleta**: You have to believe in the truth of visceral realism! Because out there, beyond these walls, many of us still do!

**奥克塔维奥**：是吗？加西亚先生，你是三个月前才进入科马拉监狱的，也是诗社中最晚到来的成员。\
**Octavia**: And what has it changed? García, you're the latest inmate here. Tell us, three months ago, before they arrested you and took you here ...

**奥克塔维奥**：请你告诉我们，在监狱外，你们本能现实主义派的运动进行得如何了？\
**Octavia**: What has the visceral realism movement accomplished out there?

一旁，沉默许久的加西亚靠在了栏杆上，发出了金属振动与摩擦的响声。他的嘴唇间有一根粗糙的卷纸条正在燃烧。\
Beside them, García, who had been patiently leaning against the railing, produces a metallic vibration on its grates. A rough paper roll burns between his lips.

**加西亚**：我们曾经吸引了许多有志青年，也的确发起了数场文学运动……\
**García**: At first, it was revolutionary. Young poets joined in droves. We held gatherings, and the literary world seemed alive again.

**加西亚**：在核心成员离开拉丁美洲的时候，我还是个孩子，我以为那无关紧要。事实却是——我们的运动再也没有任何起色了。\
**García**: I was just a kid when the leading poets left the city. Everyone thought it was only temporary. But they didn't come back, and nothing has happened since.

**加西亚**：所有人都心知肚明：属于本能现实主义者的故事，在1977年就已经宣告完结了。\
**García**: No one says it, but we all know: visceral realism died in 1977.

**虚构集**：不……它没有结束，至少在我这里没有。\
**Recoleta**: No. Not for me.

**虚构集**：它依然存在着，哪怕世上只剩下我一个人在坚信它！\
**Recoleta**: It's not dead as long as people still believe in it. I believe in it!

奥克塔维奥并没有在意对方孩子气的发言。她知道，“坚信”有时柔弱得像一滴蜘蛛丝上的露水。\
Octavia ignores the childish remark. She knows that "conviction" can be as fragile as a spider's web.

**奥克塔维奥**：为什么你们总喜欢说“遵循自我”？\
**Octavia**: Belief, faith—what is this obsession with the "true self"?

**奥克塔维奥**：为什么你们总觉得在社会身份与规训下，还藏着一个独一无二的真实自我呢？\
**Octavia**: Why does your type always insist on there being a true self hiding beneath our roles in society, our disciplines?

**虚构集**：恕我直言，理想家先生就是一个鲜活的例子，他在监狱中仍坚持着自己想做的事。\
**Recoleta**: Look at the Idealist! He never once stopped fighting for what he believed in, even long after he was put behind these bars.

**奥克塔维奥**：“理想家”，哈，真是人如其名……当他摆脱瞭望塔的视线后，他只会发现自己一无所有，并且谁也不是。\
**Octavia**: "Idealist," what a name he gave himself. Who will he be when he finally breaks free from the eyes of the central tower? When he's left without his willful audience? A nobody, that's what.

**奥克塔维奥**：那才是真相，一个令人惊恐而叹息的真相。\
**Octavia**: And that is a truth even he is terrified of.

**维尔汀**：奥克塔维奥小姐，你应该不是为了说理想家先生的坏话才特地前来的吧？\
**Vertin**: Ms. Octavia. I hope you've come with something more important to share than just some criticism of the Idealist.

**奥克塔维奥**：那不是坏话……算了。你说的不错，我是为了一件重要的事情才特地前来，而那与你们此行的目的有关。\
**Octavia**: You're right. I have an important message for you.

**奥克塔维奥**：德洛丝女士——我听到你正在寻找她。她来自圣保罗荣军院，笔名叫“兀尔德”，对吗？\
**Octavia**: Dr. Dores—I heard you were looking for her. The woman from the São Paulo Veterans' Residence. She used to write under the name "Urd," didn't she?

**维尔汀**：我很惊讶……在这座监狱中，你是第一个主动与我提起她的人。\
**Vertin**: Yes, that's right. Do you know her? You're the first person I've met here to speak plainly about her.

**维尔汀**：所以，奥克塔维奥小姐，你知道德洛丝女士现在在哪里吗？\
**Vertin**: Do you know where she might be?

**奥克塔维奥**：我确实见过她，但我并不知晓她现今在监狱的何处，也许你得直接去问监狱的管理者们。\
**Octavia**: We crossed paths, but only briefly. I'm not sure where she's gone. Maybe the authorities know.

**奥克塔维奥**：这是德洛丝女士先前交给我的东西，我想你比我更需要它。\
**Octavia**: However, she left this with me. I think you'll need it more than I do.

奥克塔维奥将随身携带的收纳册递上前。\
Octavia hands over her personal folder.

在翻开之前，她就已经转过身去。\
Before they might open it, she has already turned to leave.

**奥克塔维奥**：我还有事情要筹备，就不奉陪各位的推理游戏了。加西亚先生，我们走吧。\
**Octavia**: We have other matters to attend to. I'll leave you to your business. García, shall we?

来访者脚步匆匆地离去了，没有人看到她藏在阴影中的表情。\
Their visitors leave in haste, their faces and expressions obscured by the night's shadows.

调查员们半信半疑地翻开手中破旧的稿件收纳册。\
The Foundation's investigators open the worn manuscript folder with caution.

**维尔汀**：“在狱医先生的告知中，我得知了科马拉监狱那令人惊骇的真相，以及一只隐藏在阴影之下的无形之手，即名为‘重塑之手’的民间组织。”\
**Vertin**: "The Physician told me the horrifying truth about the Panopticon of Comala and the power behind it—Manus Vindictae."

**维尔汀**：“……他们以资助为由，实则垄断了资源的供给与分配，让整座监狱的规则洗牌，并制造了难以言喻的恐怖氛围。其中，狱医先生的默许难辞其咎。”\
**Vertin**: "By becoming the Panopticon's sole patron, they seized control of the resources and the allocation system, turning this place into a living hell. I suspect that the Physician, the current highest authority here, is responsible for this situation."

**维尔汀**：“……他们举办高强度训练，令不少身体羸弱的囚犯在绝望的折磨中病重离世；他们迫使纯血神秘学家戴上面具，在疯狂的呓语中成为被奴役的对象……”\
**Vertin**: "... I discovered that the inmates were put through brutal training, even when they were too sick to carry out their tasks. They also forced pure-blood arcanist inmates to wear their masks, effectively turning them into murmuring puppets ..."

**十四行诗**：这一切果然与重塑之手有关联。\
**Sonetto**: Just as we suspected, Manus Vindictae is orchestrating everything.

**十四行诗**：我们在乌斯怀亚的城市中，无法寻找到与重塑之手有关的线索，就是因为他们一直躲藏在科马拉监狱。\
**Sonetto**: No wonder we didn't find them in the city. They've been hiding here all along.

**维尔汀**：而这里，正是一个日常中不可能踏足的地方。\
**Vertin**: No one would've thought to come looking for them here.

重重地合上手中的稿件收纳册。\
They snap the folder shut.

似曾相识的签名字迹。在《UTTU》杂志的扉页里，在巴西圣保罗热情之家找到的账单上。\
A familiar signature, seen on the foreword page of UTTU magazine, and the receipt found in São Paulo's Heartfelt Home.

**十四行诗**：但是，这种送上门的线索……总让我感觉有些不安。\
**Sonetto**: But why would Ms. Octavia bring this to us? What's in it for her?

**十四行诗**：司辰，是否有可能，她在故意误导我们？\
**Sonetto**: Do you think she's trying to mislead us, Timekeeper?

**维尔汀**：不排除这种可能，但根据字迹判断，这本手记的确是属于德洛丝女士的。\
**Vertin**: Maybe. But the handwriting in that notebook is most certainly Urd's.

**维尔汀**：如果奥克塔维奥小姐在故意误导我们，那她一定是监狱的幕后主使……虚构集小姐，她会是你的笔友阿莱夫吗？\
**Vertin**: If she's leading us astray on purpose, why? Ms. Recoleta, what do you think? Could she be Aleph?

**虚构集**：等等……她怎么可能是我的笔友！你们没有看到她试图否定那些美好事物的极端性吗？阿莱夫绝不会如此偏颇。\
**Recoleta**: Not a chance! Haven't you seen how she denies everything beautiful in the world? Aleph would never be so biased.

**虚构集**：阿莱夫更像是一枚镜片，一枚不光映出事物的光亮，也会同样映出其中的暗影的镜片。\
**Recoleta**: No, Aleph is like a mirror. He reflects both light and shadow.

**虚构集**：而奥克塔维奥……更像是在极端的环境下逐渐忘记了自己本来的模样。\
**Recoleta**: But Octavia ... Maybe she hasn't looked at the shadow within for a long time.

**虚构集**：但我不得不承认，她的确是一名作家。\
**Recoleta**: I know that look on her face. It's the look of a writer.

**虚构集**：那是一副令我感到熟悉的模样，属于拉丁美洲的、迷茫的、挣扎的青年面孔。这一路上，我见过无数张这样的面孔……\
**Recoleta**: I've seen so many like her during my trip—the faces of a lost, struggling generation.

夜幕下，科马拉监狱如同一块被世界遗忘的墓碑，缓缓为冰冷的细雪所覆盖。\
Under the night sky, Comala Prison stands like a forgotten gravestone covered by fine, cold snow.

在形似囚室的房间中，三位寻人的女孩分享着荒诞离奇的故事；而在中央的瞭望塔前，美洲豹敲响了一扇紧闭的门扉。\
In a room repurposed from a prison cell, three girls in search of someone share an absurd, bizarre tale. Meanwhile, at the entrance of the central watchtower, a jaguar knocks on a secure door.

**狱卒**：呼……梅林先生，我前来汇报今日的监狱情况。\
**Jailer**: *deep breath* Dr. Merlin, I'm here to report on today's events.

**？？？**：请进。\
**???**: Come in.

寂静的办公室中仅有书写的唰唰声。\
Frantic writing breaks the quiet of the room.

狱卒的拜访并未让办公桌后的男子放下手中的纸笔，他心无旁骛，仿若这个世上空无一人。\
The jailer's visit does not deter the man behind the desk. He continues writing, wholly absorbed, as if each letter were filling the world around him.

**狱卒**：梅林先生，方才在囚犯活动场地中发生了一场暴动。\
**Jailer**: There was a commotion in the gallery today, sir.

**狱卒**：一位名叫理想家的囚犯受了重伤。据当时在他身边的囚犯描述，他因失血过多，一度停止了呼吸。\
**Jailer**: An inmate known as the Idealist was severely injured. The inmates nearby said he lost consciousness from blood loss.

**狱卒**：但在暴动结束后，理想家却从活动场地中消失了。这是我的失职，我搜查了一遍监狱，也没能找到他的尸体，明天我会扩大搜查的范围。\
**Jailer**: However, after we put everyone back in their cell, the Idealist was gone. I made a sweep of the grounds, but there was no trace of him.

**狱卒**：也许理想家他，并没有死亡……\
**Jailer**: It's possible that he regained consciousness and went into hiding. I'll perform a full search tomorrow.

美洲豹下意识隐瞒了癫痫发作的巴勃鲁。\
The jaguar finds herself quite unexpectedly concealing the truth about Pablo.

**狱医**：不需要。\
**The Physician**: No need.

**狱卒**：您的意思是……？\
**Jailer**: Sir?

**狱医**：是他先违反了规定，不是么？\
**The Physician**: He knew the consequences of breaking the rules, did he not?

**狱卒**：……梅林先生，我认为，今天的暴乱已经足以证明让囚犯自主持有武器的危险性。\
**Jailer**: Sir, with all due respect, I think today's incident proved just how dangerous it is to let the inmates keep their weapons.

**狱卒**：我们应该限制违禁物品的使用，或者增加巡逻狱卒的数量。囚犯的自发规训是不稳定的，我们不能仅仅依靠瞭望塔的权威性去——\
**Jailer**: We never should've let them walk around with deadly weapons! Even if we had to, we should've doubled the guards. We can't expect them to follow their own rules simply out of fear of the central tower.

狱医毫不在意地打断了她的话。\
The Physician interrupts her sharply, with no hint of concern.

**狱医**：这不是你该在意的范畴。你只需要做好属于“狱卒”的本职工作。\
**The Physician**: Such matters fall beyond your purview, Jailer. You only need to do what's required of your title.

**狱医**：继续你的汇报。\
**The Physician**: Is there anything else?

**狱卒**：……好的。今日有来自基金会的官方人员进入监狱参观，她们正在科马拉中寻找一位名叫德洛丝的女士。\
**Jailer**: There is another thing. Two guests from the Foundation came through today. They said they were looking for someone named Dores.

**狱卒**：在0号通道中，基金会的来客与囚犯一同清理了监狱中的魔精。\
**Jailer**: They've shown a willingness to cooperate. Though, they were involved with the incident in Corridor Zero.

唰唰的书写声仍在继续，她的汇报并未得到重视。狱卒深吸一口气，接下来的内容让她难以启齿。\
The sound of writing continues. Her report is disregarded. The jailer takes a deep breath. The next part is difficult to say.

**狱卒**：梅林先生，我必须汇报一件事……\
**Jailer**: Sir, there is one more thing.

**狱卒**：我已经让奥克塔维奥小姐重新安排了监狱中的劳作与物资分配，但我们的物资很快就要消耗殆尽了。\
**Jailer**: I told Ms. Octavia we're short on rations, and she's adjusted the inmates' portions accordingly. But that won't last long.

**狱卒**：那个名为重塑之手的民间机构，自三月起，他们就停止了提供资助……来自芝诺的军人带走了最后一批由他们送入监狱的囚犯。\
**Jailer**: Manus Vindictae stopped providing supplies back in March, and Zeno has collected all the prisoners they had previously placed in our custody.

**狱卒**：为什么他们忽然撤离了乌斯怀亚？是因为他们不再需要监狱了吗？\
**Jailer**: I just wonder why they have so suddenly withdrawn from Ushuaia and brought all their prisoners with them.

**狱卒**：自从原来的典狱长达尔杜夫先生调任之后，我留意到，官方似乎也再没有联系过科马拉了。\
**Jailer**: I also noticed that we haven't received any orders from the government since Warden Tartuffe was transferred.

**狱卒**：今天，我们也没有收到任何来自阿根廷官方政府的消息。\
**Jailer**: In fact, we haven't had any communication with them at all.

**狱卒**：梅林先生，无论是药物、食品还是生活用品，再过一段时间，我们就无法维持监狱的正常运作了……\
**Jailer**: Sir, in frank terms, we're facing down a serious shortage of medicine, food, and basic supplies. At this rate, the Panopticon will soon be unable to operate. Where will our inmates go then?

面前的男人长久地沉默着。\
The man before her says nothing for a long time, his pen still flickering over the page.

**狱卒**：我们是否可以寻求基金会的帮助？今日，他们派人过来视察科马拉，是不是意味着他们对神秘学家监狱或者全景监狱理论感兴趣？\
**Jailer**: Can we ask the Foundation for help? Th-They've sent their people here. Maybe they're interested in the Panopticon?

**狱卒**：也许，您会愿意会见来自基金会的使者……？\
**Jailer**: I could arrange a meeting if you like.

**狱医**：这真是一件奇异的事情。\
**The Physician**: You're unusually talkative today.

男人终于停下了书写，抬起头来。\
The man finally stops writing and looks up.

**狱卒**：……您说什么，梅林先生？\
**Jailer**: Pardon, sir?

**狱医**：狱卒这个身份，竟然让你产生了这等的责任心。你和以前不再是一个人了。\
“狱卒”——这个名字塑造了你。\
**The Physician**: It's fascinating, you know. You've become so much more concerned about this place and its inmates than when you first started. You are now dictated by your title.

**狱卒**：我很抱歉，梅林先生。是我僭越了。\
**Jailer**: I didn't mean to overstep. I'm sorry.

**狱医**：你下去吧，我接下来还有事——对了。\
**The Physician**: You can go now. I have a great deal of work to do. Oh, and one more thing.

他忽然记起了什么，叫住了准备离开的狱卒。\
He beckons the jailer back before she leaves.

**狱医**：记得保证科马拉议会的如期举行。\
**The Physician**: Make sure this month's Comala Congress is held according to schedule.

**狱卒**：请放心，我会的，梅林先生。\
**Jailer**: Yes, sir.

美洲豹的身影消失在门扉后，无声息的脚步逐渐远去。直至这时，神经一直紧绷的狱医才展露出该有的烦躁。\
The jaguar disappears beyond the door, metallic footsteps fading into the distance. Only then does the Physician allow his suppressed frustration to surface.

**狱医**：我早就说过——理想家那个家伙必须死。你得管管他，阿莱夫。你看他捅出了多大的篓子！\
**The Physician**: How many times have I warned you about this? The Idealist has to go. He's nothing but trouble for us! You're too soft on him, Aleph. Look at the mess he has us in now!

**阿莱夫**：冷静些。\
**Aleph**: Calm down.

**狱医**：一个无耻的偷盗者，自毁的狂徒，处心积虑的疯子。\
**The Physician**: He's a rabble-rousing thief, a self-destructive maniac, a snake in the grass.

**狱医**：他甚至从我手中偷走了科马拉之雨。那个疯子险些毁了这一切。\
**The Physician**: He even stole the Tear of Comala from me. He's nearly ruined everything we've worked for!

男人愤怒地举起那颗失而复得的骰子。\
The man angrily raises the once-lost and now-found die.

幽暗的室内，它若有似无地闪烁着抚慰人心的辉光。\
In the dim room, it flickers with a comforting glow.

**阿莱夫**：这只是一颗骰子，梅林。\
**Aleph**: It's only a die, Merlin. It does nothing more than a die can do.

**狱医**：你也看到他今日的举动了。虽然只有短短的一刻，他成功使用科马拉之雨改变了监狱的模样。\
**The Physician**: You were there today. You saw what he did. He managed to change the Panopticon with this die, even if only for a second.

**狱医**：他的内心如此混乱，全是非理性的映射和超现实的感受，这会彻底影响我对监狱的掌控。\
**The Physician**: He'll ruin my work, Aleph. He's a slave to his passion; his head is filled with impulsive thoughts. I don't trust him. We can't trust him!

**狱医**：阿莱夫，我已经按照你的吩咐，完成了你要求的一切，而你也必须对此付出应有的回报。\
**The Physician**: I've done everything you've asked. Now it's time to do your part.

阿莱夫对狱医的愤慨激昂呈现出一种全然的漠视，他一秒不停地书写着回信。\
Aleph responds with indifference to the Physician's frustration, continuing his writing without pause.

**狱医**：剩下的时间不多了，我绝不能、不能再出任何的差错。我不会让任何人影响我对全景监狱的实验。\
**The Physician**: Time's ticking down. I can't afford any further mistakes. No one can be permitted to stop my experiment in the Panopticon.

**狱医**：我会证明，这条道路能通向真正的答案。\
**The Physician**: I'll prove it to them that we've found the path to the ultimate answer.

## 9TH-10 费洛蒙漩涡 / The Ant Mill

那座蓝色屋顶的茅屋一如既往地沉默着。\
The cottage with the blue roof was silent as always.

能量扰动学家在一片梦的投影中，发现了巴比伦之骰的真相。\
In a fleeting dream, the Paracausality Researcher uncovered the truth behind the Die of Babylon.

正如所有的历史学家一样，她尊敬相仿的规律。正如所有的占星师一样，她尊敬星轨的移动。\
She carefully examined hidden patterns, much like an astute astrologer tracks the movements of the stars.

容忍错误不等于否认命运的真实性，相反，它证实了命运的存在。如果您对此有疑问，不妨问问伟大的赫拉克利特吧！\
What may seem like errors or accidents doesn't negate the verities of destiny. On the contrary, they affirm its very existence. Just ask the great Heraclitus!

La cabaña con el techo azul estaba silenciosa como siempre. En un sueño fugaz, la Investigadora de Paracausalidad descubrió la verdad detrás del Dado de Babilonia. Examinó cuidadosamente los patrones ocultos, como un astuto astrólogo rastrea los movimientos de las estrellas. Lo que pueda parecer errores o accidentes no niega las verdades del destino. Por el contrario, afirman su existencia. ¡Solo pregúntale al gran Heráclito.\
在无人观测的宇宙中，巴比伦之骰将永不停止地旋转。在无限长又无限短的时间里，它将为所有人赋予命运。\
La cabaña con el techo azul estaba silenciosa como siempre. En un sueño fugaz, la Investigadora de Paracausalidad descubrió la verdad detrás del Dado de Babilonia. Examinó cuidadosamente los patrones ocultos, como un astuto astrólogo rastrea los movimientos de las estrellas. Lo que pueda parecer errores o accidentes no niega las verdades del destino. Por el contrario, afirman su existencia. ¡Solo pregúntale al gran Heráclito.\
In an unobserved universe, the Die of Babylon spins in perpetuity, dictating the fate of all in time that is both infinitely long and infinitely short.

瞧，她已经闭上了眼睛！她尊重数字的偶然性，尊重命运的随机性，尊重巴比伦的决定。\
Look, she closed her eyes! She respected the randomness of numbers and destiny. She respected the Die's judgment.

否则，她自愿迷失于时间的间隙中，成为永恒徘徊的幽灵。\
Otherwise, she would have acquiescently lost herself in the gaps of time and wandered forever as a ghost in oblivion.

En un universo no observado, el Dado de Babilonia gira perpetuamente, dictando el destino de todos en un tiempo que es tanto infinitamente largo como infinitamente corto. ¡Mira, cerró los ojos! Respetaba la aleatoriedad de los números y el destino. Respetaba el juicio del Dado. De lo contrario, se habría perdido sumisamente en los huecos del tiempo y vagaría para siempre como un fantasma en el olvido.\
翌日。静穆的监狱大厅中，几乎所有科马拉的囚犯都聚集在了此处。\
En un universo no observado, el Dado de Babilonia gira perpetuamente, dictando el destino de todos en un tiempo que es tanto infinitamente largo como infinitamente corto. ¡Mira, cerró los ojos! Respetaba la aleatoriedad de los números y el destino. Respetaba el juicio del Dado. De lo contrario, se habría perdido sumisamente en los huecos del tiempo y vagaría para siempre como un fantasma en el olvido.\
In the solemn prison hall, under the half-light of the next day, the prisoners of Comala gather.

在众人的视线下，面色严肃的奥克塔维奥走上了主持台。\
Octavia steps onto the podium with a stern expression.

**奥克塔维奥**：首先，我必须向诸位澄清：昨日，发生在理想家先生身上的事情与我毫无干系。我愿以我未来的作家生涯起誓！\
**Octavia**: First, allow me to make one thing clear: I had absolutely nothing to do with what happened to the Idealist yesterday. I swear it on my career as a writer!

**奥克塔维奥**：诸位皆知，我与理想家先生分别代表着美洲诗社的两个不同派别。\
制定不要自找麻烦条约[Let sleeping dogs lie]以来数月，我们一直保持着和平。\
**Octavia**: As you all know, the Idealist and I are the representatives of the two factions of La Sociedad de Poetas de las Américas. As you also know, we have been at peace since the Let Sleeping Dogs Lie agreement was signed a few months ago.

**奥克塔维奥**：时至今日，我们仍然共同生存于瞭望塔的视线下，奉行着同样的行事原则。请诸位相信，我们与管理者们会共同努力，寻找理想家先生的下落。\
**Octavia**: Despite our differing views, we have coexisted to this day under the watchful gaze of the central tower. Rest assured that we will work tirelessly to locate the missing Idealist.

**囚犯Ⅲ**：奥克塔维奥小姐，无需自责，这并不是您的错！\
**Inmate III**: Don't put so much pressure on yourself, Ms. Octavia. His death wasn't your fault!

**囚犯Ⅲ**：分明是他先口出狂言，在精神上攻击了您！\
**Inmate III**: After all, he was the one who threw the first verbal dagger!

台下的窃窃私语自然也传到了另一派系的囚犯耳中。\
The murmurs cascading below reach the ears of the prisoners from another faction.

**罗贝托**：嘿，你们这些家伙，对理想家先生放尊重一点！\
**Roberta**: Show some respect, you morons!

**罗贝托**：理想家先生只是失踪了！在我们找到他之前，他就会完好如初地出现在我们所有人面前！\
**Roberta**: The Idealist is missing, not dead! I'm sure he'll show up in one piece before we know it!

**囚犯Ⅲ**：趁早节哀吧，罗贝托！我只能说，你们很难再找到一个像他这样疯得彻底的领导者了！\
**Inmate III**: Better face the hard truth now, Roberta. Though I have to say, it won't be easy for you to find a new leader as mad as him!

主持人的轻咳打断了台下的争论。\
A polite cough from the hostess pauses the heated debate.

**奥克塔维奥**：……请诸位保持安静！\
**Octavia**: Please, everyone, quiet down!

**奥克塔维奥**：按照条约，本次科马拉议会[The Congress]的主持人应是理想家先生。由于他在那场意外中失踪，现在由我代理——\
**Octavia**: According to the agreement, today's congress should've been chaired by the Idealist. Since he is still missing, I will be acting on his—

**？？？**：抱歉。作为议会的监督者，我来晚了。\
**???**: Pardon my lateness. Go ahead. I'm ready to moderate.

属于外来者的脚步声响起，狱卒带领着访客出现在监狱大厅的入口处。\
Unfamiliar footsteps break the regular pattern of events. The jailer leads her visitors to the entrance of the prison hall.

**狱卒**：维尔汀小姐，昨晚，我查阅了监狱近半年的档案，但均一无所获。\
**Jailer**: Ms. Vertin, I looked over the incarceration and visitor records from the past six months.

**狱卒**：科马拉监狱中，并没有关于德洛丝女士任何的官方书面记录。\
**Jailer**: There was no mention of anyone named Dores.

**维尔汀**：目前看来，只有狱医才知晓德洛丝女士的下落。我们有迫切见到监狱管理者的理由，希望您能安排。\
**Vertin**: Then it seems only the Physician knows the whereabouts of Dr. Dores. Ms. Jailer, we need to meet with the Physician. It's important.

**狱卒**：请理解，囚犯们的胡言乱语并不能代表什么。\
**Jailer**: Listen, you really shouldn't take the inmates' ramblings too seriously.

思索至面前人的身份，狱卒仍然缓和了措辞。\
Considering the identity of the person before her, the jailer softens her tone.

**狱卒**：但……基金会的诸位，如果你们确实有此诉求，我可以稍后再次去询问。\
**Jailer**: But, if it's as critical as you say, I'll make another request later.

**狱卒**：只不过，接待的时间不会是近几天。\
**Jailer**: That said, I'm afraid the meeting won't happen for at least a few days.

**维尔汀**：我们明白了。\
**Vertin**: Understood.

**狱卒**：在此之前，我诚挚邀请诸位参与今日的科马拉议会。\
**Jailer**: For now, please join us for today's congress.

**虚构集**：看这里的阵仗，难道每天大厅中都要办一场文学沙龙吗？科马拉监狱简直就是作家的天堂……\
**Recoleta**: Spectacular! Do you hold literary salons like this every day? This place is practically a writer's paradise.

**虚构集**：奥克塔维奥小姐，又见面了。今天是你来主持吗？\
**Recoleta**: So, you're the host of the salon, Octavia?

**虚构集**：也许在沙龙上，我们能撇开成见，好好聊聊文学本身！\
**Recoleta**: I say we set aside our differences and have a titillating literary discussion!

**奥克塔维奥**：……你们来得正好。除了狱卒小姐外，我希望各位客人也能作为科马拉议会的公证人，就像法院的公民陪审团那样。\
**Octavia**: You've come at the right time. You may serve as witnesses for the congress alongside the jailer, like a citizens' jury in a court.

**狱卒**：很好，这的确是一个符合议会规则的提议。\
**Jailer**: Your suggestion aligns with the congressional rules. Very well.

**虚构集**：……？什么议会？什么公证人？\
**Recoleta**: Huh? Congress? Witnesses?

**虚构集**：这议会代表着什么？学科、流派、主义、语种还是叙事视角？\
**Recoleta**: Isn't this a salon? Which topic are we discussing? Literary theories, schools, principles, languages, oh, narrative perspectives?

**奥克塔维奥**：并非如此。\
**Octavia**: None of those.

奥克塔维奥低下头，深深地看了提问者一眼。\
Octavia lowers her head, giving her questioner a long and deep look.

**奥克塔维奥**：是命运的随机性，虚构集小姐。\
**Octavia**: This congress is about the randomness of fate, Ms. Recoleta.

**虚构集**：命运的……随机性？\
**Recoleta**: Randomness of fate?

在她陷入了迷惑与恍惚之时，狱卒的声音却前所未有地高昂了起来。\
As she sinks into confusion and bewilderment, the jailer's voice rises into a triumphant introduction.

**狱卒**：来自基金会的诸位官方职员，请让我为大家介绍“科马拉议会”。\
**Jailer**: Dear visitors from the Foundation, allow me to introduce the Comala Congress.

**狱卒**：昨日发生的暴乱只是一场短暂的意外。在科马拉实验性全景监狱中，囚犯们自发性的秩序才是常态。科马拉议会正是在这种状态下诞生的最佳写照！\
**Jailer**: What happened yesterday was merely a brief anomaly. In the Panopticon, spontaneous order among the inmates is the norm, and the Comala Congress serves as its truest reflection.

**维尔汀**：这是囚犯们自主治理的方式？\
**Vertin**: Spontaneous order?

**狱卒**：是的，囚犯们通过科马拉议会，分配精神药物、安排劳作场所、管理休憩时间。这一切都是自发的。\
**Jailer**: Yes. Through the congress, the inmates assign and distribute medication, communal duties, and rest periods. They are entirely self-regulated.

她的语气充满自豪。\
Her tone is filled with pride.

**奥克塔维奥**：我宣布，第七届科马拉议会正式开始！\
**Octavia**: I hereby announce the commencement of the seventh Comala Congress!

话音落下，奥克塔维奥取出一只残旧的彩票箱，以及一个捏在手上的小玩意儿。囚犯们像一个巨大的蚁群，井然有序地移动了起来。\
As her words fall, Octavia takes out a worn lottery box and a small trinket from her hand. The prisoners move in perfect order like a swarm of ants.

**十四行诗**：一个纸皮做成的箱子，和一只4面、6面、8面、10面、12面、14面……20个面的纸质骰子。\
**Sonetto**: A cardboard box and—is that a paper die? Hmm. It has 20 sides.

**虚构集**：……？\
**Recoleta**: ...?

**奥克塔维奥**：正如所有的历史学家一样，我们尊敬相仿的规律。正如所有的占星师一样，我们尊敬星轨的移动。\
**Octavia**: We carefully examine hidden patterns, much like an astute astrologer tracks the movements of the stars.

**虚构集**：这是……？！\
**Recoleta**: Isn't this ...?!

台下的女孩情不自禁地喃喃道。\
From somewhere in the audience, the girl unconsciously mumbles a revelation.

**虚构集**：就像，巴比伦之骰……？那个凝集作品主题的麦高芬，那个无穷无尽的命运共生体，那个将人类的时间压成干瘪圆圈的符号？\
**Recoleta**: Isn't this just like the Die of Babylon?! The MacGuffin that weaves through the entire plot, the infinite symbiote of fate, and the symbol that compresses time into a shriveled circle?

**奥克塔维奥**：容忍错误不等于否认命运的真实性。相反，它证实了命运的存在。如果您对此有疑问，不妨问问伟大的赫拉克利特吧！\
**Octavia**: What may seem like errors or accidents doesn't negate the verities of destiny. On the contrary, they affirm its very existence. Just ask the great Heraclitus!

**奥克塔维奥**：在无人观测的宇宙中，骰子将永不停止地旋转……\
**Octavia**: In an unobserved universe, the Die spins in perpetuity ...

**虚构集**：“在无限长又无限短的时间里，它将为所有人赋予命运”……？\
**Recoleta**: "Dictating the fate of all in time that is both infinitely long and infinitely short"?

**维尔汀**：……？！\
**Vertin**: ...?!

**囚犯们**：瞧，我已经闭上了眼睛！我尊重数字的偶然性，尊重命运的随机性，尊重骰子的决定。\
**Inmates**: Look, I've closed my eyes! I respect the randomness of numbers and destiny. I respect the Die's judgment.

在囚犯高亢的宣读中，原作者的声音却显得迟疑而滞涩。\
As the prisoners recite their announcements, the author's voice becomes more and more sluggish.

**虚构集**：“否则，我自愿迷失于时间的间隙中，成为永恒徘徊的幽灵。”\
**Recoleta**: "Otherwise, we will acquiescently lose ourselves in the gaps of time and wander forever as ghosts in oblivion."

**虚构集**：我已经无法理解眼前的一切了……\
**Recoleta**: I-I don't understand what's going on.

**虚构集**：但，好笑的是，我也许是那个最知道会发生什么的人。\
**Recoleta**: Oh, but the irony's that I probably have more idea what's going on than anyone here.

**维尔汀**：虚构集小姐，这些……全是你小说的内容吗？\
**Vertin**: Ms. Recoleta, this is all in your novel, isn't it?

**虚构集**：是的，无论是界限的咒语、历史学家、占星师还是赫拉克利特……\
**Recoleta**: I'm afraid so. The recitations, the references to an astrologer, and Heraclitus—they couldn't possibly be just a coincidence.

**虚构集**：难道说，接下来他们要让巴比伦之骰为一切赋予命运……？！\
**Recoleta**: Then, could it be? Will they look to the die to dictate their fate?

台下女孩们的震惊并没有影响到台上的一切，议会仍在继续着。\
The girls' audible shock does not affect the proceedings on stage; the congress continues.

**奥克塔维奥**：第一次抽签将由我进行，它首先决定了本次议会的代表顺序。\
**Octavia**: I shall perform the first roll. Its result will determine the subsequent roll order for this congress.

议会主持人将二十面骰抛入纸箱，并遵循某种节奏开始了摇晃。\
The hostess tosses the twenty-sided die into the cardboard box and begins shaking it rhythmically.

**奥克塔维奥**：投掷的结果是数字“5”。本次检定符合科马拉议会投掷准则中的初始先决条件，标准投掷顺序已被决定。\
**Octavia**: The result is 5. This check complies with the prerequisite conditions of the Ruling of the Die, and the standard roll order has been established.

**奥克塔维奥**：何塞先生，请上前来。\
**Octavia**: Inmate José, please come forth.

**奥克塔维奥**：作为团众中的先攻[Initiative]，你需要第一个接受命运的裁定。\
**Octavia**: You are the first in the initiative order. Therefore, fate's judgment shall fall upon you before all else.

**囚犯Ⅲ**：是我吗……好的，好的。\
**Inmate III**: Me? O-Okay ...

被点名的囚犯上前来，他接过那只仿佛随时就要破碎的彩票箱，晃动着，让那枚代表着荒唐命运的骰子在里面翻滚。\
The prisoner steps forward, taking the fragile box in his hands, shaking it to roll the die of absurd fate inside.

骰子停止了转动，就这样，一个简单的数字决定了这名囚犯接下来数十天的命运。\
The die stops, and just like that, a simple number decides his fate.

**囚犯Ⅲ**：是“17”！！太好了！！17是像沙丘之间的绿洲那样稀有的好数字！\
**Inmate III**: 17! It's 17! Ah, what a wonderful number, 17! Like an oasis in an endless desert!

**奥克塔维奥**：判定值为“6+4+4+3”。根据科马拉议会投掷准则，何塞的奖励是60片利培酮、40片氯氮平、40片地西泮。与此同时，他将擢升为科马拉议会的文化管理员。\
**Octavia**: The result is 17, and the score combination 6+4+4+3. According to the Ruling of the Die, he shall receive 60 risperidone tablets, 40 clozapine tablets, and 40 diazepam tablets. Additionally, he will assume the role of cultural manager of the Comala Congress.

**奥克塔维奥**：述职交接前，何塞需要在第一厕所完成为期七天的清扫任务。\
**Octavia**: Before he takes office, Inmate José must clean the first restroom for the next seven days.

**囚犯Ⅲ**：太……太好了！我早就有一个伟大的想法了！扫把在这里、清洁剂在这里、对了、还有马桶刷……\
**Inmate III**: W-Wonderful! I'll gladly clean the toilet! I've got the brooms here, the toilet detergent, oh, and the toilet brush, too!

**囚犯Ⅲ**：我要写一本《科马拉监狱亲历记》♪要与每位成员进行一对一会谈♪要记下他们文学的火花爆炸的瞬间♪……\
**Inmate III**: I have been waiting for this opportunity! As cultural manager, I will speak with every inmate and complete the Comala Memoir, finally capturing the moments when literary sparks ignite and explode.

**奥克塔维奥**：接下来是爱德华多先生，请上前来。\
**Octavia**: Next is Inmate Edoardo. Please come forth.

来者的面孔显然处于极度的精神紧张中。他的眼神闪烁不定，两撇眉毛在争夺眉心，牙齿也打着群架。\
The man in question is a nervous mess. His gaze flickers, his eyebrows fight for space on his forehead, and his teeth clash against each other in turmoil.

**囚犯Ⅳ**：可……可是，我忘记了判定的准则……我什么都不记得了！该死！\
**Inmate IV**: B-But I can't remember the Ruling of the Die. I can't remember anything. Damn it!

**囚犯Ⅳ**：很抱歉，奥克塔维奥小姐，我没有办法继续下去……！自从上次没有分配到药物后，我犯了好几次病，现在脑袋里塞不下任何一个字母……\
**Inmate IV**: Sorry, Ms. Octavia, but I-I don't think I can do this! I didn't get any medication in the last congress. I've had multiple episodes. It's like ... like my brain's jammed or something!

**奥克塔维奥**：别紧张，爱德华多，遵从投掷准则是整个环节中最容易的事情。来吧，把手放上来，我会协助你进行掷骰。\
**Octavia**: It's alright, Inmate Edoardo. It's easy. You don't need to know the rules to roll the Die. Give me your hand. I'll help you.

囚犯一脸惊恐地照做了。跟随悬于空中的双手摇晃箱子——那是他唯一能做的事。\
The prisoner follows suit, hands trembling as he shakes the box—the only thing he can do.

**奥克塔维奥**：我很遗憾，爱德华多。你必须自愿踏入下水道的污秽中，并在墙上写下一个你眼下最为焦虑的、作品主题的关键词。\
**Octavia**: My sincerest apologies, Inmate Edoardo. The Die dictates that you must voluntarily descend into the sewers and write the thematic keyword that currently causes you the most anxiety on the walls.

**囚犯Ⅳ**：我……非常感谢您，奥克塔维奥小姐……\
**Inmate IV**: I ... Th-Thank you very much, Ms. Octavia.

**囚犯Ⅳ**：只是我的脑袋要裂开了。我想我需要休息一会儿，再循着臭味去往下水道……\
**Inmate IV**: Agh. I think my head's about to split in half. I ... I need a moment to rest before I head down there ...

**囚犯Ⅳ**：然后，完成我的命运。\
**Inmate IV**: ... and fulfill my destiny.

捂着脑袋的囚犯离去了。他步伐沉重，一无所获，眉心却反而得以舒展。\
Clutching his head, the prisoner leaves. His steps heavy, his hands empty, but his brow finally falling at ease.

**虚构集**：等等……！狱卒小姐，他们是在以骰子来决定一切吗？\
**Recoleta**: Jailer, are you really letting them make every decision with the roll of a die?

**虚构集**：可爱德华多的病情看起来比何塞要严重多了，他才是那个最应该得到药物的人！\
**Recoleta**: Edoardo is clearly in a much more dire condition than José. The medication should've been given to him!

**狱卒**：我先前已经解释过，这是科马拉监狱自发诞生的高效管理模式。狱医阁下将一定数量的药物、食品等生活物资交由囚犯们，他们则通过自发的方式进行分配。\
**Jailer**: As I said, this is how the inmates of the Panopticon maintain order. The Physician periodically provides medication, food, and other necessities, and the inmates distribute them in this spontaneous and efficient manner.

**狱卒**：这当中不需要管理层的介入，也不涉及到暴力事件——这就是科马拉相较于世上所有监狱的不同之处。\
**Jailer**: Neither authority nor violence is involved in this process. This is what sets Comala apart from all other custodial facilities.

**虚构集**：而这一切……仅仅是因为“命运的随机性”吗？你们管那颗用纸皮糊成的骰子叫“命运”——这是哪门子的玩笑？\
**Recoleta**: Is that it? You abdicate all agency to the roll of a paper die and call it the "randomness of fate"? What kind of sick joke is this?!

**狱卒**：你需要冷静，虚构集小姐，这是囚犯们所共同认可的公平秩序。有时，我们必须正视它所带来的牺牲和代价。\
**Jailer**: Please calm down, Recoleta. This is the method that the inmates have collectively decided to recognize. They're prepared to face the possible sacrifices that it brings.

**狱卒**：……无论你我是否能理解，我们都不该干涉一项合理运行并卓有成效的规则。\
**Jailer**: This isn't about you or me. It's not our place to interfere with a procedure that has been proven both pragmatic and effective.

**狱卒**：我身为“狱卒”的职责是维持秩序，而你，虚构集小姐，你也不具备定义这一切的资格。\
**Jailer**: My duty is to assist the inmates in maintaining order through the methods that they have established, and yours is to witness their self-governance, not judge it.

狱卒深吸一口气。比起说服对方，她的话更是在说服自己。\
The jailer takes a deep breath. Her words clearly meant to convince herself as much as anyone listening.

**虚构集**：但是，如果这都在按照小说所运行，那一切都是早已被注定的……\
**Recoleta**: If everything somehow unfolds as it does in my novel, then every roll is already predetermined.

**虚构集**：维尔汀，你还记得我昨晚所提到的故事吗？巴比伦之骰的随机性中增加了一倍的幸运，也增加了一倍的罚码。\
**Recoleta**: Vertin, do you remember the story I told you last night? The odds of both success and failure were consecutively multiplied.

**维尔汀**：我有印象。\
**Vertin**: I remember.

**虚构集**：从一次简单的失败开始，命运将会像链式反应一样无止境地溃败下去。\
**Recoleta**: As soon as a character experiences a failure, they continue to suffer failures in an endless chain reaction.

**虚构集**：爱德华多在下次、下下次和往后的每一次，都永远无法掷出大于10的点数。\
**Recoleta**: None of Edoardo's future dice rolls will ever result in a number higher than 10.

**虚构集**：而且最终，由巴比伦之骰所掌控的一切，只会导向毁灭……\
**Recoleta**: At this rate, this system ... this Sociedad ruled by the Dice of Babylon, is bound to collapse.

她看了看周围，发现如此具有重量的话语，竟然没有得到任何人的注目——一个也没有。\
She looks around, realizing that her words—weighty as they seem to her—have garnered no attention.

**虚构集**：……总而言之，爱德华多这辈子都不会获得任何的药物。\
**Recoleta**: Edoardo will never receive any medication.

**虚构集**：按照巴比伦之骰倍数的惩罚，在墙上写下关键词的瞬间，他就会迎来自身的终局！\
**Recoleta**: The moment he writes the keyword on the wall could very well be the moment he spells out his own death!

**虚构集**：如果真的是这样，我得想办法改变这一切……！\
**Recoleta**: No, I can't let this happen. I have to do something!

虚构集冲向了讲台的方向。\
Recoleta rushes to the stage.

**狱卒**：等等，虚构集小姐！你要干什么？！\
**Jailer**: Wait, Ms. Recoleta! What are you doing?

## 9TH-11 先知、宇宙、造就 / Soothsayer, Worldmaker

主持台上，奥克塔维奥有条不紊地组织着科马拉议会的运行。\
On the stage, Octavia remains the picture of serenity as she orchestrates the congress.

**奥克塔维奥**：虚构集小姐，你可以提出你的疑惑或质疑，这是你作为公证人的权益。\
**Octavia**: Ms. Recoleta, as a witness to the congress, you have the right to express your doubts—calmly.

**虚构集**：你们……\
**Recoleta**: Listen, you—

她想到了同行青年的抱怨，想到了狱卒的否定之辞，想到了她所面对的每一位编辑的迷惑脸色。\
She recalls the complaints of her two former companions, the jailer's dismissals, and the confused expressions of every editor she has ever faced.

如果她将小说的一切和盘托出，那也许只会收获一模一样的反应。\
If she were to lay out every detail of her novel here and now, she would only get the same response.

**虚构集**：……不，没什么。我也想要进行你们神圣的投掷仪式。请问我能加入吗？\
**Recoleta**: *huff* No, it's nothing. It's just that I'd like to participate in the dice-rolling ceremony. May I?

**奥克塔维奥**：当然！只要你身处科马拉监狱之中，那就证明了你与监狱的命运具有共通性。\
**Octavia**: Of course! The very fact that you're standing here in the Panopticon proves that you share a common fate with it.

初来乍到的青年作家，环视四周等待投掷的囚犯。他们面色平静，等待着命运的降临，前人的惊喜与噩运并没有影响这条蜿蜒的队列丝毫。\
Recoleta surveys the prisoners waiting to cast their die. Their expressions are serene, untroubled, calmly awaiting their fate. The joys and misfortunes of those before them do not affect the long, winding queue in the slightest.

她深吸一口气。\
She takes a deep breath.

**虚构集**：如果这一切都是全然随机的命运，那么我加入队列的时机并不会影响投掷的结果，对吗？\
**Recoleta**: It doesn't matter when I roll the Die, since the rolls are simply a reflection of the randomness of fate, right?

**奥克塔维奥**：当然。\
**Octavia**: Precisely.

**虚构集**：我要在第二十七位囚犯完成投掷之后加入，可以吗？\
**Recoleta**: Then, I'd like to perform my roll after the 27th inmate. Is that alright?

**奥克塔维奥**：如你所愿，虚构集小姐。\
**Octavia**: As you wish, Ms. Recoleta.

**奥克塔维奥**：你拥有很好的运气，科马拉的命运在眷顾你，虚构集小姐。\
**Octavia**: It seems fate favors you, Ms. Recoleta.

**奥克塔维奥**：这是属于你的药品与物资，请拿好。\
**Octavia**: Here are your supplies.

**奥克塔维奥**：请务必遵守议会的分配规定，这是所有人共通的信念，也是维持科马拉运作最重要的部分。\
**Octavia**: Please be sure to follow the distribution rules of the congress. This is an essential structure of Comala and a belief shared by all its inmates. Honor it.

**虚构集**：这一切果然……如我所料。\
**Recoleta**: Just as I suspected.

**虚构集**：奥克塔维奥小姐，既然这是我得到的东西，我想我有权处置它。\
**Recoleta**: These supplies belong to me now, Octavia. I'm free to use them however I please.

获得了个人胜利的女孩，走向蜷缩在不远处角落的爱德华多。在投掷结束后，他一直抱着头，躯体无声颤抖着。\
Recoleta strides toward Edoardo, who has curled up in a distant corner, clutching his head, as his body trembles in silence.

**虚构集**：爱德华多先生，我将我得到的东西都赠送给你。\
**Recoleta**: Here, Edoardo, take them.

**囚犯Ⅳ**：……？\
**Inmate IV**: ...?

**囚犯Ⅳ**：可……可是，我还没有完成我的命运。\
**Inmate IV**: B-But I haven't fulfilled my destiny yet.

**囚犯Ⅳ**：这些珍贵的圆片和五彩的胶囊……它们并不属于我，它们是命运馈赠给您的礼物。\
**Inmate IV**: These precious tablets and capsules ... I can't accept them. They are gifts from fate. The Die has placed them in your palm.

**虚构集**：这些药对我来说没有用，我觉得你才是最需要它们的人。\
**Recoleta**: But I don't need them; you do.

**囚犯Ⅳ**：谢谢你，善良的小姐……\
**Inmate IV**: Th-Thank you, kind miss.

囚犯的颤抖停止了，他呆滞地掐了掐自己的手臂，仿佛在分辨梦境。\
The prisoner's trembling stops. He blankly pinches his arm, as if trying to distinguish reality from dream.

随后，他猛地把对方手中的药物抢过，疯狂地塞入嘴中。\
Then, all at once, he snatches the medication from her hands and shoves it into his mouth.

**虚构集**：……爱德华多先生？你怎么了？你……你现在就需要吃药吗？\
**Recoleta**: Edoardo?! What's wrong? A-Are you taking the medicine right now?

**虚构集**：请不要着急，我会把剩下的药物都给你的！\
**Recoleta**: There's no need to rush. There's plenty of it. You can have it all.

**囚犯Ⅰ**：你可真是该死，爱德华多！这是来自命运的馈赠，你怎么能如此挥霍！\
**Inmate I**: For goodness' sake, Edoardo! How could you squander fate's gifts like this?

**囚犯Ⅰ**：善良的小姐！请将您的药物赠予我吧……我才是那个最需要它们的人！\
**Inmate I**: Kind miss, please, give me the medication. I need them more than anyone else.

**囚犯Ⅱ**：不，不，是我！给我吧，善良的小姐，将您的药物给我！求求您了！\
**Inmate II**: No, I'm the one who needs them most. Give me the medication. I beg of you.

**囚犯Ⅱ**：我很久没有睡过一个安稳的觉了！有了护身符[Amuleto]，那些该死的幽灵今晚一定会放过我的，这监狱的地板也不会再震动了。\
**Inmate II**: With the protection of these amulets, I might finally be able to get a peaceful night's sleep, no more trembling floors and wailing ghosts.

囚犯们推搡着、扭打着，许多只手朝无助的访客伸去，试图撷取她手中那些代表着救赎的小小圆片。\
The prisoners shove and struggle, countless hands reaching toward the hapless writer, trying to snatch the small round pills of salvation.

**奥克塔维奥**：够了……都停下！\
**Octavia**: Enough! Enough!!

青色的光芒使囚犯们都不约而同地抱头蹲下，骚乱停止了。\
A blue glow spreads through the room, forcing the prisoners to clutch their heads and fall down to their knees. Their riot comes to an abrupt halt.

**奥克塔维奥**：……你不该这么做的，虚构集小姐。\
**Octavia**: You shouldn't have done that, Ms. Recoleta.

**奥克塔维奥**：你一无所知，却又盲目善良。你的一次布施就会摧毁我们赖以生存的一切。\
**Octavia**: Your ignorant generosity could shatter the very basis of our survival.

她走至痛苦的爱德华多面前，将他脚边遗落的几颗胶囊捡了起来。\
She steps toward Edoardo, now writhing in pain, and picks up a few stray capsules scattered at his feet.

药片化作一阵虚无的沙砾，从她的指尖消散了。\
The pills dissolve into a stream of voided sand, vanishing as it pours through her fingers.

**奥克塔维奥**：在此之前，我们从未发生过这样的骚乱，我们用命运的随机性来决定药品与物资的分配，安排大家的劳作。\
**Octavia**: We have never had such chaos at the congress. Understand this: We rely only on the randomness of fate to distribute supplies and assign responsibilities.

**奥克塔维奥**：一旦你打破了其中一项，这个监狱的制度就会陷入彻底的溃败，它将不复存在。\
**Octavia**: If you disrupt this status quo, the entire system of the Panopticon will collapse beyond repair.

**奥克塔维奥**：我们遵从命运扑朔迷离的规律，遵从巴比伦之骰法则，才将监狱秩序维持至今。\
**Octavia**: It is only by respecting the arbitrariness of fate and adhering to the rules of the Die of Babylon that we have kept this place functioning all this time.

**虚构集**：巴比伦之骰……？！\
**Recoleta**: The Die of Babylon?!

**虚构集**：告诉我，你是从哪里得知这个名字的？！难道是你在操纵这一切吗？\
**Recoleta**: Tell me, how did you know this name? Are you the one orchestrating this whole thing?

女孩茫然又愤怒地抓住了主持人的衣领，如同在阻止她逃离一般。\
Recoleta, equally confused and furious, grabs the hostess's collar.

**虚构集**：难道，难道维尔汀的猜测是对的……你就是阿莱夫？\
**Recoleta**: C-Could it be? Are you Aleph, just as Vertin suspected?

**奥克塔维奥**：放手，虚构集小姐，你怎么也像他们一样发疯？\
**Octavia**: Let go of me, Ms. Recoleta! Have you gone mad?

**奥克塔维奥**：骰子是全然随机的，我并没有任何背后的操纵举动。我以过去与未来的作家生涯起誓过，我绝不会违背我在科马拉议会开始前的誓言。\
**Octavia**: The roll of the Die is absolutely random. I'm not orchestrating anything. Before the congress began, I made an oath. I intend to keep it.

**维尔汀**：冷静些，虚构集小姐。奥克塔维奥小姐并不像在撒谎。\
**Vertin**: Please, calm down, Ms. Recoleta. I think she's telling the truth.

她像是忽然回过神来一般松开了手。\
She lets go of her grip as the reality of their situation dawns on her.

**虚构集**：我很抱歉……奥克塔维奥小姐。只是，请你务必如实告诉我，你是如何得知巴比伦之骰的？\
**Recoleta**: S-Sorry, Octavia, but, please, you have to tell me how you learned about the Die of Babylon.

**虚构集**：这应该是只有我笔友知晓的故事……这对我来说真的很重要。\
**Recoleta**: I must know. Only my pen pal and I should have any knowledge about this die.

**奥克塔维奥**：……这是狱医先生告诉我的概念，它是一种存在于集体意识中的象征体。我们只要能够借用它，就能让科马拉处于完美的秩序之中。\
**Octavia**: I heard about it from the Physician. He described it as a symbol of collective consciousness that we could harness to maintain immaculate order in the Panopticon.

**奥克塔维奥**：至于科马拉议会，它来自狱医先生在此基础上提出的一种天才式设想。后来，它经过了数次修改，才真正落实为一个合理的方案。\
**Octavia**: The Comala Congress was coined, iterated, and perfected by the Physician based on this concept.

**维尔汀**：又是狱医。看来我们的推测无误，这一切果然和幕后的这个人有关联。\
**Vertin**: The Physician again. Everything eventually leads back to him, just as we suspected.

**虚构集**：原来如此……\
**Recoleta**: I see.

虚构集看向从头到尾一直不作声的美洲豹，大型捕食者只是默默地注视着这一切的发生。\
Recoleta casts her eyes over to the silent jaguar, who has remained wordless from beginning to end, watching it all unfold.

**虚构集**：狱卒小姐，我们现在就要见到那位狱医本人。\
**Recoleta**: Jailer, we have to meet with the Physician in person, now.

**狱卒**：我已经告诉过诸位多次了，梅林先生现在非常繁忙，不便于接待。\
**Jailer**: As I've told you many times, Dr. Merlin is too busy at the moment.

**狱卒**：关于虚构集的小说和笔友……这种无稽之谈无法成为打扰梅林先生工作的理由。\
**Jailer**: I couldn't possibly trouble him over a novel and a pen pal. They're just fantasies.

**维尔汀**：狱卒小姐，请您再考虑一下。\
**Vertin**: Couldn't you make an exception?

**维尔汀**：如果这一切，并不是无稽之谈，而是和监狱的存亡有着直接关系呢？\
**Vertin**: What if they're not just fantasies? What if they're tied to the very survival of this place?

**维尔汀**：刚刚虚构集小姐提到过，由巴比伦之骰所掌控的一切，最终只会导向毁灭。\
**Vertin**: Ms. Recoleta said the Panopticon could collapse because of the Die of Babylon.

**狱卒**：您的意思是，您相信虚构集所说的那些胡话……？\
**Jailer**: Are you seriously telling me you believe that nonsense?

**虚构集**：那些并不是胡话。你也亲眼看到我在投掷中取得胜利了！\
**Recoleta**: It wasn't nonsense, nor are they fantasies! You saw with your own eyes how I won the die roll!

**狱卒**：……那只是一个巧合。\
**Jailer**: It was just a coincidence.

她的态度将信将疑。基金会的调查员们马上意识到，现在是一个施压的好机会。\
The jailer's words are at odds with the subtle motions of her eyes and face. The Foundation's investigators seize on a prime opportunity to apply pressure.

**维尔汀**：狱卒小姐，如果我们能拿出更有力的证据呢？\
**Vertin**: What if we present you with stronger evidence to prove it's more than just a coincidence?

**维尔汀**：如果科马拉监狱中的一切，确实按照虚构集小姐的小说在进行，那么她应该可以预测接下来发生的事情。\
**Vertin**: If everything in the Panopticon proceeds according to Ms. Recoleta's novel, as she says, she should be able to predict what happens next.

**维尔汀**：包括那枚“具有绝对随机性”的骰子。\
**Vertin**: Including the roll results of the "absolutely random" Die.

**虚构集**：当然，因为巴比伦之骰并不是随机性的代表。它是一场宿命论的骗局，一个令人无可奈何的历史闭环。\
