**Recoleta**: That's right! The Die of Babylon isn't random at all. It's nothing but a supercilious fraud veiled under the guise of fate, an enactor of the inescapable loop of history, and—

**虚构集**：我觉得，你们根本就没人听我说话……算了，这就是一个没有人会听不知名作家说话的时代。\
**Recoleta**: And not one of you is paying attention to me whatsoever. Ugh, to hell with this era of ignoring unknown writers.

**维尔汀**：虚构集小姐，请你在狱卒小姐面前，预测接下来囚犯们的投掷结果。\
**Vertin**: Ms. Recoleta, please make your prediction for the next inmate's die roll.

**维尔汀**：这样就能向狱卒小姐证明，你的小说《理性家族的崛起与衰落》同监狱的联系。\
**Vertin**: This way, you can prove to Ms. Jailer the irrefutable connection between Comala and your novel, The Rise and Fall of Sanity.

**虚构集**：我很欣慰你至少记住了它的名字，维尔汀。\
**Recoleta**: You finally remembered its name! Oh, what sweet balm to my spirit!

**维尔汀**：为了证明虚构集小姐所言属实，奥克塔维奥小姐，请您继续主持科马拉议会，让下一位囚犯开始投掷。\
**Vertin**: Ms. Octavia, please continue the congress, and let the next inmate perform their roll. Then Ms. Recoleta's statement will be proven true.

主持人对此不置可否。\
The hostess of the congress remains noncommittal.

**奥克塔维奥**：感谢你的提醒。尽管已经遭受了如此粗鲁的打断，但科马拉议会必须进行下去——当然，那绝不会是为了虚构集小姐。\
**Octavia**: I appreciate the reminder. No matter the interruption, the Comala Congress must go on, though not for Ms. Recoleta's sake, of course.

**奥克塔维奥**：请下一位议会成员上前来进行投掷。\
**Octavia**: Next inmate, please.

按照骰子所规定的顺序，下一名投掷的囚犯走上前来。\
Following the die's designated order, the next prisoner steps forward to roll.

**奥克塔维奥**：你好，加西亚先生，你应该很熟悉这套流程了。\
**Octavia**: Hello, Inmate García. You know what to do.

**加西亚**：当然。\
**García**: Of course.

**虚构集**：“第六面，一根断裂的石柱，一个运气与灾厄的交汇之点。”\
**Recoleta**: "The 6th face. A broken pillar. The conflux of fortune and calamity."

**虚构集**：所以，下一位囚犯会获得的数字是6。\
**Recoleta**: So, the result of the next roll will be a 6.

准确无误的预言让触发事件之厅陷入了彻底的沉默。\
Her prophetic precision plunges the Hall of New Encounters into breathless silence.

**奥克塔维奥**：……我们得到的命运是数字6。\
**Octavia**: As fate reveals, the number is 6.

**维尔汀**：得到的数字确实如虚构集小姐所说。\
**Vertin**: Just as Ms. Recoleta predicted.

**狱卒**：再来一次。我怎么会相信这种巧合般的儿戏……\
**Jailer**: That could still be a coincidence. Do it again.

**虚构集**：“第十三面，隐秘而无尽的变奏曲。令人心境紊乱的是，它显然不具备实际的开头与结尾。”\
**Recoleta**: "The 13th face. A bewildering cadenza lacking a true beginning or end."

**虚构集**：“第四面，快溺亡的人用尽力气游向水底，却发现自己将一面镜子当成了水面。”\
**Recoleta**: "The 4th face. A drowning man used the last of his strength to swim to safety, only to discover he'd mistaken a mirror for the surface of the water."

**虚构集**：“第十七面，沙丘之间的绿洲，微微的湿气和诡秘的宁静让他意识到，那是一座不属于现世的幻影之城。”\
**Recoleta**: "The 17th face. He limped toward the distant oasis, only for the faint moisture and eerie stillness to cruelly reveal it as a mirage."

**虚构集**：“第六面，又是一根断裂的石柱，裂痕一模一样。它证实了能量扰动学家的猜测，那是一片环形的废墟。”……\
**Recoleta**: "The 6th face. Another broken pillar, with identical cracks to the last. It confirmed the Paracausality Researcher's hypothesis—this place used to be a circular building."

**虚构集**：这样足够了吗？这一节已经快要念完了……\
**Recoleta**: Is that enough? I've almost finished the entire chapter.

**奥克塔维奥**：这……这不可能……\
**Octavia**: It's not possible.

一次又一次“巧合般的儿戏”让人群喧闹了起来。\
One "coincidence" after another begins to stir into an uproar.

巧合仿佛无穷无尽。\
The coincidences appear endless.

**奥克塔维奥**：……！你……你到底是谁？\
**Octavia**: Who are you?

**虚构集**：我很抱歉……但我一早就告诉过你了，奥克塔维奥小姐。\
**Recoleta**: I'm sorry if this comes as a shock to you, but I did warn you, Octavia.

**虚构集**：巴比伦之骰所代表的，并不是命运的随机性。\
**Recoleta**: Now, it's proven. The Die of Babylon is anything but the so-called "randomness of fate."

**奥克塔维奥**：……你是神的使者，还是掌握古老预言术的霍比族祭司？\
**Octavia**: Have you been sent here by some god, or are you a Hopi prophet?

**奥克塔维奥**：你带着这样的消息前来，是为了拯救我们，还是击溃我们的世界？\
**Octavia**: Have you brought this knowledge to save us, or to shatter our beliefs, our world?

一个注定不需要答案的问题。她无所适从地望着手中的纸皮箱子与二十面骰——此刻，它们显得那样滑稽可笑。\
A question destined never to need an answer. She lets her eyes fall into the cardboard box and onto the twenty-sided die. The ridiculousness of its nature becomes starkly visible.

**奥克塔维奥**：你们究竟是什么东西的拙劣仿制品？我们又是什么？这座监狱到底是什么？\
**Octavia**: What is this thing in my hand? What are we? What is this prison?

**狱卒**：无论是巫术、神秘术还是什么更未知的力量……这太不可思议了。\
**Jailer**: I don't know if it's some kind of sorcery or arcane skill, but it's unfathomable.

**狱卒**：我会带你们去见狱医，但这不是因为我答应了你们的请求，而是因为这一切都已经超出了我的预料。\
**Jailer**: I'll take you to the Physician. Not because of your earlier request, but because the situation has escalated beyond my means.

**狱卒**：你们需要得到来自科马拉监狱管理者本人的专业裁决。\
**Jailer**: The overseer of the Panopticon will decide how to handle your situation.

**维尔汀**：虚构集小姐，没想到你真的能做到这样的事情。\
**Vertin**: To be honest, Ms. Recoleta. I wasn't sure you'd be able to correctly predict everything.

**十四行诗**：司辰，难道在此之前，您都只是在误打误撞地尝试吗……？\
**Sonetto**: Timekeeper, are you saying that you risked everything on a hunch?

**维尔汀**：但我们成功了。\
**Vertin**: It worked, didn't it?

**狱卒**：诸位，梅林先生就在中央瞭望塔的某个位置。请随我来。\
**Jailer**: Come with me. Dr. Merlin's office is in the central tower.

大展身手的女孩则跟在队伍的最后，没有任何话语能钻进她高速思考的脑袋里。\
For her part, the now vindicated writer follows at the end of the line, letting her mind race like a bullet train.

**虚构集**：如果继续下去，在第六版故事修改中，小镇中的所有人最后都会因为巴比伦之骰而死去……因为只有死亡能够达成历史闭环。\
**Recoleta**: In the sixth version of my novel, everyone in the town dies because of the Die of Babylon, for only death can close the loop of history.

**虚构集**：而你，狱卒小姐，你就是银行职员对吗？\
**Recoleta**: And Jailer, you're the Bank Clerk, right?

**虚构集**：……所以最后，你会像银行职员一样，因为发现自己与沙漠捕鱼人是同一个人而崩溃吗？\
**Recoleta**: So, in the end, will you also have a meltdown, like the Bank Clerk does, when he realizes that he and the Dune Piscator are the same person?

**虚构集**：如果这一切都与《理性家族的崛起与衰落》有关，那我才是撰写它的人……\
**Recoleta**: If all of this is tied to The Rise and Fall of Sanity, then, as its creator ...

**虚构集**：我会搞清楚这一切的。\
**Recoleta**: I will get to the bottom of this.

## 9TH-12 台前，幕后 / Behind the Operating Curtain

看似整洁的室内密布着细小的划痕和难以辨别的污渍，令人感到压抑。空气中弥漫着微弱的消毒水味道，其中混杂着潮湿的霉气。\
An otherwise tidy room is covered in fine scratches and small unidentifiable stains. The smell of disinfectant lingers in the air, mixed with mildew.

**狱卒**：请诸位在此稍等片刻。\
**Jailer**: Wait here a moment.

**狱卒**：梅林先生应当正在忙碌中。就诸位的拜访诉求，我会将情况完整地向他汇报。\
**Jailer**: I'll report the situation and your request to Dr. Merlin.

**狱卒**：我不能保证梅林先生一定会接见各位，但……我会尽力让他改变主意。\
**Jailer**: However, since he's always busy, I can't guarantee he'll agree to meet you, but I'll do my best to persuade him.

美洲豹的身影无声息地消失在办公室内间的门后。\
The jaguar's figure slinks out through the inner door.

**维尔汀**：现在是个好时机，十四行诗。\
**Vertin**: Now's our chance, Sonetto.

**十四行诗**：司辰，您的意思是？\
**Sonetto**: Our chance? What do you mean, Timekeeper?

**维尔汀**：想让狱卒小姐批准我们搜查瞭望塔并不是一件易事。我觉得我们应该主动出击，寻找任何有用的线索。\
**Vertin**: It's unlikely that the jailer will let us search the central tower, even in this situation. We should take the initiative and look for clues while she's away.

**十四行诗**：我明白了，司辰……我会尽力的！\
**Sonetto**: I-I see, Timekeeper. I will do my best.

第一助手迅速开始了违规的搜查。\
Sonetto swiftly conducts a thoroughly unauthorized search.

**维尔汀**：感谢你的协助，虚构集小姐。如果不是你所展现的神奇预测，我们很难说服狱卒小姐改变主意。\
**Vertin**: Thank you for your assistance, Ms. Recoleta. Without your precise predictions, we wouldn't be standing here now.

**维尔汀**：虽然我仍未弄明白这一切如何与骰子、与你的小说扯上联系，但——\
**Vertin**: I haven't yet grasped the connection between the Die, your novel, and what's happening in this place, but ...

**维尔汀**：哪怕是根据排除法，我们也几乎可以断定：你的笔友阿莱夫就在这扇门的背后。\
**Vertin**: By process of elimination, it's almost certain that your pen pal, Aleph, is right behind this door.

**虚构集**：……有时候，我很佩服你的果断，维尔汀。我想应该有很多人和你说过，你是一个很特别的人。\
**Recoleta**: Sometimes I envy your decisiveness, Vertin. I'm sure many people have praised the special talent of yours.

**维尔汀**：你还好吗？看起来你似乎不如刚刚进入监狱那般兴奋。\
**Vertin**: Are you alright? You don't seem as excited as when we first entered Comala.

虚构集看向紧闭的大门，她并不确定自己是否希望它会在下一秒打开。\
Recoleta holds her gaze on the tightly shut door, uncertain whether she hopes it will open now or ever again.

**虚构集**：如果那个在瞭望塔中操纵一切的视线真的是阿莱夫——\
**Recoleta**: The all-seeing sentinel of the Panopticon, veiled within the central tower ... If it truly is Aleph, I—

**虚构集**：这是一个可怕的猜想，我暂时还不知道该怎么去面对它。\
**Recoleta**: I don't know how to face such a terrifying and increasingly plausible reality.

**十四行诗**：很抱歉打断了你们的谈话——但司辰，我想您需要看看这个。\
**Sonetto**: Sorry to interrupt, but, Timekeeper, I think you'll want to see these.

**维尔汀**：落款兀尔德——这是德洛丝女士留下的信。\
**Vertin**: Signed "Urd." This is a letter from Dr. Dores.

轻盈的签名字迹，同稿件收纳册上的一致。\
The delicate signature matches the one in the manuscript folder.

**虚构集**：她的字迹和我想象中一样漂亮。这封信是写给谁的？\
**Recoleta**: Her handwriting—It's as beautiful as I'd imagined. Who is it addressed to?

**虚构集**：“阿莱夫阁下亲启”……？！\
**Recoleta**: "Dear Mr. Aleph ..." Aleph?!

**维尔汀**：是的，这是德洛丝女士与阿莱夫来往的信件。\
**Vertin**: Looks like Dores and Aleph are acquaintances. Or, at least, they've had some correspondence.

**维尔汀**：“敬爱的阿莱夫阁下亲启。初次通信，冒昧叨扰。我是科马拉监狱中的囚犯之一，名叫德洛丝。如今，我以笔名‘兀尔德’来信，向您请教问题。”\
**Vertin**: "Dear Mr. Aleph, my apologies if this reaches you at an inconvenient time. I am Dores, pen name 'Urd,' an ordinary inmate of the Panopticon of Comala. I write seeking your guidance, if you wouldn't mind offering it to me."

**德洛丝**：“我从狱医梅林先生那儿听说——”\
**Dores**: "I heard from the Physician, Dr. Merlin, that ..."

**德洛丝**：您能回答人们向您询问的所有问题。类似的说法，理想家与其他囚犯的只言片语中同样有所耳闻。\
**Dores**: You have the answer to every question—a statement which has been echoed by the Idealist and the other inmates.

**德洛丝**：您是科马拉监狱的典狱长，是隐秘的投资者，还是隐藏在背后的权力意志？您真的是科马拉的至高存在吗？\
**Dores**: I have something I wish to ask you. What exactly is your role at the prison? Chief warden? A secret backer? An observer who dominates the prison? Are you truly the supreme ruler of the Panopticon of Comala?

她们迫不及待地将下一封信拆开。\
They tear open the next letter, eager to read on.

**阿莱夫**：敬爱的兀尔德女士：\
**Aleph**: Dear Urd,

**阿莱夫**：恐怕这些猜测都不准确，我不过是一名选择自囚于此的囚徒罢了。然而，既然您有疑问，我确实可以作答。\
**Aleph**: I do indeed have answers for every question, including yours. I'm afraid every one of your speculations is off the mark. I am merely an inmate who chose to imprison himself here.

**阿莱夫**：且允许我先指出一项事实：您的身份并不如您自称那般普通。您是科马拉的囚犯，也是重塑之手的客人。是什么让您对监狱中的一切起了兴趣？\
**Aleph**: And allow me to point out that your identity isn't as ordinary as you claim. Why is it that you, my fellow inmate and guest of Manus Vindictae, are so interested in Comala?

**维尔汀**：德洛丝女士是重塑之手的……客人？\
**Vertin**: Dr. Dores, a guest of Manus Vindictae?

突然之间，器皿碎裂的声响打断了书信的阅读。\
A muffled shattering of glass interrupts their reading.

**十四行诗**：这是门后传来的声音……怎么回事？他们还好吗？\
**Sonetto**: It came from inside the room. Do you think they're okay?

**虚构集**：狱卒小姐——狱医先生——！请问里面发生了什么事！\
**Recoleta**: The jailer and the Physician! What happened?

大门一如既往地沉默着，执行着封锁与扭曲的意志，无人应答。\
The door defies any attempt at an answer, sealing all the events from view.

**维尔汀**：他们也许发生了什么意外。我们直接进去看看吧。\
**Vertin**: I'm not sure, but it could be bad. Come on. Let's go in and see if they're alright.

并未上锁的大门通向了一个破旧而压抑的小房间。\
The unlocked door leads to another room, more decrepit and oppressive than the last.

一张冰冷的手术台摆放在房间中央，四周堆满了零散的药品与医疗器具。\
A cold operating table lies in the center, surrounded by scattered bottles and medical instruments.

**维尔汀**：我想，我们也许误入了狱医的工作地点……\
**Vertin**: It seems we've stumbled upon the Physician's—

**虚构集**：我早该想到的，狱医的工作地点……但这种鬼地方是手术室？！\
**Recoleta**: The Physician's office. I should've known. But, is this an operating room?

**虚构集**：这里简直是这座监狱中最怪异的地方……\
**Recoleta**: As if this prison wasn't bizarre enough already.

狭窄的手术室内，突如其来的闯入者让美洲豹惊慌失措起来。\
Inside the narrow operating room, the jaguar reacts badly to their intrusion.

**狱卒**：你们怎么能私自闯进来？我不是告诉过诸位，请在外面等候吗？！\
**Jailer**: Didn't I tell you to wait outside? What do you think you're doing, barging in like this?

**虚构集**：我们只是在担心你的情况，狱卒小姐。\
**Recoleta**: We were just worried about your safety, Jailer.

**狱卒**：别说了，快离开这里——\
**Jailer**: Enough. Get out of—

**？？？**：安静！\
**???**: Quiet!

**狱医**：在一开始，爬虫脑[Reptilian Complex]主导着一切。\
**The Physician**: The reptilian complex governs all our fundamental functions.

**狱医**：我们像所有的爬虫与鸟类一样，遵循着典型的本能生存：心跳、呼吸、攻击、逃跑，拥有了领地与等级意识。\
**The Physician**: Our heartbeat, breathing, fight-or-flight responses, and our territory and hierarchy awareness—our primitive ancestors, like reptiles and birds, followed such instincts to survive.

**狱医**：进化使我们获得了边缘系统[Limbic System]。\
**The Physician**: Through millions of years of evolution, we developed the limbic system.

**狱医**：它处理着我们的行为与记忆，使我们产生对快乐的追求，同时带来了恐惧、痛苦、忧虑与愤怒。一切得以被蒙上意志的色彩。\
**The Physician**: This processes emotions and forms memories. It allows us to feel—fear, sadness, anger, joy—our behaviors are given "meaning."

**狱医**：在最后，却是新皮质[Neocortex]占据了我们脑容量的三分之二。\
**The Physician**: Now, it's the neocortex that makes up more than two-thirds of our total brain volume.

**狱医**：语言与感知、逻辑推理、抽象的能力，构成了人性与行为的多维。我们阅读创作，认知世界与自我，定下一个又一个的目标——\
**The Physician**: Language, perception, logical reasoning, abstract thought—this is what forms the complexity of human nature. We read, create, perceive. We try to understand both the world and ourselves. We are forever setting goals, one after another.

**狱医**：而这一切，不过都发生在颅骨内的方寸之地中，在这弯曲拥挤的脑皮层里。\
**The Physician**: And all this—these multitudes—happens within the confines of the skull, in the tight folds of the crowded cerebral cortex.

**维尔汀**：他是在……做手术？！\
**Vertin**: Is he performing surgery?

**狱医**：一个精密的、让人迷惑的、容易损坏的器官……\
**The Physician**: Such a delicate and elaborate organ.

**狱医**：如果它再也不能遗忘，它会变成什么模样——\
**The Physician**: Were it unable to forget, what would come of it?

**狱医**：这个巴掌大的房间，能同时容纳数十个人吗？\
**The Physician**: Can this space, no larger than the palm of my hand, truly accommodate dozens of people at once?

终于，狱医放下了组织剪与持针器，昭示着手术的结束。然而破旧冰冷的机器也同时发出警告，生命的曲线正在逐渐拉直。\
At last, the Physician sets down his operating scissors and needle, signaling the end of the surgery. Yet at the same time, the old machine issues an alarm, signaling that his patient's vital signs are wavering.

**虚构集**：台上的病人，他……发生了什么事情？他看起来不太好！\
**Recoleta**: What's happened to the patient? It looks like he's dying.

没有人回答她急切的问话。屏幕上，最后一丝波浪形的室颤与室扑也消失了，室内只余恒长的警报声。\
Her anxiety rises as the question goes unanswered. On the screen, the last waveforms disappear, leaving only a constant flat tone.

**虚构集**：手术，失败了吗……？\
**Recoleta**: Did the surgery fail?

**狱医**：荒谬！手术当然成功了。\
**The Physician**: Nonsense! The surgery was a tremendous success.

**狱医**：我帮助他消除了令他困苦的癔症，同时光复了科马拉监狱的秩序。\
**The Physician**: I have erased his debilitating hysteria and restored order to the Panopticon.

**狱医**：你们闯入这里想干什么？\
**The Physician**: What are you trying to achieve by barging in here?

手术台后的男子看向不请自来的访客，但并没有给她们回答的机会。\
The man behind the operating table stares at the uninvited guests expectantly but does not give them a chance to respond.

**狱医**：算了，下一台手术马上就要开始了。\
**The Physician**: Forget it. The next operation requires my attention.

**狱医**：狱卒，马上带她们出去。15分钟后将下一位病患带进来。\
**The Physician**: Jailer, show them out. Bring me the next patient in 15 minutes.

**狱卒**：……很抱歉，但维尔汀小姐，请你们现在就离开吧。\
**Jailer**: I'm sorry, Ms. Vertin. I'm afraid you have to leave now.

她上前一步，拦在了众人的面前，语气几乎是恳求的。\
Recoleta steps forward, blocking their path. There is a hint of pleading in her voice.

**虚构集**：拜托了，只需要一分钟的时间！我有非常重要的事情问你——\
**Recoleta**: Please, just let us speak with you! It'll only take a moment! I have something very important I need to ask.

她的提问还未成形，就被狱医毫不留情地打断了。\
Her question is not given time to take shape.

**狱医**：重要？没有什么比我在科马拉所做的实验更重要。\
**The Physician**: Important? Nothing is of greater importance than my experiments in the Panopticon, outsiders.

**狱医**：外来者们，为了维持实验的长久进行，时间的稳定性必须超越一切。\
**The Physician**: To ensure they continue, the stability of time and schedule is absolutely paramount.

**虚构集**：科马拉的实验……？！科马拉监狱的幕后控制者，果然就是你吗？\
**Recoleta**: Experiments in the Panopticon? So you really are the controller of the prison, then?

**狱医**：控制者？真是一个老旧而幼稚的说法。\
**The Physician**: Controller? What an outdated notion—superficial, really.

**狱医**：一切都是自发的、非个性化的权力，由谁来行使根本无关紧要。控制者无处不在，却从不使用物质手段——建筑本身才是维系一切的关键。\
**The Physician**: The Panopticon has no need for such a power. Regardless of who occupies the central tower—or even if no one's there at all—every inmate is both the observer and the observed, both wielders and subjects of power.

**狱医**：所有人都是那个匿名的观察者，而科马拉监狱不过是一个模版罢了。\
**The Physician**: Achieving such a state requires no physical or violent measures; the structure of the Panopticon itself is the mechanism which sustains it. Comala is simply a manifestation of this model.

**狱医**：一旦我验证了这种模式的可行，只需要做一些必要的修改，它就能套用在任何职能的场所中。\
**The Physician**: Once I confirm its feasibility and adaptability, this model can be applied to any functional setting with only minor modifications.

**狱医**：它是如此的优越、如此的有效，如此具有超凡的价值。\
**The Physician**: So far, it has proven to be far superior to any current system of governance in our world—transcendental, even.

**狱医**：……该死，我根本没有必要和你探讨这一切。剩下的时间已经不多了。\
**The Physician**: Curse it! Why am I wasting time explaining this to you? Time is running out.

调查员敏锐地察觉到了其中的关键。\
The investigator keenly senses the key within his words.

**维尔汀**：梅林先生，您一直在强调的“时间”，指的究竟是什么？\
**Vertin**: Dr. Merlin, you keep mentioning "time." What exactly do you mean by that?

**狱医**：就连那群丧失了全部理智的面具脑袋都知晓——\
**The Physician**: Really? You need to ask? Even those oily-headed lunatics know it.

**狱医**：时代的终点马上要到来了，不是吗？\
**The Physician**: The end of this era is imminent, is it not?

果然如此——那个呼之欲出的词。\
Indeed—the word that was so close to being spoken.

**维尔汀**：梅林先生，您知晓“暴雨”的存在。\
**Vertin**: You know about the "Storm."

**狱医**：这就是你们的叫法吗——一场冲刷一切的“暴雨”？\
**The Physician**: That's what you call it, is it? A "Storm" that washes everything away?

**狱医**：来自圣洛夫基金会的职员，你们应该比我更为明了，很快，这里的一切都将不复存在。\
**The Physician**: You employees of the St. Pavlov Foundation should know better than I. Soon, this era and everything in it will cease to exist.

**狱医**：长时间的稳定观察已成奢望。我需要在这个监狱变成一片废墟或者更加不可理喻的事物之前，证明全景监狱的可行性。\
**The Physician**: I must prove the feasibility of the Panopticon model before this place is turned to ruins, or something even more unrecognizable.

**虚构集**：带走一切的“暴雨”……维尔汀，你们究竟在说什么？\
**Recoleta**: A "Storm" that washes everything away? Vertin, what on earth are you two talking about?

话题发展的方向逐渐超越了一名自诩想象力丰富的作家的想象。\
The conversation extends beyond even the most imaginative creations of the aspiring writer.

**维尔汀**：……\
**Vertin**: ...

**狱医**：没人能预测我们会回到什么年代。\
**The Physician**: No one can predict the era to which we'll be reversed.

**狱医**：我见证着这片土地一次又一次回到过去，这座监狱不断改变模样……\
**The Physician**: I've seen the eras change time and time again—the transformation of this place over and over.

**狱医**：但在九次所谓的“暴雨”中，无论我们返回到何种年代，考迪罗主义的幽灵从未离开过这片土地。\
**The Physician**: But no matter which era each of these nine "Storms," as you call them, has taken us back to, caudillismo continues to plague this land.

**狱医**：无论是古典的依附论学家，还是殉难的救赎者，我都见识过了——年轻的作家，你与那些被雨水带走的知识分子没什么不同。\
**The Physician**: Dependency theorists, martyred revolutionists ... I've seen them all. You, young writer, are no different from those intellectuals who were swept away in the rain.

**狱医**：……这个时代的浪潮，它疯狂、激进、残暴、魔幻，里面没有什么所谓的浪漫，只有困兽的剧烈挣扎，一轮又一轮循环的开始。\
**The Physician**: There is no romance in this era, only the repeated cycles of madness and brutality—an endless, meaningless struggle.

**狱医**：只有在这个被流放的边陲，我们能稍微远离野心者的掠夺与他们所带来的混乱。\
**The Physician**: Only in this forgotten corner can we momentarily escape the plundering of the marauders and the chaos they unleash.

**狱医**：虽然很快，那些戴面具的家伙就要把这里洗劫一空了。\
**The Physician**: Although, it won't be long before this place is looted by those oily-headed lunatics.

**狱医**：就像在此之前，在这片如银子般富饶的土地上，已经发生过无数次的掠夺那般……\
**The Physician**: Just as it has countless times before on this land as rich as silver.

他自言自语着。\
He mutters to himself.

**狱医**：但没关系，即使在一片废墟之中，我们仍能拯救我们自己……\
**The Physician**: But there is still hope. Even in a wasteland, we may still be saved.

**狱医**：只要我赶在所有人之前，寻找到那条通往超限的道路，这一切都会迎来答案。\
**The Physician**: As long as I uncover the path to transcendentality, I will find the ultimate answer.

**狱医**：够了，请你们离开！我已经在你们身上浪费了过多的时间！\
**The Physician**: Ugh, I've already wasted far too much time on you! Leave. Now!

狱医转过身去，开始为下一场手术做准备，整理那些残破不堪的手术工具。\
The Physician turns away, beginning preparations for the next surgery, organizing his worn-out instruments.

**狱卒**：事已至此，请诸位不要再纠缠了。\
**Jailer**: You heard him. Please don't press things any further.

**虚构集**：我知晓你的意思了，先生。你不想再跟我讨论我的小说，我也不会再多提。\
**Recoleta**: Alright, sir, I get it. Obviously, you don't want to discuss my novel with me anymore, so I won't insist upon it.

**虚构集**：那些书信的往来，那些振奋人心的修改建议……也许对你来说都没有意义……\
**Recoleta**: All the letters we wrote to one another, all those inspiring revisions and suggestions ... I guess they meant nothing to you.

她的声音在颤抖。退稿、闭门羹、激烈的批评——这比她所经历的那一切都要更加令她怅然。\
Her voice wavers. Rejections, closed doors, harsh critiques—this proves more devastating than all of them together.

**虚构集**：但我仍有一件事必须要告知你。狱卒小姐，你能让我们和狱医先生单独谈话吗？\
**Recoleta**: But there's still something I must tell you. Jailer, could you please allow us a private conversation with the Physi—no ...

**虚构集**：和……阿莱夫先生。\
**Recoleta**: With Aleph.

闻言，背对着众人的狱医停下了手中的动作。\
Hearing this, the Physician stops.

**狱医**：狱卒，你先出去吧。让我和访客单独谈话五分钟。\
**The Physician**: Leave us, Jailer. I'll spare these outsiders five minutes.

**狱卒**：……\
**Jailer**: ...

美洲豹沉默地离开了手术室，不属于大型捕食者的悲伤目光最后望了女孩们一眼。这一次，她什么也没有回应。\
The jaguar turns to leave, her face revealing an uncharacteristic sorrow as she lingers on the girls one last time. This time, she offers no words.

## 9TH-13 迷宫的主人 / Master of the Labyrinth

寂静的室内只余心电监护仪的声响。\
Only the steady beeping of a heart monitor keeps the eerie silence at bay.

**虚构集**：呼……\
**Recoleta**: *deep breath*

**虚构集**：狱医先生，如果你真的是阿莱夫的话……我不知道你为什么要这么做，要利用我的小说来操纵监狱。\
**Recoleta**: Dr. Merlin, or should I say Aleph? I don't know why you're using my novel to manipulate the Panopticon.

**虚构集**：但无论是小说还是现实，最终都无法达到你想要的效果。\
**Recoleta**: But you need to know that it won't serve your purpose, whether in fiction or reality.

**虚构集**：你说，想通过这种模式，让所有人都成为科马拉监狱的观察者……但你有正视过科马拉监狱现在真实的状态吗？\
**Recoleta**: You claim that the inmates are "both the observer and the observed" and "both wielders and subjects of power." How could you be so blind as to not see the true state of the Panopticon?

**虚构集**：那些囚犯没有因为这个所谓的实验，而实行某种完美的纪律……相反，他们成为了一种可悲的存在，享受着来自瞭望塔的视线，进行着夸张的自我表演。\
**Recoleta**: The inmates haven't achieved any "perfect order." No, they've devolved into pitiful caricatures of themselves—performers in some endless pantomime to be watched from the central tower.

**虚构集**：本应根据病情分配的药物与物资，变成了一场彰显“命运的随机性”的表演道具；瞭望塔与环形监狱，则成为了他们的舞台。\
**Recoleta**: Even their medication has become a prop to demonstrate the so-called "randomness of fate" in the theater that is the Panopticon.

**虚构集**：监狱并没有因为这场表演而变得更好，应该得到救治的病人最终只会默默地死亡在角落。\
**Recoleta**: This farce hasn't made the Panopticon a better place. No, it has warped it into a twisted theater of cruelty where the sick are denied treatment and left to quietly perish in the dark corners of its halls.

**虚构集**：就连文学也是如此……\
**Recoleta**: And literature has died alongside them.

**虚构集**：这个监狱的一切，都是在这种“权力的视线”下诞生的怪物……\
**Recoleta**: This prison is a monster born under the gaze of this "all-seeing power."

**虚构集**：阿莱夫，这就是你想要的答案吗？\
**Recoleta**: Aleph, is this truly the ultimate answer you've been searching for?

漫长的沉默后，狱医仿佛被惊醒一般，他后退一步，失手碰掉了台上的手术刀具。\
The Physician suddenly seems startled, stepping back and accidentally knocking over his tools.

**狱医**：……什么？\
**The Physician**: What?!

**狱医**：这就是……我获得的答案？\
**The Physician**: Are you suggesting that this is the answer I've reached?

**狱医**：你的意思是，在我不知晓的时刻，我的探索早已失败了吗？\
**The Physician**: That my experiment has been a failure all along, and I've been too blind to see it?

**狱医**：不，这不可能。福柯的理论是完美的！\
**The Physician**: No, impossible. Foucault's theory is flawless!

全盘否定的言辞让他难以容忍。男人看似镇定地在台面上寻找着什么，却不小心将所有手术工具都清空到了地上。\
Having his life's work denied is something he cannot tolerate. The man searches the tabletop with feigned composure, but in doing so, he unintentionally sweeps all the surgical tools onto the floor.

**狱医**：我排除了所有的障碍，才让这座监狱运作起来，它是如此的纯粹，如此的独立……\
**The Physician**: I have removed every obstacle to the running of this prison. It is pure, sacrosanct.

**狱医**：我不断评估、改变下属的行为，只为了让他们用最好的方法来监管这里。\
**The Physician**: I have constantly re-evaluated the system, adjusting my instructions to my subordinates to ensure the most efficient maintenance of the established order.

**狱医**：……而你现在告诉我，我所做的一切，都早已失去了原本的意义？\
**The Physician**: And now, you stand here and tell me that everything I've done has been meaningless from the very beginning?

**狱医**：我奉行的理论，它早已被另一种权力模式取代？\
**The Physician**: That the power model I have implemented has already been replaced by an alternative?

**狱医**：外来者，你只是妄图阻碍纪律的运作……那些犯人，他们仍然处于完美的纪律之中！\
**The Physician**: No, outsiders. The perfect order of the Panopticon shall not be disrupted. I will not be swayed by your lies!

**狱医**：在这个优越的场所里，任何情况都瞒不过我。\
**The Physician**: This facility is superior to all others. Nothing here escapes my notice.

终于，在不易察觉的角落中，他找到了那颗萦绕着黑雾的二十面骰。\
At last, in a barely noticeable corner, he finds the twenty-sided die wreathed in black mist.

**狱医**：制造奇迹不易，我们一向知晓。\
**The Physician**: That said, it isn't easy to work a miracle, as we all know.

**狱医**：我将亲自确认一切。\
**The Physician**: I shall personally verify it all myself.

监狱掌控者所有的情绪，在将骰子握入手掌的瞬间消融。\
All of his emotions dissolve as he grips the die.

狭窄的手术室震颤着，仿佛回应掌控者的呼唤一般，发出扭曲的尖啸。\
The narrow operating room shakes, as if responding to him, emitting a distorted screech.

**维尔汀**：发生了什么？\
**Vertin**: What's happening?

**狱医**：来自另一个时代的访客们，你们企图凭借语言传播的疾病，将科马拉的幽禁打破。\
**The Physician**: Visitors from another era, you have come here with plagued ideologies in an attempt to break the subtle balance of the Panopticon.

**狱医**：但你们有认真凝视过脚下的每一片瓷砖、每一条裂缝、每一道水痕的消失与重现吗？\
**The Physician**: But did you not notice the tiles beneath your feet, the cracks, and water stains on the walls constantly changing right before your eyes?

**狱医**：从这个房间，到另一个房间，到每个房间。\
**The Physician**: This room, the previous room, every room.

**狱医**：你们徘徊于此，认为它们一模一样，认为它们是一个不可理喻的疯人迷宫。\
**The Physician**: You have blindly wandered through them, seeing them as nothing more than the building blocks of a monotonous labyrinth.

**狱医**：但这里并非奇妙幻想的空间，而是基于对秩序与权力的运用所诞生的天地。\
**The Physician**: But this place was not born from the chaotic imaginings of a madman. No, every inch has been crafted through the meticulous harnessing of order and power.

**狱医**：从一根在风中漂浮的蜘蛛丝开始，到活动场地走廊把手上的一粒锈迹结束——\
**The Physician**: Every wisp of spider silk drifting in the wind, every speck of rust on the gallery rail,

**狱医**：我亲手搭建了这座圆形的房子。\
**The Physician**: every detail of the Panopticon has been built by my own hands.

**狱医**：在这颗无尽变幻的骰子里，它的映射足以让概念变成现实，让思想成为物质。\
**The Physician**: With this ever-shifting die, concepts may be transformed into reality, and ideals into substance.

**狱医**：我观察着每一件事物，时间每一分秒的流动：你们的脚步从来没有走出过这个实验的范围。\
**The Physician**: I observe the movement of every entity—the passage of every second. The moment you entered this realm, you, too, became subjects of my experiment.

**虚构集**：在理想家先生遇袭的时候，我们也遇到过这样的情况！\
**Recoleta**: This happened when the Idealist was attacked, too!

**十四行诗**：原来从一开始，我们就身处骰子所构建的监狱之中吗……\
**Sonetto**: To think we've been trapped in a prison fabricated by a die all this time ...

**十四行诗**：这一切，都是狱医所创造的场景……？\
**Sonetto**: Did the Physician really build all this with such a small, simple object?

**维尔汀**：监狱的扭曲愈发严重了……我们要做好随时战斗和撤退的准备。\
**Vertin**: The distortion is getting worse. Prepare yourselves to fight or flee.

情况逐渐变得不受控制。手术室中，所有的一切都在尖啸，扭曲，化作意义不明的黑白线条。\
The situation begins to spiral out of control. Now everything in the room screeches and twists until they become a mess of meaningless black-and-white lines.

**虚构集**：拜托了，梅林先生，快停下来！！！\
**Recoleta**: Please, Dr. Merlin. Stop this!

**狱医**：不，你们的要求太荒唐了。\
**The Physician**: No. You're asking for the impossible.

**狱医**：这种精心设计的概念不应该受到一丝外来影响就陷入紊乱……因为它是注定要传遍整个社会机体的……\
**The Physician**: Power model of the Panopticon is destined to permeate all of society. Such insignificant interferences could never plunge it into chaos.

**狱医**：但你失败了，梅林。\
**The Physician**: But it already has, Merlin. You've failed.

**狱医**：我没有！我没有！只要保证它不停地运作……\
**The Physician**: I have not failed! As long as I keep the prison running ...

狱医摆弄着骰子，古怪地自言自语着。\
The Physician fiddles with the die, muttering baffling and incoherent words to himself.

**狱医**：运作的只是骰子，而并非你的权力机制。\
**The Physician**: It isn't your power model running the prison. It's the die.

**狱医**：它是巫术，是魔法，它不包含多种多样的力量，并不是你所追求的权力物理学，也无法成为权力实验室。\
**The Physician**: It's simply a form of magic, unrelated to the microphysics of power you seek. It provides no aid in your experimentation with power.

**狱医**：它是重塑之手和军政府给你的幻想，一个不存在的存在。\
**The Physician**: It's a false hope, a castle in the sky given to you by the military Junta and Manus Vindictae.

**十四行诗**：重塑之手？\
**Sonetto**: Manus Vindictae?

**十四行诗**：你果然和重塑之手有关系。你们究竟想做些什么？\
**Sonetto**: So you really are working with them. What exactly do you intend to do?

**狱医**：我……\
**The Physician**: I ...

**狱医**：所以我也失败了吗？\
**The Physician**: Then, I've also failed?

**狱医**：就像追求本能现实主义的理想家、炼制永生之泉的帕拉塞尔苏斯、寻找单面硬币的扎伊尔那样，成为了一个在混乱纷芜现实中迷失的可怜虫。\
**The Physician**: I've ended up a pathetic fool, lost in the chaos of reality, just like the Idealist chasing visceral realism, Paracelsus seeking the Fountain of Youth, and Zahir obsessing over the one-sided coin.

**狱医**：阿莱夫，一切都是从哪里开始溃败的？\
**The Physician**: When did it all start falling apart, Aleph?

**狱医**：是从门把手的松动、囚犯溃烂的伤口、每日28毫克浓度的消毒水、墙壁上第二块灰砖的裂缝扩至6毫米开始吗？\
**The Physician**: When the doorknob loosened? When the prisoners' wounds started to fester? Or when the daily disinfectant concentration reached 28 mg, or the crack in the second gray brick on the wall expanded to 6 mm?

**狱医**：还是说从典狱长达尔杜夫，带着国家福柯协会解散的消息离开乌斯怀亚开始？\
**The Physician**: Or was it when Warden Tartuffe left Ushuaia with news of the Foucault Association's dissolution?

**狱医**：我们这儿理应是精神分析的最佳实践场所……为什么他们不再探讨这一切了？\
**The Physician**: This place should've been the ideal ground for psychoanalytic practice. Why did they halt all research, all discussion?

**狱医**：我们被旧时代和新时代同时放弃了，对吗？\
**The Physician**: We've been abandoned, haven't we? By eras old and new.

**阿莱夫**：你为科马拉设计了一切，每一处细节都经过了精心的雕琢和漫长的调整。\
**Aleph**: You designed and have maintained everything in Comala, right down to the smallest detail.

**阿莱夫**：但最终这一切细节也将你束缚在这个监狱中。梅林，你马上就会丢失自己的名字，永远成为一个被困于此处的“狱医”。\
**Aleph**: But it is these details that trap you. And, as the bars close around you, you are losing your name, Merlin, and you are becoming the Physician, a man forever imprisoned within these walls.

**狱医**：我不能理解……\
**The Physician**: I don't understand.

**阿莱夫**：这些虚假的时代，它本身就是一本无尽的书。在这本可怕的书里寻找答案，本身就是错误的。\
**Aleph**: All these false eras are like a dreadful novel with no conclusion. Trying to find answers within such things is, in itself, a mistake.

**阿莱夫**：你和他们一样，注定无法寻找到属于自己的超限。\
**Aleph**: Much like them, you are destined never to attain transcendentality.

**狱医**：……\
**The Physician**: ...

**狱医**：告诉我，阿莱夫，那个答案，它真的存在吗？\
**The Physician**: Tell me, Aleph. Does the ultimate answer even exist?

那颗掌控一切的骰子重得让他再也无法握住，它掉到了地上。\
The die becomes too heavy for him to hold any longer. It drops to the floor.

监狱的扭曲与震颤终于归于寂静，仿佛一道不可视的巨大脉搏停止了瞬息。\
The distortions and tremors of the prison finally subside, as if the pulse of a massive heart had stopped for an instant.

受到扬起的烟尘影响，互相搀扶着站稳身形的女孩们并未留意到谜底的出现。\
Amid the swirling dust, the girls help each other stand but fail to notice the truth revealing itself before them.

**十四行诗**：咳咳……司辰，您还好吗？\
**Sonetto**: *cough* Timekeeper, are you alright?

**维尔汀**：咳咳……我没事，你呢？还有虚构集小姐，你还好吗？\
**Vertin**: *cough* Yes, and you? And Ms. Recoleta, are you okay?

**维尔汀**：虚构集小姐……？\
**Vertin**: Ms. Recoleta?

烟雾散去，没有人应答。被点名的少女只是震惊地望着眼前的人影。\
The smoke clears, but no one responds. The named girl simply stares in shock at the figure before her.

**虚构集**：你……你是……\
**Recoleta**: Y-You're ...

**？？？**：乌托邦[Utopia]源自于希腊语，意思是“不存在的地方”。\
**???**: The word "utopia" derives from Greek. It means "no place."

**？？？**：人们深信不疑，潜心琢磨这无休止的迷宫，探索人类的奥秘。\
**???**: People cannot understand the structure of the labyrinth, yet they continue to follow its paths.

**？？？**：同时，人们迷惑不解，亦感荒谬，信奉命运带来的吉凶祸福。\
**???**: They cannot comprehend the mechanics of fate, yet they believe in its jurisdiction.

**？？？**：仿佛只需如此，世上所有的一切都会变得微不足道。\
**???**: As if, by doing so, everything will naturally fall into place.

**阿莱夫**：在今日，极夜已经造访南方。\
**Aleph**: And now, the polar night approaches.

**阿莱夫**：欢迎你的到来，我的笔友。\
**Aleph**: How good it is to see you, pen pal.

## 9TH-14 镜子与面具 / The Mask in the Mirror

**维尔汀**：狱医先生呢？不对……\
**Vertin**: Where did the Physician go? Wait.

**维尔汀**：先生，您究竟是……\
**Vertin**: Sir, are you ...?

没有人留意到面前的陌生囚徒是何时出现在那儿的。\
No one notices when the unfamiliar prisoner appears.

他平静、普通得如同一面亘古不变的镜子，仿佛一开始就存在，存在于这个房间、这个迷宫之中，存在于所有人的身边。\
He seems calm and almost ordinary, like an unchanging mirror that has stood here all along—in this room, in this labyrinth, passed unseen by everyone.

**虚构集**：唔……\
**Recoleta**: *pant*

近在眼前的答案让她仓惶地后退了一步。仿佛事到如今，这个名字所代表的含义，与接下来会发生的事情，让她本能地感到害怕。\
The answer she now sees plainly makes her step back in a panic.

但她最终仍然喊出了那个名字。它沉重，冰冷，让人无所适从。\
But in the end, she says the name out loud. Its sound is heavy, cold, and leaves her at a loss.

**虚构集**：阿莱夫。\
**Recoleta**: Aleph.

**虚构集**：是你，我的笔友……阿莱夫。\
**Recoleta**: It's you, my pen pal.

**虚构集**：你果然在这里，在科马拉监狱之中。\
**Recoleta**: You are in fact in Comala.

**虚构集**：那些回信，那些措辞，那些字符的组合，它们并不是我的想象，也不是神圣的恶作剧……维尔汀，十四行诗！一切就和我先前告诉你们的一样！\
**Recoleta**: All those letters, all the ideas we shared—they weren't just my imagination or some prank. Vertin, Sonetto, it's all just as I told you!

**虚构集**：它们果然都是有意义的，是真实的存在。嗯……\
**Recoleta**: They weren't meaningless. *pant* They're all real.

只是为何，她并没有感到一丝的欣喜？\
Yet, why does she feel no joy?

**维尔汀**：先生，所以您就是阿莱夫，监狱的控制者？\
**Vertin**: So, sir, are you Aleph, the ruler of this prison?

**维尔汀**：就是您用骰子控制了监狱，并隐匿了德洛丝女士的行踪？\
**Vertin**: Are you the one controlling the Panopticon with a die? The one hiding Ms. Dores's whereabouts?

**阿莱夫**：新奇的提问。有别于之前的两千六百六十六个问题。\
**Aleph**: What curious inquiries, quite different from the last 2666 questions I've received.

**阿莱夫**：诸位科马拉的访客，你们可以叫我阿莱夫，也可以叫我任何名字，无论是敬神的符号，还是可笑的代称。\
**Aleph**: My guests, you may call me Aleph, or by any other name, be it a symbol of god's oneness or a farcical epithet.

**阿莱夫**：我只是一位自愿居住于此的囚徒。组成科马拉万千字符中的一个。\
**Aleph**: I am merely one of the many prisoners who voluntarily reside here—a single letter in the alphabet of the Panopticon.

**维尔汀**：一个字符……阿莱夫先生，您的说法与措辞，都显然与狱医先生相别甚远。\
**Vertin**: A letter ... The way you speak is quite different from Dr. Merlin.

**维尔汀**：但我仍然有些费解，您和狱医究竟是什么关系？\
**Vertin**: Still, I wonder what your relationship is with him.

在昏暗的灯光下，面前的男子看起来疲惫不堪。\
Under the dim lighting, the man looks drained of all energy.

**维尔汀**：我有一个斗胆的猜测：您就是狱医，对吗？\
**Vertin**: But allow me to make a guess: You're Dr. Merlin, aren't you?

**阿莱夫**：这是一个不完全正确的说法。但你可以如此认为。\
**Aleph**: I'm afraid that's not entirely accurate, but you may think of it that way.

**阿莱夫**：梅林，他是我脑海中诞生的一个幻影，一个不完整的重演……他是我，但也并不完全是我。\
**Aleph**: Merlin is a figment born of my mind, an incomplete reenactment. He is me, yes, but not entirely.

**阿莱夫**：他……他们只是在自己的命题中求索的失败者。\
**Aleph**: He—or rather, they—failed to find their answers.

**阿莱夫**：我旁观着这一切，看着他们在注定的命运中挣扎，最后理所当然地溃败，而没有去阻止。这就是我们的关系——仅此而已。\
**Aleph**: They fought against their predestined fates, only to be inevitably crushed under their weight. I simply stood by and watched it all unfold. That was the extent of our relationship.

**维尔汀**：他们……？\
**Vertin**: "They"?

**阿莱夫**：你们已经见过梅林与理想家了，也亲眼目睹了他们的死亡。\
**Aleph**: You've already met Merlin and the Idealist—even witnessed their demise.

**阿莱夫**：理想家被困于诗句的梦魇，最终甚至失去了自己的名字。\
而梅林，不过也是被困于科马拉的建筑结构之中罢了。\
**Aleph**: Shackled by the delusions of verses, the Idealist lost his own name. Merlin, too, imprisoned himself within the system of the Panopticon.

**阿莱夫**：沉湎于美妙的希望中无可自拔，孤注一掷。他们的行为确实给诸位带来了一定的麻烦。\
**Aleph**: I'm sure their desperate pursuits caused you some trouble.

**阿莱夫**：如今，他们以自身的溃败作为这场短暂邂逅的落幕。\
**Aleph**: Please forgive them. After all, your fleeting encounters led to the demise of them both.

**维尔汀**：……我想我大概明白了。所以理想家先生与狱医，都是您的一部分，或者说，您的人格之一。\
**Vertin**: I think I understand now. The Idealist and the Physician are both parts of you, or, to put it another way, they're your alter egos.

看来，狱卒小姐所说的“监狱中都是精神病人”，并非一句虚言。\
It seems the jailer's diagnosis, that the whole prison is mad, has been shown to be more accurate than anyone could have imagined.

**十四行诗**：狱医先前提到了重塑之手——科马拉监狱中的一切，以及狱医，又和重塑之手有什么关系？\
**Sonetto**: The Physician mentioned Manus Vindictae. What's the relationship between this prison and the Manus?

**阿莱夫**：基金会的访客们，我们都经历过那些消逝的年代。\
**Aleph**: Visitors from the Foundation, we all witnessed those eras perish.

**阿莱夫**：1977年，第四次暴雨来临前，我来到了乌斯怀亚。他们找到了我——国家福柯学会的人。\
**Aleph**: In 1977, not long before the fourth "Storm," I arrived in Ushuaia. Shortly after, some members of the National Foucault Studies Association reached out to me.

**阿莱夫**：同时到来的，还有一个自称重塑之手的神秘学家组织。他们都想让我回答他们的问题，把我称为“顾问”。\
**Aleph**: But it wasn't just them. An arcanist organization called Manus Vindictae also approached me. Each of them wanted answers. They named me their "advisor."

**十四行诗**：重塑之手的“顾问”？\
**Sonetto**: You acted as an "advisor" to the Manus?

**阿莱夫**：他们分别给了我一个概念，以及一个寓言。\
**Aleph**: The two parties presented me with a concept and a parable, respectively.

**十四行诗**：概念，以及寓言……？\
**Sonetto**: A concept and a parable?

**阿莱夫**：国家福柯学会想要在这里探求全景监狱概念的可行性。\
**Aleph**: The Foucault Association sought to explore the feasibility of the Panopticon concept here.

**阿莱夫**：而重塑之手，则向我展示了，那一则关于过去和未来的寓言。\
**Aleph**: While Manus Vindictae showed me a parable of the past and future.

**阿莱夫**：我日夜不停地寻找答案，在无尽的文字与现实中逡巡——于是梅林基于此诞生了。这是一种尝试，也是一种代价。\
**Aleph**: Day and night, I wandered through endless texts, endless realities, as I searched for answers. And thus, Merlin was born. He was both an experiment and a price I paid.

**阿莱夫**：很抱歉，全新的方向，总是会使我陷入人类摄取知识的局限性。\
**Aleph**: A new concept, a new direction ... Pursuing such things always leaves me confined by the limitations of human knowledge.

**阿莱夫**：梅林终其一生，只想通过探索福柯理论的方式，来获取那个唯一的、无限的答案。\
**Aleph**: Merlin spent his entire life exploring Foucault's theories in pursuit of that singular yet infinite answer.

**维尔汀**：可是，阿莱夫先生，您仍然没有说清楚您帮助重塑之手的理由。\
**Vertin**: What about the Manus, Mr. Aleph? You didn't explain why you helped them.

**阿莱夫**：……理由？\
**Aleph**: Explain why?

**阿莱夫**：他们发问了，就像你们一样。\
**Aleph**: Because they asked me to, just as you have.

**阿莱夫**：而我只是在为他们的问题寻找答案。\
**Aleph**: I simply worked to answer their questions.

**维尔汀**：……阿莱夫先生，您的意思是，在您眼中，我们和重塑之手并没有不同。\
**Vertin**: So you're saying that, to you, we're no different from Manus Vindictae?

**维尔汀**：如果我们发问，您也会如实地回答这一切吗？\
**Vertin**: And if we ask, you'll answer us, without holding anything back?

**阿莱夫**：这不正是我们正在经历的事情吗？\
**Aleph**: Is that not precisely what is happening this very moment?

**维尔汀**：……\
**Vertin**: ...

阿莱夫拾起了那枚掉落在地上的骰子。它闪烁着抚慰人心的微弱辉光。\
Aleph picks up the fallen die. It flickers with a familiar, comforting glow.

**阿莱夫**：这就是他们交给梅林的玩具。一个名叫科马拉之雨的巫术骰子。\
**Aleph**: This is what the Manus gave Merlin, a magical die named the\
Tear of Comala.

**阿莱夫**：二十世纪初的探险家们，在无人踏足的南极大陆挖掘出这块属于神祗的魔法石头。它来自一道古远的门扉。\
**Aleph**: It was once a gemstone that belonged to a god. At the beginning of the century, explorers plucked it from an ancient gate they discovered in Antarctica.

**阿莱夫**：他们惊讶地发现，这块石头能够忠实地映射出人们内心的渴望，将幻影的断壁残垣变成现实。\
**Aleph**: To the explorers' amazement, the gemstone could turn human desires into reality.

**阿莱夫**：它被雕琢成代表命运的骰子模样。他们曾用它搭建起一所流放神秘学家的疗养院，最后这所疗养院，又被改造成了如今的监狱……\
**Aleph**: So, they cut it into a die, a symbol of fate, and used it to build a sanatorium, which was later transformed into the Panopticon you are standing in right now.

他的话语并不迂回，却依旧让经历了这一切的外来者们感到困惑。\
His words are direct, yet they still leave the outsiders perplexed.

**虚构集**：阿莱夫……所以，科马拉的幕后主使，真的是你吗？\
**Recoleta**: Then, Aleph, you really are the mastermind behind the Panopticon?

一直沉默的女孩握紧了手中的笔记本。她的指节正因用力而泛白。\
The silent girl grips her notebook. Her knuckles turn white from the pressure.

那是一本尚未出版的小说雏形。那里留存着只有她本人所知晓的——属于每日伏案，属于自我审视，属于逐字逐句地质疑、推敲、考究的岁月。\
The draft of an unpublished novel, with words that only she knows—the countless hours spent at her desk, the self-reflections, the meticulous questioning, revisions, and scrutiny of every word.

那是一段属于作家的人生。\
That book holds the life of its writer.

**虚构集**：你说，梅林他想要用全景监狱去追求属于自己的答案，可是这和我的小说有什么关系？\
**Recoleta**: You said Merlin used the Panopticon to seek his answer. W-What does that have to do with my novel?

**虚构集**：我不能理解……阿莱夫，你为什么要用我的小说来操纵监狱中的一切？\
**Recoleta**: I don't get it, Aleph. Why would you use my novel to manipulate this place?

**虚构集**：这里的人们，罗贝托、加西亚、奥克塔维奥、巴勃鲁，还有狱卒小姐……他们都因此而沦陷于一场注定结局的命运之环。\
**Recoleta**: Roberta, García, Octavia, Pablo, the jailer, everyone ... Not one of them deserved to be trapped in a deadly loop in which everyone's fate is already predestined.

**虚构集**：他们被迫成为了阿马尔菲塔诺小镇中的幽灵，被困于这座环形的废墟……\
**Recoleta**: They're just like the ghosts in Amalfitano, inescapably trapped within the ruins.

**虚构集**：……你究竟想要做什么？\
**Recoleta**: Tell me, what is it you really want?

闻言，孤寂的囚徒只是不解地把玩着手中的骰子。\
Hearing this, the lonely prisoner fidgets with the die, looking puzzled.

**阿莱夫**：但这是你自己提出的问题。\
**Aleph**: It's not about what I want. It's about what you want.

**阿莱夫**：第一封信件的第三行。\
**Aleph**: The third line of your first letter.

**阿莱夫**：你说，你想要给《理性家族的崛起与衰落》这篇小说一个结局。\
**Aleph**: You said you wanted to give The Rise and Fall of Sanity an ending.

## 9TH-15 阿莱夫 / Aleph

**虚构集**：“我们仍然能在圣特莱莎大学图书馆中，寻找到有关巴比伦之骰的历史记录。”\
**Recoleta**: "Historical records of the Die of Babylon can still be found in the library of Santa Teresa University."

**虚构集**：不，不。这样的开场会让故事不清不楚。\
**Recoleta**: No, no, no. An opening like this would make the story too ambiguous.

**虚构集**：“1975年，墨西哥索诺拉州，阿马尔菲塔诺小镇，在那栋蓝色屋顶的茅屋中，一件诡异而可怕的事情发生了。一切起因于当地一项神奇的民俗……”\
**Recoleta**: "In 1975, in the town of Amalfitano, Sonora, Mexico, something terrible and eerie took place in the cottage with the blue roof. It all began with the peculiar customs of the loc—"

**虚构集**：不对，我是怎么得知这件事的呢？得在小说开始时加入一个故事的讲述者！\
**Recoleta**: Wait, how did I learn about all this? I need to add a role for the narrator—the storyteller!

**虚构集**：“一名来自墨西哥超现实主义派的诗人告诉了我这个故事：像往常一样，一名老妇人走进了小镇的酒馆。就在这时——”\
**Recoleta**: "A surrealist poet from Mexico told me this story. An old woman walked into the bar she frequented in town. At the same moment ..."

**阿莱夫**：“银行职员亦走进了这家酒馆。他带来了一个全新的消息：跨国企业将会在阿马尔菲塔诺兴建一家饼干肥皂厂。”\
**Aleph**: "... the Bank Clerk entered the bar, too, bringing news that a multinational corporation was going to build a cookie soap factory in Amalfitano."

**虚构集**：等等，银行职员？我从来不知道阿马尔菲塔诺还有银行……\
**Recoleta**: Wait, "Bank Clerk"? I didn't know there were banks in Amalfitano.

**虚构集**：但……这很合理！商业银行是资本主义生产模式的标志……谢谢你，我的笔友！\
**Recoleta**: But it does make sense! Commercial banks are no doubt a hallmark of capitalism. Thanks, pen pal!

**虚构集**：Los registros históricos del Dado de Babilonia aún se pueden encontrar en la biblioteca de la Universidad Santa Teresa. 一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一 En 1975, en el pueblo de Amalfitano, Sonora, México, ocurrió algo terrible y escalofriante en la cabaña con el techo azul.Todo comenzó con las costumbres peculiares de los loc— 一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一 Un poeta surrealista de México me contó esta historia. Una anciana entró en el bar al que solía ir en el pueblo. Al mismo tiempo … ... el Empleado del Banco también entró al bar, trayendo la noticia de que una corporación multinacional iba a construir una fábrica de jabón de galletas en Amalfitano.\
 “在他成为银行职员之前，他也曾是小镇古老习俗拥护者中的一员。”\
**Recoleta**: Los registros históricos del Dado de Babilonia aún se pueden encontrar en la biblioteca de la Universidad Santa Teresa. 一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一 En 1975, en el pueblo de Amalfitano, Sonora, México, ocurrió algo terrible y escalofriante en la cabaña con el techo azul.Todo comenzó con las costumbres peculiares de los loc— 一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一一 Un poeta surrealista de México me contó esta historia. Una anciana entró en el bar al que solía ir en el pueblo. Al mismo tiempo … ... el Empleado del Banco también entró al bar, trayendo la noticia de que una corporación multinacional iba a construir una fábrica de jabón de galletas en Amalfitano.\
 "Before he became a Bank Clerk, he was an advocate of the town's ancient customs."

**虚构集**：“他曾是一名疲惫的沙漠捕鱼人。”\
**Recoleta**: "He was a Dune Piscator."

**阿莱夫**：“在接受了巴比伦之骰赋予他的命运之后，他选择将一切都抛之脑后：可悲可怕的村庄，隐藏在无限随机之中的轮回。”\
**Aleph**: "After accepting the fate bestowed by the Die of Babylon, he chose to leave everything behind: the sad horrifying village, and the cycles hidden within infinite randomness."

**虚构集**：噢，这很讽刺，但也很现实。现在，我们还需要一位与他形成对照的角色，一个宿命论的拥护者。\
**Recoleta**: Oh, how ironic. But it's still realistic, too. Now we just need a contrasting character—a believer in fate.

**虚构集**：Antes de convertirse en Empleado del Banco, era un defensor de las antiguas costumbres del pueblo. Era un pescador de dunas. Después de aceptar el destino otorgado por el Dado de Babilonia, eligió dejar todo atrás: el triste y aterrador pueblo y los ciclos ocultos dentro de la infinita aleatoriedad.\
 “一名年迈的织工在古老的作坊中，不停地转动她的纺车，这是巴比伦之骰赠给她最珍贵的礼物。”\
**Recoleta**: Antes de convertirse en Empleado del Banco, era un defensor de las antiguas costumbres del pueblo. Era un pescador de dunas. Después de aceptar el destino otorgado por el Dado de Babilonia, eligió dejar todo atrás: el triste y aterrador pueblo y los ciclos ocultos dentro de la infinita aleatoriedad.\
 "An elderly weaver sat in her ancient workshop, tirelessly spinning her wheel, a precious gift bestowed to her by the Die of Babylon."

**阿莱夫**：“她双眼已盲，低声诉说着自己所经历的一切。”\
**Aleph**: "The Blind Weaver softly recounted all she had experienced."

**虚构集**：阿莱夫，这简直是一个天才的提议。眼盲的织工，不可能目击谋杀案的目击证人！\
**Recoleta**: What a brilliant idea, Aleph! A blind weaver couldn't possibly witness the murder!

**虚构集**：好极了，好极了，让我在这一节里加入一个死于谋杀案的赶驴人幽灵……\
**Recoleta**: Fantastic! In that case, I'll add a donkey driver who gets murdered in this chapter.

**虚构集**：每一次，你的提议都让这个故事更进一步，阿莱夫。\
**Recoleta**: With each of your suggestions, the story takes a step forward. Thanks, Aleph.

**虚构集**：但为什么……我仍然看不见它的终局？\
**Recoleta**: But I still can't see any sign of the ending.

**虚构集**：这种感觉就好像，无论我们新增多少角色，这个沙漠小镇中却总是缺少了一名核心的关键人物……\
**Recoleta**: It's like no matter how many new characters we add, there's still something missing in the desert town. It lacks a key figure.

**虚构集**：阿莱夫，我到底该怎么办？到底要怎么样，才能给这个故事一个真正的结局？\
**Recoleta**: Aleph, what should I do? How do I give this story an ending?

**阿莱夫**：Antes de convertirse en Empleado del Banco, era un defensor de las antiguas costumbres del pueblo. Era un pescador de dunas. Después de aceptar el destino otorgado por el Dado de Babilonia, eligió dejar todo atrás: el triste y aterrador pueblo y los ciclos ocultos dentro de la infinita aleatoriedad. Una anciana tejedora se sentó en su antiguotaller, girando incansablemente su rueca, un regalo precioso otorgado por el Dado de Babilonia. La Tejedora Ciega relató suavemente todo lo que había vivido.\
 你提出了这个问题：“如何给这个故事一个结局？”\
**Aleph**: Antes de convertirse en Empleado del Banco, era un defensor de las antiguas costumbres del pueblo. Era un pescador de dunas. Después de aceptar el destino otorgado por el Dado de Babilonia, eligió dejar todo atrás: el triste y aterrador pueblo y los ciclos ocultos dentro de la infinita aleatoriedad. Una anciana tejedora se sentó en su antiguotaller, girando incansablemente su rueca, un regalo precioso otorgado por el Dado de Babilonia. La Tejedora Ciega relató suavemente todo lo que había vivido.\
 You asked me yourself, "How do I give this story an ending?"

**阿莱夫**：你说，它已经从一行行的文字，化作一个狂热的、无限的谜题。它变成了一门秘密的语言，一列无用信息的组合，一则失去寓意的寓言故事。\
**Aleph**: You described to me how your words had transformed into an immoderate, infinite puzzle—an unrecognizable language, a collection of ambiguous information, and a parable that had lost all meaning.

**阿莱夫**：它困扰着你，让你永恒地被困囿于那座炎热的沙漠小镇之中。\
**Aleph**: The absence of an ending still gnaws at you, forever trapping you in that scorching desert town.

**阿莱夫**：而我只是在尝试解答它。\
**Aleph**: All I'm doing is trying to find it for you.

**虚构集**：难道从去年九月的时候，我们第一次来信开始，你就一直在科马拉监狱里做着这种……操纵吗？\
**Recoleta**: A-Are you saying you've been manipulating the happenings in the Panopticon like this ever since we first exchanged letters last September?

她艰难地发问了，期待着一个否定的回答，来结束这荒唐的一切。\
She struggles, vainly hoping for him to deny it.

**阿莱夫**：是的。每一次，根据你对小说的修改，科马拉监狱中的一切亦会做出对应的调整。考究的细节是故事得以顺利进行的关键。\
**Aleph**: Yes. Every time you revised the novel, corresponding adjustments were made in the Panopticon. Faithfully reflecting the intricacies of every detail was key to ensuring the story proceeds smoothly.

**阿莱夫**：有时，梅林会完成这一任务；有时是理想家；再之前，则是扎伊尔和帕拉塞尔苏斯。\
**Aleph**: Such adjustments were handled by Merlin mostly; sometimes, the Idealist; and before them, Zahir and Paracelsus.

**虚构集**：每一次……？\
**Recoleta**: "Every time"?

**阿莱夫**：阿马尔菲塔诺的故事，已经在监狱降临过六次了。\
**Aleph**: 6 versions of the Amalfitano story have played out in the Panopticon already.

**虚构集**：那些泥地间被碾死的青蛙，寿终正寝的牛，坠入大海的睡鼠……\
**Recoleta**: Does that mean ... the frog crushed in the mud, the cow dying of old age, the dormouse falling into the sea,

**虚构集**：那些在决斗中死去的幽灵，骤变的巴比伦之骰……\
**Recoleta**: the ghost killed in the duel, and the sudden changes to the Die of Babylon ...

**虚构集**：你在回信中为《理性家族的崛起与衰落》编写的后续，那些死亡、混淆、疯狂与破碎的一切，难道说，难道说，都是在这里……\
**Recoleta**: All the revisions you suggested—all the deaths, chaos, and madness—they all actually happened right here?

一直无所不知的囚徒陷入了难得的沉默——他并不会回答一个索问者早已明了答案的问题。\
The ever-knowing prisoner falls into a long, dark silence. He will not answer a question when the one asking already knows the answer.

**阿莱夫**：……无尽终有尽时，虚构集。\
**Aleph**: Even eternity has its limits, Recoleta.

**阿莱夫**：在第六次故事中，我们加入了盲眼的织工这一角色，她是一个特殊的存在。\
**Aleph**: In the sixth revision, we added the Blind Weaver, an extraordinary figure.

**阿莱夫**：就像你在第七次来信中所新增的，提着箱子的能量扰动学家一样。\
**Aleph**: Just like the Paracausality Researcher who carries a suitcase that you introduced in your seventh letter.

**十四行诗**：提着箱子的……能量扰动学家？\
**Sonetto**: The Paracausality Researcher carrying a suitcase?

**十四行诗**：虚构集小姐，你所写的这个角色，难道指代的真的是司辰吗？\
**Sonetto**: Ms. Recoleta, is this character really based on the Timekeeper?

**虚构集**：什么？！怎么可能，维尔汀和能量扰动学家绝不会是同一个人！\
**Recoleta**: What? Of course not! The Paracausality Researcher is an entirely different character!

**阿莱夫**：你还不明白吗？我们离结局非常近了，仅有一次投掷的距离。\
**Aleph**: Don't you understand? We are only one die roll away from the ending.

阿莱夫举起那颗无限迷宫的核心，科马拉之雨正在他手中缓缓旋转着。\
Aleph lifts the core of the Infinite Labyrinth. The Tear of Comala swirls slowly in his hand.

**虚构集**：我……我不明白，你到底还想做些什么？\
**Recoleta**: I-I don't ... What on earth are you trying to do?

手术室的白炽灯瞬间黯淡，墙壁上映射出水面的波纹，而后化作无数面镜子。\
The filament lamps of the operating room dim in time with his motions. The walls ripple like water, then transform into countless mirrors.

镜子中映出了无数的信息——\
Within the mirrors, an endless stream of information appears.

仿佛通了灵的电话、老旧的无线电、摇晃的幻灯机、喑哑的电影机、时刻表……还有无数门语言的词典。\
A seemingly possessed telephone babbles, an old radio sings, a flickering slide projector whirs and cracks, a muted film projector spins, a timetable opens, and dictionaries of countless languages flow past.

一个没有出口的房间，一个永远的困境，一个囚徒的居所。\
A room without an exit, an eternal predicament, a prisoner's dwelling.

**阿莱夫**：虚构集，是无限轮回的命运，让你来到乌斯怀亚的科马拉监狱。\
**Aleph**: Recoleta, it is the cycle of fate that has brought you to the Panopticon of Comala in Ushuaia.

**阿莱夫**：重新回到《理性家族的崛起与衰落》之中吧，再次成为故事中的一名角色。\
**Aleph**: Now, return to The Rise and Fall of Sanity. Return and become a character once more.

**阿莱夫**：你追寻着这个故事的结局，但在这个故事之外，你又如何能找到它的结局？\
**Aleph**: You've been searching for its ending, but how could you possibly find it when you're no longer inside the story?

**阿莱夫**：我相信，这一次，你能亲眼目睹一切的终局。你不再需要感到孤独和痛苦了。\
**Aleph**: I believe that this time, you will witness the grand finale with your own two eyes. No more sadness. No more loneliness.

**阿莱夫**：那在劫难逃的、骰子的最后一次转动，就是你一直渴求的答案……\
**Aleph**: The answer you've long sought lies in the inevitable final roll of the Die.

**虚构集**：狱卒小姐是银行职员，兀尔德女士是盲眼的织工，那罗贝托、加西亚和奥克塔维奥小姐他们呢？\
**Recoleta**: So the jailer is the Bank Clerk and Urd is the Blind Weaver. But what about Roberta, García, and Octavia?

**虚构集**：他们甚至没能拥有自己的角色，只是那群被命运摆布的动物吗……\
**Recoleta**: They weren't even assigned roles! They were just playthings, helpless in the face of "fate."

**虚构集**：……我凭什么决定一个人在监狱中所有的遭遇，凭什么为他制定所有的惩罚与胜利？\
**Recoleta**: What right do you or I have to decide what happens to them, to dictate their gains and losses?

**阿莱夫**：但他们都看不懂，不是吗？\
**Aleph**: But they couldn't possibly understand such a thing, could they?

**阿莱夫**：对你而言，这只是一个故事，虚构集。但对那些无法理解故事的人而言，这就是苦涩或甜美的命运。\
**Aleph**: To you, it's just a story. But to them, it is the manifestation of bittersweet destiny.

**虚构集**：难道因为这些都是虚构之物，就能够掩盖你将科马拉变成地狱的可怖事实吗……\
**Recoleta**: Do you think hiding behind the guise of fiction absolves you from the reality that you've turned the Panopticon into a living hell?

**虚构集**：我做过很多徒劳的努力，寄出过无数没有回音的稿件……是的，我的笔友，你确实是唯一能看懂《理性家族的崛起与衰落》的人。\
**Recoleta**: Yes, you're the only one who truly understands The Rise and Fall of Sanity. Goodness knows how many manuscripts I sent out that never received a reply.

**虚构集**：我很感谢你给我回信，感谢你能理解我的小说——这比安第斯山脉的日出还珍贵。\
**Recoleta**: I was so grateful to you. For your replies, for understanding my novel. Those things were more precious to me than any sunrise over the Andes.

**虚构集**：但……如果我知道你是通过这样的方式给我回答的，我宁愿从一开始，就不要收到那封回信……\
**Recoleta**: Had I known that your feedback was created in such a way, and at such a cost, I would've preferred not to receive it at all.

**虚构集**：你不明白吗？！那些看不懂我小说的人，他们都是我的朋友……哪怕我们只同行了一段路程就分别，亦或是仅仅认识了短暂的一天……\
**Recoleta**: Don't you get it? Even if they don't understand my novel, the people I meet are still my friends, whether we took a long journey together or we simply chatted for a few hours.

**虚构集**：对我而言，他们都是复杂的奇迹。他们与我自身产生了不可分割的关联，是我的一部分。\
**Recoleta**: We formed an inseparable, miraculous bond. They're a part of me.

**虚构集**：你怎么能够拿这一切与小说做简单的类比？\
**Recoleta**: How could you treat them like fictional characters?

**虚构集**：这既不尊重我的文字，也不尊重关于生命的一切。\
**Recoleta**: It's disrespectful to my work and to life itself.

作者的抗拒如此尖锐，瞬间击碎了魔法师精心搭建的迷宫。\
The writer's resistance is so sharp that it cuts through Aleph's carefully constructed labyrinth easily.

**阿莱夫**：但这是你提出的问题。\
**Aleph**: But you raised the question yourself.

**阿莱夫**：为什么你如此抗拒得到答案？\
**Aleph**: Why do you resist receiving its answer?

他低下头，那张坚不可摧的面具上仿佛突然出现了裂痕。\
He lowers his head, and for the first time, cracks appear on that indestructible mask.

**狱医**：哈，他们总是这样。提出一个疑问，然后抛弃它，将它扔在时代的脑后。\
**The Physician**: Hah, they're always like this, aren't they? They throw a question at you only to abandon it along with the fading of the era.

**狱医**：阿莱夫，你早就知晓，这场“暴雨”不会放过任何人。\
**The Physician**: This "Storm" will spare no one. You've known it all along, Aleph.

**狱医**：只有环形的权力牢狱方可以掌控这一切，一座洞察一切的高塔，才是完美的规训方案。\
**The Physician**: Only the timeless Panopticon can maintain control. The all-seeing tower. The perfect governing system.

**理想家**：梅林，你当真是个无可救药的废物。你没有听过那位伟大诗人的箴言吗？世界本身就是一座巨大的迷宫了！我们为什么要再建一座？\
**The Idealist**: What a hopeless fool you are, Merlin. Haven't you heard what they say? "There is no need to build a labyrinth when the whole world already is one!"

**理想家**：真正有意义的只有文学。时代的浪潮会将这些被抛下的问题洗涮，最终它们又会回到脑海中的沙滩上来。这种事情我们已经经历过不少了！\
**The Idealist**: Your meaningless questions will be swept away by the tides of time, only to resurface on the shores of our minds once more. We've seen it happen over and over again! Surely you've realized by now that the only true meaning can be found in literature.

**理想家**：从一百年前到现在，文学才是唯一的解答，这位孤独的牛仔只是一时迷了路。\
**The Idealist**: For over a century, literature has remained the singular, ultimate answer. This lonely cowboy is simply feeling lost at the moment.

**狱医**：放屁，理想家！你是在浪费我们的时间！\
**The Physician**: Spare us your ramblings, Idealist! You're wasting our time.

**阿莱夫**：停下……\
**Aleph**: Enough.

映射内心的骰子不堪重负，呈现出灼热的裂痕。\
The die that reflects the heart can no longer bear its weight, as it glows from within burning fissures.

四周的镜面上，反射出无数道属于阿莱夫的身影，每一面都呈现出不同的容貌。他们像幽灵一样挤满这个狭窄的房间。\
On the surrounding mirrors, countless reflections of Aleph appear, each wearing a different face. They crowd into the room as a flood of ghosts.

**维尔汀**：阿莱夫先生，他的状态不太对劲……小心，那枚骰子似乎出问题了。\
**Vertin**: Aleph seems to be in a terrible state. We have to be careful. Something isn't right about that die!

混乱的战斗戛然而止。\
The chaotic battle comes to an abrupt halt.

**十四行诗**：等等，你是……人类？\
**Sonetto**: Wait, Mr. Aleph, are you human?

第一助手后退了一步。最终，本来指着前方的玻璃笔迟疑着移开了。\
Sonetto steps back, lowering her glasfeder.

她震惊地发现，对方并没有任何的神秘术能力，从头到尾，他所拥有的只有骰子。\
She is shocked to realize that her opponent has no arcane skills at all. From beginning to end, all he had was the die.

**十四行诗**：先生，请交出骰子，停下你危险的行为……！\
**Sonetto**: Please hand over the die peacefully!

**维尔汀**：阿莱夫先生，不要再挣扎了，这毫无意义。\
**Vertin**: Mr. Aleph, please stop resisting. It's futile.

**阿莱夫**：是的……这一切都毫无意义。\
**Aleph**: Futile. Yes, it's all futile.

**阿莱夫**：规则的铁笼和理想的文学，都是无用的，只是追寻超限道路上所产生的幻象。\
**Aleph**: The cage of rules, the ideals of literature ... Both are futile, mere illusions conjured along the path to transcendentality.

**阿莱夫**：他们都害怕自己只不过是另一个人梦中所产生的幻影，因而抗拒走入那片会吞噬一切的真实，却离超限越来越遥远。\
**Aleph**: They all fear that they're nothing more than phantoms in someone else's dream—that reality will devour everything, including their very existence. That's why they drift further and further away from transcendentality.

**阿莱夫**：最终，他们都没能挣脱那个虚假的梦。没有人能。\
**Aleph**: They couldn't break free from that false dream. None of them could.

操纵骰子的魔法师笨拙地看向故事创作者。\
Aleph stumbles as he looks up at the storyteller.

**阿莱夫**：狱医和理想家都不出所料地走向了毁灭。\
**Aleph**: Both the Physician and the Idealist walked toward their own destruction. Just as I expected.

**阿莱夫**：但……虚构集，你的小说，它还没有。它没有结局。\
**Aleph**: But your novel still has hope, Recoleta. Its ending hasn't been written yet.

**阿莱夫**：在得到结局之前，我们无法否认，它也许是一个迈向超限的答案。\
**Aleph**: We cannot deny that it may be the answer to achieving transcendentality.

**维尔汀**：……所以，阿莱夫先生，您是不会停下这一切的，对吗？\
**Vertin**: You're not going to stop, are you?

**维尔汀**：在得到一个答案之前。\
**Vertin**: Not until you get your "answer."

**维尔汀**：十四行诗，我们得先抢过那颗控制监狱的骰子——\
**Vertin**: Sonetto, we have no choice but to seize the die from him by force.

第一助手的神秘术凝聚在玻璃笔的笔尖。就在此时，一直沉默的青年作家向前走了一步。\
Sonetto's arcane energy gathers at the tip of her glasfeder. At this moment, the silent storyteller takes a step forward.

**虚构集**：够了。\
**Recoleta**: Enough.

**虚构集**：我说……够了！\
**Recoleta**: I said, enough!

她颤抖着，取出了从不离身的笔记本。\
She shakes as she reveals the notebook that has never left her side.

## 9TH-16 虚构的界限 / The Boundary of Fiction

1990年，瓜达拉哈拉，国际图书博览会会场。\
1990, Guadalajara, International Book Fair.

人们在书柜与走廊间来来往往，彼此热烈交谈，空气中充盈着多种语言的交汇。\
People move between bookshelves and corridors, engaged in heated conversations. The air is filled with the mingling of multiple languages.

**编辑**：很遗憾，虚构集小姐，我们无法刊登你的小说。希望你能拿出更成熟的作品！\
**Editor**: I'm afraid we can't publish your novel in its current state, Recoleta. We look forward to seeing more refined work from you in the future!

**编辑**：噢，克鲁斯先生，稍等一下！请问您是否有空赏脸和我们聊聊《青鸟》的版权问题？我们甜橙庄园出版社很喜欢您的儿童文学风格……\
**Editor**: Ah, Mr. Cruz! What a pleasure to see you here! I'm an editor from Naranja Dulce Publishing House. Could you spare a moment to discuss the copyright for The Bluebird? We're huge fans of your children's literature.

交谈的编辑追着另一位作家的身影远去了，留下了站在原地的虚构集。这是今天拒绝她的第十七家出版社。\
The editor leaves, hurrying after another writer, leaving Recoleta standing alone in place. The 17th publisher to reject her today.

**虚构集**：嘿……放轻松！这种被书本环绕的地方简直就是天堂，至少在这里，在今天，我不应该那么快感受到沮丧。\
**Recoleta**: Hey, relax, Recoleta! Look at all the books around you. This place is heaven! You can't get down on yourself, not here!

**虚构集**：没关系的，一次庄严隆重的拒绝可能是某种不祥的预兆，但十七次——它就什么都不是了。\
**Recoleta**: There are so many writers and publishers here. It's only natural you'd be turned down 17 times. This is just the beginning!

在一日之内遭受十七次拒绝的青年作家翻阅着手中的场地指引。\
The young writer, attempting to forget her 17th rejection, flips through the event guide in her hands.

**虚构集**：接下来我该去哪个展区呢？等等……这本手册里面应该有一些线索才是。\
**Recoleta**: Now, which section should I visit next? Hmm, oh, this brochure might help.

她将厚厚的手册翻到最后一页，上面赫然陈列着所有受邀参与本次大会的作者与联系方式。\
She turns to the last page of the thick handbook, where all the invited authors and their contact details are listed.

**虚构集**：好极了，一位作家和另一位作家的直接交流——没有什么比这更好的事情！\
**Recoleta**: Wonderful! An exchange of ideas between writers—nothing could be more incredible than that!

**虚构集**：在当年，乔伊斯也是受到了易卜生一封信的鼓励，才完成了伟大的《尤利西斯》。我该把我的手稿寄给——\
**Recoleta**: I recall James Joyce was inspired by a letter he received from Henrik Ibsen. So, maybe what I need is to find someone to share my manuscript with, but who?

**虚构集**：塔德奥，埃玛·宗兹，阿莱夫，阿威罗伊……\
**Recoleta**: Tadeo, Emma Zunz, Aleph, Averroes ...

敲门声打断了女孩在领奖台上发言的美梦。\
A knock at the door interrupts her daydream.

**虚构集**：……房东先生！\
**Recoleta**: Oh, it's you, sir!

**虚构集**：请放心，我保证下个月一定补齐房租！要我说，您这破烂公寓还真不值这价钱，墙上这些裂缝就像是从上个世纪遗留下来的……\
**Recoleta**: Don't worry. I promise I'll catch up on the rent next month! Although I must say, this apartment's hardly worth the price. The cracks on the walls must date back to the last century!

**房东**：哼，我一点儿也不急。反正你要是交不出房租，我就得请你搬到街角那座随时会坍塌的殖民公寓去住，或者去圣特尔莫市场的地摊上卖橘子。\
**Landlord**: Hmph, make all the excuses you want, ingrate. If you don't pay the rent soon, you'll either end up in that crumbling colonial building on the corner or on the street selling oranges at the San Telmo market!

**房东**：对了，听胡丽娅太太说，你又从纺织厂辞工了？\
**Landlord**: By the way, Julia told me you lost your job at that textile factory.

**房东**：你这小姑娘，活像是被咒语附身似的！难不成世上真有“在同一个地方工作超过三个月就会身亡”的咒语吗？\
**Landlord**: You under some kind like "can't work in one place for more than three months" curse or something, little girl?

**虚构集**：您不知道那间纺织厂里头发生了什么可怕的事情。我只不过是为受到压榨的工人们提供一些协助罢了。\
**Recoleta**: Oh, you don't even want to know about the terrible things that happened in that factory. All I did was lend the oppressed workers a hand.

**房东**：你和那些满嘴胡话的大学生一个模样——算了，我今天来不是为了说这个的。\
**Landlord**: Bah, you're just like those college kids—full of hot air. Anyway, I'm not here about the rent.

**房东**：前段时间，你刚从国外回来的时候，不是一直念叨着让我注意你的信件吗？\
**Landlord**: Didn't you tell me to watch out for your letters a while back, when you'd just returned from abroad?

**房东**：喏，你的信——\
**Landlord**: Well, here it is, a letter for you.

女孩愣住片刻后，她飞速地抢过信，一把摔上房门，颤抖着展开信件。\
The girl freezes for a moment, then snatches the letter and slams the door shut, almost buzzing with excitement as she unfolds it.

**虚构集**：哦，天啊，竟然真的会有人给我回信——我是说，谢谢您，房东先生！\
**Recoleta**: My goodness! Someone actually wrote back to me! This is incredible! Oh, oh, thank you so much for bringing it to me, sir!

她飞速地裁开了那封漂洋过海的信件。\
She slits open the long-traveling letter.

**虚构集**：“敬爱的虚构集小姐……”\
**Recoleta**: "Dear Ms. Recoleta ..."

**虚构集**：让我看看……回信的作家，是一位名叫阿莱夫的先生！\
**Recoleta**: It's from—let's see—Aleph!

**同行青年Ⅰ**：嘿，我留意你很久了。你不是本地人吧？你一直在这儿写什么？\
**Young Woman**: Eh, I've been watching you. You're not a local, are you? What are you writing?

**虚构集**：噢，你好！事实上，我三天前才到布宜诺斯艾利斯——中间的故事长得像一段探戈，曲折但没什么值得一说的。\
**Recoleta**: Oh, hello! You're right. I just arrived in Buenos Aires three days ago. My trip's been a lot like a Copes tango performance—full of twists and turns, but nothing much worth telling, really.

**虚构集**：至于现在，我正在给我的笔友写回信！说来有些话长，但我给他寄去了小说的复件，没想到他竟然真的回信了……\
**Recoleta**: I'm actually writing a reply to my pen pal! Long story short, I sent him a manuscript of my novel, and to my surprise, he actually wrote back.

**虚构集**：总之，这听起来很奇妙对吧！\
**Recoleta**: Amazing, isn't it?

**虚构集**：最新的来信中，我们正讨论到这部小说缺少了一个更为重要的角色，因此它无法得到一个决定性的结局。\
**Recoleta**: In our recent letters, we've been discussing how my novel lacks a key character to drive the story toward a decisive ending.

**虚构集**：于是，我们正在商量是否需要引入一个新的幽灵，作为故事的转折。\
**Recoleta**: So we've been debating whether to introduce a new ghost to act as a turning point for the story.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：这么说来，你是个作家？嘿，潘乔，过来看看！我遇到一位真正的作家！\
**Young Woman**: Oh, so then you're a writer? Hey, Pancho, come over here! I've found an actual real-life writer!

**同行青年Ⅱ**：这有什么可大惊小怪的，作家有什么稀奇的？我初中的时候写过不少诗呢！\
**Young Man**: What's the big deal? I wrote plenty of poems in middle school.

**虚构集**：噢，这么说来，你也是一位诗人了！\
**Recoleta**: Oh, so you're a poet!

**虚构集**：我有预感，我们会共同开启一场不可思议的冒险故事！你们有兴趣参加本能现实主义派的运动吗？\
**Recoleta**: I have a feeling we're about to embark on an incredible adventure together! Are you interested in joining the visceral realism movement?

**同行青年Ⅰ**：我从来没听说过这本能……什么的派系。但这好像很有意思！\
**Young Woman**: Vis what? I've never heard of it. But it sounds like fun.

**虚构集**：太好了！事不宜迟，等我写完这封回信，两位就与我一起前往乌斯怀亚吧！\
**Recoleta**: Fabulous! We have no time to waste. Once I finish this letter, you two must join me on a journey to Ushuaia!

**同行青年Ⅱ**：乌斯怀亚？那不是世界尽头吗？咱们跑到那个冻得要命的鬼地方干什么？\
**Young Man**: Ushuaia? The end of the world? Why the heck would we go to that icebox?

**同行青年Ⅰ**：潘乔，别扫兴！你什么时候变成这么没趣的人了？试想一下，我们会看到怎样壮丽的景色，聆听多少荒芜中的故事！\
**Young Woman**: Oh, don't be such a downer, Pancho. Just think of the fun we'll have, the breathtaking scenery we'll see, and the incredible stories we'll hear.

**同行青年Ⅱ**：……好吧，玛利亚，只要你想去，这些都不是问题。\
**Young Man**: Fine, María. I'll deal with the cold if you really wanna go so badly.

**同行青年Ⅰ**：话说回来，能不能讲讲你写的小说？\
**Young Woman**: By the way, could you tell us about your novel?

**虚构集**：当然，路上我会慢慢讲给你们听的！让我想想该从哪儿开头呢？\
**Recoleta**: Of course. I'll tell you all about it on the way. Hmm, now where to begin?

**虚构集**：就从阿马尔菲塔诺里，那座蓝色屋顶的茅屋开始吧……\
**Recoleta**: Alright, let's start with the cottage with the blue roof in Amalfitano.

**虚构集**：从我们的第一次来信开始，已经过去了六个月。\
**Recoleta**: It's been six months since we first exchanged letters.

**虚构集**：在这六个月里，从智利流浪到墨西哥，又从墨西哥流浪到阿根廷的一路上，我从不曾停止写作。\
**Recoleta**: Since then, I've been traveling. First from Chile to Mexico, then from Mexico to Argentina. And I've never stopped writing.

**虚构集**：我不知道我的小说，它究竟是什么，我只是在写，一直不停地在写。\
**Recoleta**: I'm not really sure what the purpose of my novel is. I just keep writing and writing. I can't stop.

**虚构集**：文学应当拥有怎样的力量？又该承载什么？或许只有持续不断地写下去，我才会明白……\
**Recoleta**: What power does literature hold? What responsibilities? Perhaps only by continuing to write will I understand one day.

虚构集翻开她的笔记本，几乎每两张纸页间都夹着另一种颜色的信纸。\
Recoleta flips through her notebook, every turn of the page containing a different-colored letter.

经过漫长的旅行后，这一页页信纸就像褪色的谜团，上面的字迹早已模糊不清。\
After their long journey, these pages of letters form a faded riddle, their handwriting long since blurred.

**虚构集**：阿莱夫，你说得对，我确实是很想要一个故事的结局。\
**Recoleta**: Aleph, you're right. I do want an ending to my novel.

**虚构集**：但不应该是以这种方式……\
**Recoleta**: But not like this.

**阿莱夫**：虚构集，你真的不知道吗……？\
**Aleph**: You really have no idea, do you, Recoleta?

唯一的读者意识到了接下来会发生的事，这迫使他说出了一直隐瞒的真相。\
Her only reader realizes she has still not grasped what is happening, forcing him to reveal a truth he has long concealed.

**阿莱夫**：《理性家族的崛起与衰落》是关于你的故事。\
**Aleph**: The Rise and Fall of Sanity is your story.

**虚构集**：……什么？\
**Recoleta**: What do you mean?

**阿莱夫**：你是一个幽灵，一个游荡在这片被遗弃的土地上，却还在试图书写神话的幽灵。\
**Aleph**: You are a ghost, wandering this forsaken land, still striving to create a miracle.

**阿莱夫**：你诞生于阿马尔菲塔诺，是整个故事最核心的人物：作者自身写照的角色，一名流浪诗人。\
**Aleph**: You are a wandering poet born in Amalfitano, the foolishly brave protagonist of the story, and the embodiment of the author herself.

**阿莱夫**：你是那位作家，却也并非那位作家，是她幻想中的自我，一个隐秘的、关于流浪梦想的化身，一个故事中勇敢而荒唐的主角。\
**Aleph**: A reflection, yes. The author, no. You are simply a figment of her imagination, a manifestation of her dream to wander.

**阿莱夫**：你没有发现吗？你的文学追求，那些愚蠢而高尚的冒险，它们并不属于这个年代，只是一道来自1975年的旧时代泡影……\
**Aleph**: Have you not realized it? The literary pursuits and romantic adventures you described ... they are merely faded memories from 1975.

**阿莱夫**：与“你”一同参加本能现实主义运动的诗人们，他们也早已离开了拉丁美洲。\
**Aleph**: The poets who joined the visceral realism movement with "you" left Latin America long ago.

**虚构集**：旧时代的……泡影？\
**Recoleta**: Faded memories?

**阿莱夫**：这是你的小说，不仅是你所创作的小说，还是关于你自身的小说……\
**Aleph**: As for the novel, it's yours now—a story you're writing, a story about yourself.

**阿莱夫**：你的离去，使得阿马尔菲塔诺成为一座鬼城，所有的角色都失去与你的联系，相继化作模糊的存在。\
**Aleph**: Your departure has turned Amalfitano into a ghost town. The characters have lost their connection to you. They're gradually fading away.

**阿莱夫**：……如果你摧毁这部小说，你也会随着故事而消失。\
**Aleph**: If the novel is destroyed, you too will cease to exist.

**维尔汀**：等等……虚构集，他说的是真的吗？\
**Vertin**: Wait, this is ... Ms. Recoleta, is what he said true?

**虚构集**：……\
**Recoleta**: ...

**虚构集**：我知道你从不说谎，我的笔友。\
**Recoleta**: I ... I know you never lie, pen pal.

**虚构集**：在第一次回信中，你告诉我，需要在最初就决定好角色所被赋予的身份与命运，并让其一直在故事中遵循下去……\
**Recoleta**: In your first letter, you told me that a character's role and fate must be determined from the outset and consistently adhered to throughout the story.

**虚构集**：这太新奇了，一个来自旁观者的视角，一个博学的读者，一个无问不答的先知。\
**Recoleta**: Reading the perspective and insights of a walking encyclopedia—having such a person be willing to share their thoughts at all—was an exhilarating experience.

**虚构集**：我从来没有想过故事还能这样发展。欣喜若狂都不足以形容我那一刻的心情。\
**Recoleta**: I had never imagined my novel could develop in this way. Words could hardly describe how I felt in that moment.

**虚构集**：我一直知道的，从来没有人能看懂这个小镇中发生的事情，从来没有。\
**Recoleta**: No one but you has ever understood the story of that town, let alone offered any revisions.

**虚构集**：第二次、第三次，乃至往后的每一次来信，我按照你的建议，在故事中加入了银行职员、沙漠捕鱼人、盲眼的织工、死于谋杀的赶驴人……\
**Recoleta**: Following your advice, I added the Bank Clerk, the Dune Piscator, the Blind Weaver, and the Murdered Donkey Driver.

**虚构集**：阿马尔菲塔诺小镇不再仅有那座蓝色屋顶的茅屋，新到来的幽灵挤满了沙漠上空。\
**Recoleta**: Amalfitano was no longer an empty town with a single blue-roofed cottage. The new ghostly residents had begun to fill the skies over it.

**虚构集**：理性家族的历史与故事也越来越完整，我能够感觉到，它的结局近在咫尺。\
**Recoleta**: The story was finally reaching completion. I could feel that the ending was within reach.

**虚构集**：我越来越迫切地想要见到这位唯一的笔友。这个异乎寻常的想法占据了我的脑海。\
**Recoleta**: I became increasingly eager to meet my pen pal. I couldn't get the thought out of my mind.

**虚构集**：我不知道我要与“阿莱夫”说什么。一句来自作者的、轻飘飘的感谢？还是说，我要与这个唯一的读者商讨阿马尔菲塔诺的未来？\
**Recoleta**: I wasn't sure what I would say to this Aleph. A simple "thank you," perhaps? Or maybe a discussion about the future of Amalfitano with its sole reader?

**虚构集**：或者我也只是受困于这个念头的、受到命运摆布的人罢了……\
**Recoleta**: Or maybe I'm no different from everyone else—led up the garden path by "fate."

**阿莱夫**：……\
**Aleph**: ...

**虚构集**：无论你所说的这一切，是真实亦或虚假——我是一个幽灵，一个隐秘的化身，一个虚构出来的存在。\
**Recoleta**: But even if I am a ghost, as you say, an incarnation of someone else, a fictional being—

**虚构集**：但……这又何妨？\
**Recoleta**: So what?

**虚构集**：无论我自身是否会随之消亡……我的决心都不会改变。\
**Recoleta**: My resolve will not waver, even if my existence is bound to fade away.

**虚构集**：因为文学不应该是这样的。\
**Recoleta**: Because this isn't what literature is supposed to be.

**虚构集**：你曾告诉我，故事里没有纯粹的现实，只有一个个深渊，一层层谎言堆叠的地基……\
**Recoleta**: You once told me there isn't an ounce of reality in fiction—only voids and glorified lies.

**虚构集**：我将回答你，在现实与虚构那闪烁不定的边界里，我早已接受了自身存在的事实。\
**Recoleta**: Let me tell you this: whether real or fictional, corporeal or intangible, I have accepted my existence.

**虚构集**：阿莱夫，停下这一切吧。\
**Recoleta**: Now, let's put a stop to this, Aleph.

**虚构集**：他们……那些监狱中的朋友们，他们并不是我笔下的角色。你不仅把他们困于这座环形的废墟之中，也困住了你自己。\
**Recoleta**: The inmates aren't characters in my novel. They're people trapped in a prison, just as you are.

**虚构集**：你赋予了我操纵他人命运的力量，让我成为了一名愧疚的神明，一个虚假的、让人顶礼膜拜的造物主……\
**Recoleta**: By simulating my story here, you have made me into some kind of god, a guilty false creator, a dictator of fate.

**虚构集**：但我根本不想要这样……！\
**Recoleta**: I never wanted any of this!

那些破碎的文字和幽灵的幻影呼啸而出，从故事的结构、从字里行间解脱，充满悔恨与痴醉。\
Shattered words and ghostly illusions roar forth, breaking free from the story's structure and the gaps between its lines, filled with regret and obsession.

被撕碎的信纸与书页，纷纷扬扬地在房间内飘落，像是一个美丽的冬夜水晶球。\
Torn letters and book pages flutter in the air, like snow in a crystal globe on a winter night.

一切都归于宁静。\
Everything is quiet.

**十四行诗**：虚构集小姐，她消失了……\
**Sonetto**: Ms. Recoleta has vanished.

**十四行诗**：难道，阿莱夫说的都是真的吗？\
**Sonetto**: Did she really "cease to exist" like Aleph said?

**维尔汀**：虚构集……\
**Vertin**: Recoleta ...

## 9TH-17 往昔的幽灵 / Ghosts of the Past

无人知晓的夜晚，风带来了属于沙漠的冰冷与荒凉。\
On an unknown night, the wind carries the cold desolation of the desert.

在那座蓝色屋顶的茅屋里，一个女孩梦见了一座环形的监狱。\
In the cottage with a blue roof, a girl dreams of a circular prison.

然后，她醒了过来。\
Then, she wakes.

**虚构集**：En una noche misteriosa, el viento trajo la fría dureza del desierto. En la cabaña de techo azul, le llegó en un sueño: una cárcel sin esquinas Y entonces, despertó.\
 ……真是一场混乱又荒唐的梦。\
**Recoleta**: En una noche misteriosa, el viento trajo la fría dureza del desierto. En la cabaña de techo azul, le llegó en un sueño: una cárcel sin esquinas Y entonces, despertó.\
 What a bizarre dream.

**虚构集**：那现实的味道，尝起来如此的沉重和悲伤……\
**Recoleta**: The taste of reality—so bitter and sad.

**虚构集**：但是它又充满了精确的辩证，哈哈——那是我内心的投影吗？\
**Recoleta**: But full of dialectical thinking, haha. Maybe the people of the Panopticon were reflecting my inner thoughts?

她环视四周，打量着结了蜘蛛网的角落、堆上天花板的稿纸和落满灰尘的墨水瓶。\
She looks around, surveying the cobwebbed corners where stacks of manuscripts have piled up to the ceiling and over empty ink bottles collecting dust.

**虚构集**：看来我真的是小说中的人物！\
**Recoleta**: Ah, so I really am a character in the novel!

**虚构集**：噢！这栋最为神秘的蓝色屋顶茅屋，原来是我的住所。那些幽灵们所说的可怖传闻，果然只是以讹传讹。\
**Recoleta**: The mysterious cottage with the blue roof was my home all along. Then, the rumors the ghosts spread were indeed just that—rumors.

归来的青年作家走出了自己的家，来到了熟悉又陌生的沙漠小镇街道。\
The young writer steps out of her home and into the streets of the familiar yet foreign desert town.

无数没有名字的角色与幽灵都闻讯赶来，挤满了道路与上空。\
Countless nameless characters and ghosts arrive upon hearing the news, filling the roads and skies.

**银行职员**：我亲爱的作家朋友，你终于回到阿马尔菲塔诺了！\
**The Bank Clerk**: Welcome back to Amalfitano, dear writer!

**虚构集**：谢谢你的欢迎，亲爱的资本主义象征。但我记得我明明摧毁了这本小说……\
**Recoleta**: Thank you, dear icon of capitalism. But, didn't I tear this novel to pieces?

一名风尘仆仆、戴着帽子的女士走上前。\
A woman wearing a peculiar hat steps forward.

**能量扰动学家**：因为阿马尔菲塔诺，是生与死的边界，是超脱一切存在的存在。\
**The Paracausality Researcher**: You see, Amalfitano is a dimension beyond life and death.

**能量扰动学家**：因为这里，是你内心的投影，它并不真实，自然也无从消亡。\
**The Paracausality Researcher**: This town is a reflection of your inner thoughts. It's incorporeal. You can't tear something incorporeal into pieces.

**能量扰动学家**：因为文字是一条能跨越生与死的河流，它不受到时间所管辖。\
**The Paracausality Researcher**: Literature is endless and timeless, like a river flowing across life and death.

**虚构集**：您不愧是我最喜爱的角色，总是能让我领悟到生活另一面的答案。\
**Recoleta**: No wonder you're my favorite character. You never cease to enlighten me.

**门槛旁的乞丐**：但很可惜，文学它只是无用的举动。没有人能看懂，也没有人会记得你的文字！\
**The Door-Side Beggar**: Unfortunately, literature is a dangerous and futile calling. Nobody truly understands or even remembers your work!

**门槛旁的乞丐**：还记得那句俗语吗？当我们从所有人的记忆中消失时，就是我们真正的死亡。\
**The Door-Side Beggar**: Do you remember the saying? "The only truly dead are those who have been forgotten."

**门槛旁的乞丐**：哈哈，虚构集，你只能留在这个生与死的边界！一旦离开了阿马尔菲塔诺，你还是会迎来消亡的命运！\
**The Door-Side Beggar**: Hahaha, Recoleta, you'll disappear for good if you leave Amalfitano again. It'll be like you never existed!

**虚构集**：乞丐先生，作为一个彻底的批判型角色，我一直非常欣赏您的批判性思维。\
**Recoleta**: I've always admired your critical thinking, sir. It fits your role perfectly.

一双粗糙的手握住了青年作家的手，来者摸索着她掌心的纹路。\
Rough hands grasp the writer's palm, feeling at the lines etched into her skin.

**盲眼的织工**：没关系的，虚构集。没关系的。\
**The Blind Weaver**: Everything will be alright, Recoleta.

**盲眼的织工**：无论之前发生了什么事情，你回到了这里，这是最重要的。\
**The Blind Weaver**: Whatever happened, you've returned now. That's what matters.

**盲眼的织工**：巴比伦之骰得以恢复正常，得以再次转动，我们所有人都会迎来属于自己的结局。\
**The Blind Weaver**: The Die of Babylon will roll again, and each of us will get our endings.

在场的人都欢呼起来。\
The crowd erupts in cheers.

**赶驴人的幽灵**：快侦破那起发生在酒馆的谋杀案，让我的灵魂得以安息在这片大地！\
**The Murdered Donkey Driver**: That's right. Solve the murder at the bar and put my soul at rest!

**沙漠捕鱼人**：快摧毁一直困囿着这座村庄的疯狂，让它不再受到古远幽灵的侵扰！\
**The Dune Piscator**: Free the village from the madness inflicted by the ancient spirit!

**能量扰动学家**：快修正巴比伦之骰的随机性，让风中飘荡的频率不再为所有人带来噩运！\
**The Paracausality Researcher**: Fix the randomness of the Die of Babylon and flatten the calamitous frequency!

**所有人**：快掷下最后一次骰子吧，虚构集！\
**Amalfitano Residents**: Roll the Die one last time, Recoleta!

青年作家往前走了一步，所有人与幽灵都饱含期待地望着她。\
The young writer takes a step forward. Everyone, the living and the ghosts, watches expectantly.

**虚构集**：原来我一直在追求的，是那个“我”所未能给我的结局吗？\
**Recoleta**: So the ending I've been searching for is the one the other "me" was unable to give me?

**虚构集**：那个不顾一切、投身于抗争的“我”，那个忙于做怪人和献祭者的“我”，那个终究离开了这片大陆的“我”……\
**Recoleta**: The "me" that plunged headfirst into the struggle against an undefeatable power. The "me" who ultimately left this land ...

**虚构集**：我终于找到了……我的结局……\
**Recoleta**: After all this time, I've finally found my ending.

她握住了那颗闪闪发亮的巴比伦之骰。\
She grasps the gleaming Die of Babylon.

**虚构集**：而现在，只需最后一下骰子的转动，一切都会结束……\
**Recoleta**: Just one more roll, and it will all be over.

**虚构集**：我的故事，小镇中的一切，都会迎来真正的、我一直在追求的结尾……终于……\
**Recoleta**: My story, my town ... Everything will finally come to an end.

**虚构集**：但那场环形监狱的梦境，也会同时结束，对吗……？\
**Recoleta**: But the dream about the Panopticon ... It'll end as well, won't it?

她停下了动作。\
She stops.

**银行职员**：亲爱的，那只是一场梦而已。\
**The Bank Clerk**: Oh, sweetheart, it's just a dream.

**门槛旁的乞丐**：你要为了一场虚无的梦，抛弃你穷尽一生的追求吗？\
**The Door-Side Beggar**: Ha, don't tell me you're abandoning your lifelong pursuit for a measly dream!

**赶驴人的幽灵**：在那场残酷的梦中，没有人能够理解这部伟大的小说，理解发生在小镇中的一切。\
**The Murdered Donkey Driver**: That dream is cruel. No one understands this great novel there or this amazing town.

**盲眼的织工**：但在这里，你是一位真正的作家。这里才是你的故乡，虚构集。\
**The Blind Weaver**: But here, you are a true writer. This is your home, Recoleta.

**虚构集**：但我想念我的朋友们了……那场梦境同这里一样，也仍然没有结束。\
**Recoleta**: But I already miss my friends in that dream. It exists, just like this place does.

**沙漠捕鱼人**：虚构集，我们也是你的朋友！\
**The Dune Piscator**: But we're your friends too, Recoleta!

**能量扰动学家**：……哪怕离开了阿马尔菲塔诺，你有可能永远地消散，你也要这么做吗？\
**The Paracausality Researcher**: You might disappear forever if you leave Amalfitano. Are you sure you want to leave?

青年作家放下了手中的骰子。\
The young writer puts down the die in her hand.

那颗代表着一切终点的骰子，再次消失在了夹着沙的风中。\
The die that signifies the end of everything vanishes into the sandy wind.

**虚构集**：朋友们，你们都知道的，我这一生，都在进行着一些愚蠢而不求回报的冒险……\
**Recoleta**: You know what I'm like, my dear friends. I've spent my life embarking on foolish, unrewarded adventures.

**虚构集**：毕竟这就是我，不是吗？\
**Recoleta**: That's just who I am, isn't it?

**虚构集**：阿马尔菲塔诺确实是一个理想的地方。一个适合流浪，也适合短暂停留，更适合迷失的地方。\
**Recoleta**: Amalfitano is indeed an ideal place—a place for wandering, for a short trip, and for losing oneself for a while.

**虚构集**：我亲爱的虚构朋友们，我永远喜爱你们……\
**Recoleta**: And it has you, my fictional friends, who I love so dearly.

**虚构集**：但我仍然需要回去我的梦境中看看，那些监狱中的朋友们，他们也同样重要……\
**Recoleta**: But I must return to my dream and see my friends there. They're just as important to me.

闻言，小镇的幽灵们都露出了释怀的笑容。\
As they hear her words, the ghosts of the town smile with relief.
